// Gabriele\nSteinhauser And Matthew Dalton \xe2\x80\x93 July 7,\n2015..........................................................................................................\n263\n\n\n\n\n\n*TODAY\xe2\x80\x99S KEY STORIES*\n\n\n\n*Hillary Clinton Courts Bigger Crowds in Return to Iowa\n<http://www.nytimes.com/politics/first-draft/2015/07/07/clinton-returns-to-iowa-as-she-courts-bigger-crowds/>\n// NYT // Amy Chozick \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nHillary Rodham Clinton returned to one of the most liberal pockets of the\nstate that shunned her in 2008, to speak at a public library packed with\nIowans who ranged from those curious to see the former first lady to those\ncommitted to caucusing for her in next February\xe2\x80\x99s contest.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI want people\xe2\x80\x99s lives to be better when I finish as your president than\nwhen I started,\xe2\x80\x9d Mrs. Clinton told a crowd of roughly 350 people in remarks\nthat ranged from foreign policy and economic issues to the drug epidemic\nand mental health.\n\n\n\nThe event marked the start of another phase in Mrs. Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s 2016 campaign\nin which she intends to speak to larger crowds and take more questions from\nvoters in the early nominating states of Iowa and New Hampshire.\n\n\n\nOn Tuesday, Mrs. Clinton also sat down for an interview with CNN, her first\nwith a national television outlet since she announced her candidacy\nofficial in April.\n\n\n\nThis liberal college town, home to the University of Iowa, that\noverwhelmingly favored Barack Obama and John Edwards in 2008 (she came in\nthird statewide) could serve as a test of whether Mrs. Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s message\nresonates with the Democratic Party\xe2\x80\x99s base. Senator Bernie Sanders, a\nsocialist who is also seeking the party\xe2\x80\x99s nomination, drew a crowd of 300\npeople at an event here in May.\n\n\n\nIn her speech, an animated Mrs. Clinton seemed to try to hit all the\nliberal notes, including combating climate change, giving women access to\nreproductive health care and celebrating the Supreme Court\xe2\x80\x99s recent\ndecisions to legalize same sex marriage nationwide and uphold a key\nprovision of Mr. Obama\xe2\x80\x99s health care overhaul.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cIf a Republican is elected president, that will be the end of the\nAffordable Care Act,\xe2\x80\x9d Mrs. Clinton said.\n\n\n\nHer calls to make college more affordable played well in the almost\nall-white and largely female crowd. \xe2\x80\x9cHow many of you had loans to go to\nhigher education? I did, I did, so did Bill,\xe2\x80\x9d Mrs. Clinton said. \xe2\x80\x9cI had\nlike two jobs. He had like five. We were just working around the clock.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nDespite pleas from liberal groups, Mrs. Clinton has not gone as far as Mr.\nSanders, who said he would eliminate tuition at public colleges to reduce\nstudent debt.\n\n\n\nMrs. Clinton pushed for greater gun control measures, which contrasts her\nto Mr. Sanders, who has been one of the Democratic Party\xe2\x80\x99s most ardent\ndefenders of Second Amendment rights. \xe2\x80\x9cLet\xe2\x80\x99s not be afraid of the gun\nlobby, which does not even really represent the majority of gun owners,\xe2\x80\x9d\nshe said.\n\n\n\nAfter the event, Mrs. Clinton took questions from reporters. She called the\ncollapse of the Greek economy a \xe2\x80\x9ctragedy\xe2\x80\x9d and called on European leaders to\nreach an agreement. And she declined to comment on a controversial\nprovision of a nuclear agreement with Iran that would require the nation to\ndisclose its previous nuclear experimentation, an issue that has divided\nthe Obama Administration.\n\n\n\nWhen asked about Mr. Sanders\xe2\x80\x99s surge in the polls, Mrs. Clinton said she\nalways expected the race to be competitive. \xe2\x80\x9cIt should be competitive. It\xe2\x80\x99s\nonly the presidency of the United States we\xe2\x80\x99re talking about, so the more\nthe better,\xe2\x80\x9d she said.\n\n\n\nAfter Iowa City, Mrs. Clinton headed to Ottumwa, Iowa, where she would talk\nto Iowans at a grassroots-organizing event. The campaign said it has\nalready directly reached 16,000 Iowans and recruited at least one committed\ncaucusgoer in each of the state\xe2\x80\x99s 1,682 precincts.\n\n\n\nBut Mrs. Clinton still has much to do in this state where voters expect to\npersonally meet their candidates before participating in the famous\ncaucuses, which take place Feb 1, 2016. Her lead over Mr. Sanders has\nnarrowed in a recent poll \xe2\x80\x94 she still leads by double digits \xe2\x80\x94 and Iowans\nare clearly checking their options.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI think I\xe2\x80\x99m here out of curiosity more than anything else at this point,\xe2\x80\x9d\nsaid Ashley Heffernen, 22, a recent graduate who waited in line with her\nboyfriend to hear Mrs. Clinton and hopefully ask a question about\nimmigration. \xe2\x80\x9cI want t see all the candidates,\xe2\x80\x9d Ms. Heffernen said.\n\n\n\nColleen Russo also waited in line outside the library. She supported Mr.\nObama in 2008, but said she wanted to show her five-year-old granddaughter\nViviana, who wore a pink dress and purple tiara, that a woman could be\npresident. \xe2\x80\x9cShe couldn\xe2\x80\x99t be more experienced,\xe2\x80\x9d Ms. Russo said of Mrs.\nClinton.\n\n\n\nJorge Guerra, 26, who stood next to the Ms. Russo and her grandchild,\ninterjected: \xe2\x80\x9cWell, I\xe2\x80\x99m glad you didn\xe2\x80\x99t bring her to see Michele Bachmann.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nMr. Guerra said part of what is holding him back from being all-in for Mrs.\nClinton was her relationship to Wall Street and corporations. \xe2\x80\x9cIt unnerves\nme,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cI want her to be as honest about and be as open as possible\nabout a lot of these questions.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nMs. Russo agreed and said there were still things about Mrs. Clinton that\ngave her pause, but said Mrs. Clinton was most likely to win a general\nelection. \xe2\x80\x9cI think she needs to be more exposed and talk to bigger groups,\nlike Bernie does,\xe2\x80\x9d she said, referring to Mr. Sanders. Mr. Guerra nodded.\n\xe2\x80\x9cShe can\xe2\x80\x99t hide. Not someone like her.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nMrs. Clinton seemed acutely aware of how tough things may be for her in\nIowa. After her remarks, she took questions from the audience. Dozens of\nhands went up.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m gonna let you pick,\xe2\x80\x9d she told the crowd. \xe2\x80\x9cBecause I don\xe2\x80\x99t want to lose\nany potential caucusgoers.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n*Clinton steps up attacks on GOP presidential candidates in Iowa \xe2\x80\x94 but\nsteers clear of knocking her Democratic rivals\n<http://www.washingtonpost.com/blogs/post-politics/wp/2015/07/07/clinton-steps-up-attacks-on-gop-presidential-candidates-in-iowa-but-steers-clear-of-knocking-her-democratic-rivals/>\n// WaPo // Jose Del Real \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nHillary Rodham Clinton escalated her criticism of her GOP presidential\nrivals during a campaign stop here in Iowa City on Tuesday, knocking the\nfield of candidates on immigration reform, health care and LGBT issues\nwhile steering clear of directly attacking her Democratic primary rivals.\n\n\n\n"How many people running on the Republican side try to demean immigrants,\ninsult immigrants, cast aspersions on immigrants? They know as well as we\nknow, we are not going to deport 11 or 12 million people living here,\xe2\x80\x9d she\ntold a crowd of about 250 attendees in a packed room at the Iowa City\nPublic Library. "I hear the Republican candidates \xe2\x80\x94 and it\'s not even the\nmost vitriolic \xe2\x80\x94 none of them any longer support a path to citizenship. All\nof them would basically consign immigrants to second-class status."\n\n\n\nClinton echoed those sentiments in an interview with CNN after the campaign\nevent, in which she said the Republican field is on "a spectrum of\nhostility." During that interview she denounced controversial comments by\nGOP presidential candidate and real estate mogul Donald Trump about Mexican\nimmigrants. She specifically criticized former Florida governor Jeb Bush\nfor not supporting an immigration reform plan that would give immigrants a\npath to citizenship, a position he once said he favored.\n\n\n\nThe former secretary of state paired those comments with warnings that a\nRepublican president in 2016 would roll back the Affordable Care Act and\nwould continue fighting for same-sex marriage bans, which the Supreme Court\nrecently ruled were unconstitutional. She told supporters at the event that\nthose issues highlight why she believes the country needs a Democrat in the\nWhite House after President Obama leaves office.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe Republicans want to turn the clock back. They are going to look for\nevery way they can,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cInstead of saying marriage equality is the\nlaw of the land and now let\xe2\x80\x99s move on to the next part of the agenda, which\nis ending discrimination against LGBT folks, they are going to try to fight\na rearguard action.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nBut even while she spoke critically and aggressively about the GOP\npresidential hopefuls, the presumed Democratic frontrunner avoided making\nswipes at her primary challengers \xe2\x80\x94 mostly pointedly, Sen. Bernie Sanders\n(I-Vt.), who has received outsize attention from the left flank of the\nparty and is drawing crowds at campaign events that reach into the\nthousands.\n\n\n\n"This is going to be competitive. It should be competitive \xe2\x80\x94 it\'s only the\npresidency of the United States we\'re talking about," she joked during a\nquestion-and-answer session with reporters after the campaign event. She\ndid not, however, directly answer the question: what she thought about\nSanders\'s recent surge on the left.\n\n\n\nMeanwhile, the campaign\'s months-long ramp-up in the four early voting\nstates hit a new peak Tuesday when 20 additional field organizers joined\nthe Clinton campaign\'s Iowa operation, where the campaign has already\ninvested a large amount of resources in hopes of capturing a decisive win\nin the first-in-the-nation caucuses. That addition, as the Des Moines\nRegister first reported and the Washington Post confirmed, means her team\nnow includes an imposing 47 paid organizers \xe2\x80\x94 in Iowa alone.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThis continues from our assumption that this is a competitive caucus that\nneeds a significant organization to earn every vote,\xe2\x80\x9d said Clinton\nspokesperson Jesse Ferguson. \xe2\x80\x9c[W]e\xe2\x80\x99ll have to work for every vote.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n*Hillary Clinton: On immigration, the GOP is just like Donald Trump\n<http://www.politico.com/story/2015/07/hillary-clinton-last-rodeo-campaign-stop-iowa-2016-119810.html#ixzz3fIDR7BDz>\n// Politico // Gabriel Debenedetti \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015*\n\n\n\nIOWA CITY, Iowa \xe2\x80\x94 Hillary Clinton believes Donald Trump should be thrown in\nthe doghouse for his comments on immigration. And that the rest of the\nRepublican party should be tossed in there with him.\n\n\n\nIn her first national TV interview since she launched her campaign, the\nDemocratic front-runner seized on the real estate mogul\xe2\x80\x99s controversial\ncomments on immigration (calling many Mexican immigrants \xe2\x80\x9crapists\xe2\x80\x9d and\n\xe2\x80\x9ccriminals\xe2\x80\x9d) to shame the rest of the Republican presidential field.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m very disappointed in those comments and I feel very bad and very\ndisappointed with him and with the Republican Party for not responding\nimmediately and saying, enough, stop it,\xe2\x80\x9d Clinton said to CNN after\nheadlining an organizing meeting in a local public library.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut they are all in the \xe2\x80\x94 you know, in the same general area on\nimmigration. They don\xe2\x80\x99t want to provide a path to citizenship. They range\nacross a spectrum of being either grudgingly welcome or hostile toward\nimmigrants.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nClinton has already publicly bashed Trump for his comments, through not by\nname, after having previously accepted campaign contributions from him and\neven attending one of his weddings.\n\n\n\nBut on Tuesday, she played into fears the Republican establishment has\nabout Trump dragging down the rest of the party with his inflammatory\ncomments.\n\n\n\nShe also took aim at former Florida Gov. Jeb Bush, who has been more\nsupportive of immigration reform than his rivals.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cHe doesn\xe2\x80\x99t believe in a path to citizenship. If he did at one time, he no\nlonger does,\xe2\x80\x9d Clinton said. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd so pretty much they\xe2\x80\x99re \xe2\x80\x94 as I said,\nthey\xe2\x80\x99re on a spectrum of, you know, hostility, which I think is really\nregrettable in a nation of immigrants like ours.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nClinton touched on the email controversy that has bogged down the early\ndays of her campaign, as well, saying she did not violate any rules by\nusing a private email server while serving as secretary of state.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cLet\xe2\x80\x99s take a deep breath here. Everything I did was permitted by law and\nregulation,\xe2\x80\x9d she said.\n\n\n\nAnd, she added, there\xe2\x80\x99s an upshot \xe2\x80\x94 the public now gets a glimpse into her\ndaily life, from telling aide John Podesta to wear socks, to her struggles\nwith operating a fax machine.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cNow I think it\xe2\x80\x99s kind of fun. People get a real-time behind-the-scenes\nlook at what I was emailing about and what I was communicating about,\xe2\x80\x9d she\nsaid.\n\n\n\nThe interview, with Brianna Keilar, touched on a broad range of topics \xe2\x80\x94\nfrom Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s doppelganger on \xe2\x80\x9cSaturday Night Live\xe2\x80\x9d to her plans for an\neconomic policy speech in Kansas City on Monday to Democratic rival and\nsurging candidate Bernie Sanders (\xe2\x80\x9cI always thought this would be a\ncompetitive race.\xe2\x80\x9d)\n\n\n\nClinton also answered a question about the brouhaha around a woman possibly\nbumping Alexander Hamilton off the $10 bill. Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s not crazy about a\ncompromise in which a woman might share the bill with Hamilton.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat sounds pretty second class to me. So I think a woman should have her\nown bill,\xe2\x80\x9d she said.\n\n\n\nThe airing of the interview followed a full day in Iowa, during which the\nfront-runner appeared looser-than-usual on the campaign trail.\n\n\n\nNearly three months into what could be the political fight of her life,\nClinton noted on Tuesday that her time to ride off into the sunset is not\nall that far away.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThis is my last rodeo,\xe2\x80\x9d Clinton said during a campaign stop in the\nfirst-in-the-nation voting state on Tuesday afternoon before taking\nquestions from reporters. Clinton said she wants to play a role in setting\nthe country on the right path before hanging up her hat \xe2\x80\x94 but hopefully,\nshe said, not until 2025, after eight years in the Oval Office.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI believe that we can leave not just the country in good shape for the\nfuture, but we can get a deep bench of young people to decide they want to\ngo into politics to continue the fights that we\xe2\x80\x99re going to be waging,\xe2\x80\x9d she\nsaid.\n\n\n\nThe rodeo characterization may have been more apt than she intended. Her\ncampaign has been criticized in recent days for using a rope to corral\nreporters who were following Clinton during a parade over the July 4th\nweekend. Greeting reporters after an organizing meeting at the Iowa City\nPublic Library, Clinton nodded to the minicontroversy, looking at the\nbarrier between her and the press and asking if it was the equivalent of a\nrope holding them back.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI think it should come down,\xe2\x80\x9d she deadpanned.\n\n\n\nShe also glanced upon a range of issues in the news.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cLet\xe2\x80\x99s not be afraid of the gun lobby, which does not even really represent\nthe majority of gun owners in America,\xe2\x80\x9d Clinton told the crowd of more than\n350 locals. While she refused to take the bait and attack Sanders when\nprompted, she has recently been speaking more about gun control \xe2\x80\x94 an issue\non which she differs from Sanders, who hails from gun-friendly Vermont.\n\n\n\nClinton also focused on the dangers of climate change more than she usually\ndoes, calling it \xe2\x80\x9cone of the most existential threats to our country and\nour world.\xe2\x80\x9d And she again said that \xe2\x80\x9cif a Republican is elected president,\nthat will be the end of the Affordable Care Act.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n\n\nHillary Clinton \'disappointed\' in Donald Trump\n\nAt times musing on her career as secretary of state, Clinton at one point\nsaid that she jokes with former Secretary of State Henry Kissinger about\nthe difficulties of conducting diplomacy in the modern era.\n\n\n\nBut she refused to weigh in forcefully on the ongoing negotiations over\nIran\xe2\x80\x99s nuclear program, telling reporters, \xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t think it\xe2\x80\x99s useful for\nme to publicly comment right now on what the negotiations are attempting to\nresolve.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThere needs to be full transparency, disclosure and verifiable inspections\ngoing forward, and certainly any part of the Iranian nuclear or military\nestablishment that has anything to do with the program past, present and\nfuture needs to be subject to that,\xe2\x80\x9d she added.\n\n\n\nNonetheless, the former top diplomat did call the economic situation in\nGreece a \xe2\x80\x9ctragedy,\xe2\x80\x9d insisting that it is important \xe2\x80\x9cthat we can see an\noutcome here that will actually help Greece recover and keep them in the\neurozone, and keep Europe united.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n*SOCIAL MEDIA*\n\n\n\n*Zeke Miller (7/7/15, 4:53 pm)*\n<https://twitter.com/ZekeJMiller/status/618523312272977920>* - But there\'s\nplenty there to mine that HRC still hasn\'t put to rest.*\n\n\n\n*HRC** NATIONAL COVERAGE*\n\n\n\n*Hillary Clinton Opens a Previously Guarded Door\n<http://www.nytimes.com/politics/first-draft/2015/07/07/today-in-politics-hillary-clinton-opens-a-previously-guarded-door/>\n// NYT // Maggie Haberman \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nMrs. Clinton is about to give her first national close-up in her second\npresidential campaign.\n\n\n\nShe has been a candidate for almost three months. In that time, she\xe2\x80\x99s done\na few news conferences and a smattering of local interviews in early\nstates, but no national sit-downs.\n\n\n\nBut this afternoon, she will sit with the CNN reporter Brianna Keilar in\nIowa. The interview comes as Mrs. Clinton has faced increasing criticism\nfor avoiding questions on policy (the trade deal supported by President\nObama but opposed by many Democrats) and on personal issues (her use of a\nprivate email account at the State Department and the fund-raising\npractices of her family\xe2\x80\x99s foundation).\n\n\n\nMrs. Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s aides said that her early focus was on interacting with as\nmany voters as possible in small settings and that this national interview\nwould be the first of several.\n\n\n\nMuch of the early campaign was about allowing Mrs. Clinton to exist in a\nsafe political space, bringing one of the world\xe2\x80\x99s most famous political\nfaces back down to earth from her days as secretary of state so that voters\ncould forge a bond with her. But over the weekend, a half-dozen protesters\ncreated an unpredictable environment for Mrs. Clinton as she marched in a\nparade in northern New Hampshire. At the same time, her aides sought to\ngive her a buffer so that voters could see her, separating journalists with\na rope, creating a series of viral photos that ricocheted through Twitter.\n\n\n\nThe challenges that the Clinton campaign, and the candidate, face are\nunique. But while her political problems may be complex, the solution that\nher team seems to have settled on, at this point, is fairly simple: Open\nthe doors to the news media a bit wider.\n\n\n\n*Hillary Clinton relied heavily on white voters in 2008. In 2016, it\xe2\x80\x99s\nreversed.\n<http://www.washingtonpost.com/blogs/the-fix/wp/2015/07/07/hillary-clinton-relied-heavily-on-white-voters-in-2008-in-2016-its-reversed/>\n// WaPo // Philip Bump \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nThere are a lot of reasons that Hillary Clinton lost in 2008. One of the\nmost prominent was that she was running against one of the most dynamic\ncandidates in recent memory at a time when people were eager for something\nnew. Another was that the dynamic candidate she was running against was\nblack.\n\n\n\nThe latter became more of a problem over the long term, as Obama racked up\nprimary victories in states with large black populations in the Deep South\nand cut into Clinton\'s dominance elsewhere. In Iowa and New Hampshire, two\nof the whitest states in the union, it played less of a role.\n\n\n\nBut now, weirdly, the whiteness of those early states might be something of\na problem for her. And she\'s actually doing better among non-whites.\n\n\n\nThe CNN/ORC poll released last week reinforced that Clinton is doing much\nbetter in 2016 than any of her opponents -- especially among non-white\nvoters.\n\n\n\nShe leads among white voters, too, of course -- and handily. But her lead\nover Sen. Bernie Sanders (I-Vt.) among white voters is 34 points and\nappears to be narrowing. Among non-white voters -- which we will emphasize\nalso includes Latinos -- it\'s 52 points.\n\n\n\nIf Sanders keeps closing the gap with white voters, that could be a problem\nin Iowa and New Hampshire. Clinton\'s big lead among non-white voters won\'t\nbe much of an advantage until South Carolina -- which, incidentally, she\nlost by a wide margin in 2008.\n\nOne question mark: What becomes of the support for Joe Biden if he finally\ndecides not to run? In CNN\'s polling, Biden ate up one-fifth of the\nnon-white support. If that support goes to Clinton, the dynamic above\nbecomes even more stark.\n\n\n\nRemember, there is no reason at this point to think that Hillary Clinton\nwill not be the Democratic nominee. There is not much of a reason to think\nthat she will lose Iowa, and there\'s only a speculative idea that she might\nlose New Hampshire.\n\n\n\nBut those two states might end up being much closer than we might once have\nexpected in part because they are awfully white -- a fact that might have\nbeen one reason Clinton won New Hampshire in 2008 and was able to stay in\nthe race.\n\n\n\n*Hillary Clinton: Republican candidates \xe2\x80\x98on a spectrum of hostility\xe2\x80\x99 toward\nimmigrants\n<http://www.washingtonpost.com/blogs/post-politics/wp/2015/07/07/hillary-clinton-republican-candidates-on-a-spectrum-of-hostility-toward-immigrants/>\n// WaPo // Ed O\xe2\x80\x99Keefe \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nHillary Clinton says that Republican presidential candidates "range across\na spectrum of hostility" when it comes to immigration and that her campaign\nwill advocate for comprehensive reforms.\n\n\n\nSitting on Tuesday for her first national television interview as a\ndeclared presidential candidate, the Democratic frontrunner lumped together\nall GOP candidates when asked by CNN about Donald Trump\'s recent comments\nabout Mexican immigrants. Interviewer Briana Keilar asked Clinton what she\nmade of Trump\'s comments, noting that he had been a donor to some of her\nprevious campaigns.\n\n\n\n"I\xe2\x80\x99m very disappointed in those comments and I feel very bad and very\ndisappointed with him and with the Republican Party for not responding\nimmediately and saying \'Enough, stop it,\' " she said. "But they are all in\nthe same general area on immigration. They don\xe2\x80\x99t want to provide a path to\ncitizenship. They range across a spectrum of being either grudgingly\nwelcome or hostile toward immigrants. And I\xe2\x80\x99m going to talk about\ncomprehensive immigration reform. I\xe2\x80\x99m going to talk about all the good,\nlaw-abiding, productive members of the immigrant community that I\npersonally know, that I\xe2\x80\x99ve met over the course of my life. That I would\nlike to see have a path to citizenship."\n\n\n\nClinton added that no Republican candidate supports establishing a system\nthat would allow eligible illegal immigrants to eventually apply for\ncitizenship. But Keilar noted that Bush has previously supported such a\nsystem.\n\n\n\nClinton shot back: "He doesn\xe2\x80\x99t believe in a path to citizenship. If he did\nat one time, he no longer does."\n\n\n\nShe added that Republicans are "on a spectrum of hostility, which I think\nis really regrettable in a nation of immigrants like ours. All the way to\nkind of grudging acceptance but refusal to go with a pathway to\ncitizenship. I think that\'s a mistake."\n\n\n\nIn his 2013 book "Immigration Wars," Bush laid out a specific set of\ncriteria that illegal immigrants \xe2\x80\x94 adults and children \xe2\x80\x94 would need to meet\nto apply for legal status and in limited circumstances, perhaps\ncitizenship. He has more recently suggested that citizenship could be\nextended only as part of a bipartisan agreement that included changes in\nU.S.-Mexico border security, a reduction in immigrants allowed to enter the\ncountry due to family ties and an increase in the number allowed to enter\nthe United States for economic purposes.\n\n\n\nBush\'s campaign responded to Clinton\'s comments just moments after they\naired, noting that she voted for amendments that stopped immigration reform\nwhen she was a senator and that she said last year that unaccompanied\nminors crossing the U.S.-Mexico border "should be sent back."\n\n\n\n"She is now running further to the left on immigration policy than even\nPresident Obama\xe2\x80\x99s White House believes is legally feasible," Bush\nspokeswoman Emily Benavides said in a statement. "Hillary Clinton will say\nanything to get elected and her numerous flip-flops on immigration prove\nit."\n\n\n\nBenavides added that as he wrote in his book, Bush "believes in a\nconservative legislative solution to fix our broken immigration system that\nincludes earned legal status for those currently in the country after they\npay fines and taxes, learn English, and commit no substantial crimes while\nsecuring our border."\n\n\n\nIn the CNN interview, Clinton sounded similar to Bush when expressing\ngeneral views on immigration \xe2\x80\x94 that the United States will never be able to\ndeport the 11 million to 12 million people believed to be in the country\nillegally, and that a revamped immigration system would spur economic\ngrowth and increase tax revenues.\n\n\n\n"We know we\'re not going to deport 11 or 12 million people. We shouldn\'t be\nbreaking up families," she said. "We shouldn\xe2\x80\x99t be stopping people from\nhaving the opportunity to be fully integrated legally within our country.\nIt\xe2\x80\x99s good for us, it\xe2\x80\x99s good economically, it\xe2\x80\x99s good for the taxes that will\nbe legally collected. It\xe2\x80\x99s good for the children so that they can go as far\nas their hard work and talent will take them. So I am 100 percent behind\ncomprehensive immigration reform that includes a path to citizenship."\n\n\n\nAnother GOP presidential candidate, Sen. Lindsey O. Graham (S.C.),\nco-authored the bipartisan comprehensive immigration reform bill that\npassed the Senate in 2013, and remains an advocate for allowing eligible\nimmigrants to apply for citizenship.\n\n\n\nClinton made similar charges against GOP candidates to a wider group of\nreporters just before taping the CNN interview in Iowa City.\n\n\n\n"How many people running on the Republican side try to demean immigrants,\ninsult immigrants, cast aspersions on immigrants? They know as well as we\nknow, we are not going to deport 11 or 12 million people living here," she\ntold reporters.\n\n\n\n"I hear the Republican candidates \xe2\x80\x94 and it\'s not even the most vitriolic \xe2\x80\x94\nnone of them any longer support a path to citizenship. All of them would\nbasically consign immigrants to second-class status."\n\n\n\nKeilar also asked Clinton about the possibility that she might face Bush in\nthe general election.\n\n\n\n"Well, we\'ll see, that\xe2\x80\x99s up to first the Republicans on his side and the\nDemocrats on my side," she said. "What\xe2\x80\x99s great about America is anyone can\nrun for president. That\xe2\x80\x99s literally true. And you have to go out and do\nwhat everybody else does \xe2\x80\xa6 you have to work really hard. So whoever is\nnominated by their respective parties will be the nominee, and then we\'ll\nsee who\xe2\x80\x99s on the other side."\n\n\n\n*Hillary Clinton Blames \xe2\x80\x98Constant Barrage of Attacks\xe2\x80\x99 by GOP for Polls\nQuestioning Her Honesty\n<http://www.wsj.com/articles/hillary-clinton-blames-constant-barrage-of-attacks-by-gop-for-polls-questioning-her-honesty-1436312049>\n// WSJ // Laura Meckler \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nHillary Clinton on Tuesday blamed voter perceptions that she is\nuntrustworthy on a \xe2\x80\x9cconstant barrage of attacks\xe2\x80\x9d by Republicans over many\nyears, and said she\xe2\x80\x99s confident she will overcome them during the course of\nthe 2016 presidential campaign.\n\n\n\nSome of those attacks have focused on her exclusive use of a private email\naccount for official business as secretary of state. In an interview with\nCNN, Clinton repeated her assertion that she had complied with rules in\nplace at the time. Mrs. Clinton added that said she went \xe2\x80\x9cabove and beyond\xe2\x80\x9d\nthose standards by submitting her emails to the State Department, though\nrules in place did require her to preserve the records.\n\n\n\nIn her first national television interview, and before that in a brief news\nconference with reporters in Iowa, the front-runner for the Democratic\nnomination hedged as much as she revealed. She declined to say whether she\nsupports raising taxes on the wealthy, said it was best for her to withhold\ncomment on the Iran nuclear negotiations, and dodged a question about which\nwoman\xe2\x80\x99s image should be on the $10 bill. She also declined to discuss the\nrise of the long-shot campaign of rival Sen. Bernie Sanders of Vermont.\n\n\n\nShe said she is \xe2\x80\x9cvery disappointed\xe2\x80\x9d by the disparaging remarks Republican\ncandidate and entrepreneur Donald Trump uttered last month about Mexican\nimmigrants, calling them \xe2\x80\x9crapists,\xe2\x80\x9d and denounced the GOP presidential\nfield for opposing a path to citizenship for people in the U.S. illegally.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThey are all in the same general area on immigration,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cThey\ndon\xe2\x80\x99t want to provide a path to citizenship. They range across the spectrum\nof being either grudgingly welcome or hostile toward immigrants.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nMrs. Clinton also criticized the city of San Francisco for failing to\nfacilitate the deportation of a repeat felon who had been kicked out of the\nU.S. five times before and who earlier this month killed a woman walking on\na city pier. \xe2\x80\x9cThe city made a mistake not to deport someone that the\nfederal government thought should be deported,\xe2\x80\x9d she said.\n\n\n\nSome recent polls have found a drop in the number of voters who see Mrs.\nClinton as honest and trustworthy. Asked about that by CNN, Mrs. Clinton\nsaid that was to be expected \xe2\x80\x9cwhen you are subjected to the kind of\nconstant barrage of attacks that are largely fomented by and coming from\nthe right.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThis has been a theme that has been used against me and my husband for\nmany, many years,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. She said that entire books were filled with\n\xe2\x80\x9cunsubstantiated allegations\xe2\x80\x9d so \xe2\x80\x9cof course that\xe2\x80\x99s going to raise questions\nin people\xe2\x80\x99s minds.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nA recent book suggested conflicts of interest between foreign donations to\nthe Clinton family foundation and her work as secretary of state, though it\nfailed to reveal evidence of a quid pro quo.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI have every confidence during the course of this campaign people are\ngoing to know who will fight for them and be there for them,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cAt\nthe end of the day, I think voters sort it out.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nOn the question of her email practices, she said that everything she did\nwas permitted by law in place at the time. \xe2\x80\x9cThere was no law. There was no\nregulation. There was nothing that did not give me the full authority to\ndecide how I was going to communicate,\xe2\x80\x9d she said.\n\n\n\nShe dismissed concerns expressed by Republicans about her decision to\ndelete emails that she and her aides determined to be unrelated to\ngovernment work. \xe2\x80\x9cI turned over everything I was obligated to turn over and\nthen I moved on,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cPeople delete on a regular basis.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nShe said that her decision to turn over the government-related emails to\nthe State Department, which requested them last year, was \xe2\x80\x9cabove and\nbeyond\xe2\x80\x9d what was required. In fact, in 2009, the National Archives and\nRecords Administration issued regulations that said agencies allowing\nemployees to do official business on unofficial email accounts had to\nensure that any records sent on private email systems are preserved \xe2\x80\x9cin the\nappropriate agency record-keeping system.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n*The making of a Hillary Clinton echo chamber\n<http://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/the-making-of-a-hillary-clinton-echo-chamber/2015/07/07/01625c5e-24ae-11e5-b72c-2b7d516e1e0e_story.html>\n// WaPo // Philip Rucker \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nOne day in May, operatives from a Washington-based super PAC gathered New\nHampshire mayors, state representatives and local politicos at St. Anselm\nCollege for a day of training.\n\n\n\nThey rehearsed their personal tales of how they met Hillary Rodham Clinton\nand why they support her for president. They sharpened their defenses of\nher record as secretary of state. They scripted their arguments for why the\nDemocratic front-runner has been \xe2\x80\x9ca lifetime champion of income\nopportunity.\xe2\x80\x9d And they polished their on-camera presentations in a series\nof mock interviews.\n\n\n\nThe objective of the sessions: to nurture a seemingly grass roots echo\nchamber of Clinton supporters reading from the same script across the\ncommunities that dot New Hampshire, a critical state that hosts the\nnation\xe2\x80\x99s first presidential primary.\n\n\n\nThe super PAC, called Correct the Record, convened similar talking-point\ntutorials and media-training classes in May and June in three other early\nvoting states \xe2\x80\x94 Iowa, South Carolina and Nevada \xe2\x80\x94 as well as sessions\nearlier this spring in California.\n\n\n\nPresidential campaigns have for decades fed talking points to surrogates\nwho appear on national television or introduce candidates on the stump. But\nthe effort to script and train local supporters is unusually ambitious and\nillustrates the extent to which the Clinton campaign and its web of\nsanctioned, allied super PACs are leaving nothing to chance.\n\n\n\nWhen, say, a Londonderry Times reporter calls a Rockingham County\nDemocratic Committee member for comment on Clinton, he or she will parrot\nCorrect the Record\xe2\x80\x99s talking points about Clinton having been a fighter for\nthe middle class \xe2\x80\x94 from improving rural health care as first lady of\nArkansas to raising the minimum wage as a senator from New York.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe are holding sessions with top communicators across the country where we\ntalk about the best ways to discuss Secretary Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s strong record of\naccomplishments, how to articulate Secretary Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s positions most\neffectively and how to correct Republican operatives\xe2\x80\x99 distortions of the\nfacts,\xe2\x80\x9d said Adrienne Watson, communications director at Correct the Record.\n\n\n\nBut asking local supporters to use talking points could undermine the\norganic nature of grass-roots political interactions. No longer can a\njournalist call up a state representative in Iowa and expect to hear his or\nher personal, unvarnished take on Clinton \xe2\x80\x94 nor can a Rotary Club member\nwatch a fellow small-business owner talk about Clinton at their monthly\nluncheon \xe2\x80\x94 without suspecting he or she is reading from a script.\n\n\n\nThe super PAC\xe2\x80\x99s effort also comes as Clinton struggles on the campaign\ntrail to appear accessible and genuine. Some Democrats have long believed\nClinton sounds too scripted on the stump, especially compared to Sen.\nBernie Sanders (I-Vt.), her insurgent primary rival whose authenticity and\nliberal message are drawing thousands of Democrats to his rallies.\n\n\n\nNew Hampshire state Sen. Lou D\xe2\x80\x99Allesandro, a local elected official for\ndecades and a longtime Clinton supporter, said he did not attend Correct\nthe Record\xe2\x80\x99s session, which was held May 18 at the New Hampshire Institute\nof Politics at St. Anselm.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99ve known Hillary for a long time,\xe2\x80\x9d D\xe2\x80\x99Allesandro said. \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99ve known her\nhusband for a long time. She\xe2\x80\x99s been at our home. I\xe2\x80\x99ve visited her in\nWashington. I believe that I can articulate where she is on issues and I\nreally don\xe2\x80\x99t need anybody to tell me what to say. I believe that you stand\nfor people because you believe what they stand for and you articulate it.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nCorrect the Record \xe2\x80\x94 one of several super PACs run by Clinton ally David\nBrock \xe2\x80\x94 coordinates some of its activities with Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s campaign, but\nofficials said the campaign played no role in the training sessions.\n\n\n\nThe Clinton campaign has its own surrogate operation that distributes\ntalking points to supporters to ensure that their messages in local and\nnational media are consistent.\n\n\n\nThe super PAC\xe2\x80\x99s on-camera media training was conducted by the Franklin\nForum and led by the group\xe2\x80\x99s president, John Neffinger, a Democratic\nstrategist who specializes in coaching people for television interviews.\n\n\n\nCorrect the Record held a series of similar media sessions in the spring of\n2014 to prepare Clinton backers for interviews surrounding her national\nbook tour for \xe2\x80\x9cHard Choices,\xe2\x80\x9d the memoir from her State Department years.\n\n\n\nWatson said the super PAC plans to hold additional campaign-oriented\ntraining sessions later this year.\n\n\n\nTo supporters like Eleni Kounalakis, who served as ambassador to Hungary in\nClinton\xe2\x80\x99s State Department, the program is welcome news. In March, she\nparticipated along with about 20 other supporters in a Correct the Record\nsession in San Francisco and said she thought it helped her and other\nClinton fans refine the case they make for Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s candidacy in public.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cMany people who are very vocal in supporting Secretary Clinton are very\ncomfortable taking about why among their friends and in small groups \xe2\x80\x94 but\nwhen it comes to talking to the media, that can be very intimidating,\xe2\x80\x9d\nKounalakis said. \xe2\x80\x9cSome people feel like, I know Hillary has been there for\nthe working person in her life, in her career, but I want someone to help\nme prepare those arguments so that I have that confidence to speak in a\nbroader context.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nNick Sottile, 21, president of the College Democrats of South Carolina,\nsaid he felt \xe2\x80\x9clucky\xe2\x80\x9d to attend a May 7 Correct the Record session in\nColumbia, S.C.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt got right to the heart of things \xe2\x80\x94 how to cut through the noise and\ntalk about Secretary Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s record,\xe2\x80\x9d Sottile said. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd not just what to\nsay, but how to talk about her as a young person in South Carolina. It was\ngood training in how to be an effective talker.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n*Lawmakers: Feds Should Have Deported Undocumented Immigrant Before SF Pier\nShooting\n<http://www.nbcnewyork.com/news/national-international/Lawmakers-Feds-Deported-Francisco-Sanchez-Steinle-Pier-14-312193501.html>\n// AP \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nLawmakers and politicians are criticizing the failure to deport an\nimmigrant with multiple felony convictions and an outstanding drug warrant\nwho allegedly went on to murder a woman in San Francisco.\n\n\n\nPresidential hopeful Hillary Clinton, in an interview with CNN, said that\nthe City of San Francisco\'s law enforcement officials were wrong to release\nfrom jail Mexican national Francisco Sanchez, who is now at the center of a\nnational immigration controversy.\n\n\n\n"The city made a mistake, not to deport someone that the federal government\nstrongly felt should be deported,\'\' Clinton said. "So I have absolutely no\nsupport for a city that ignores the strong evidence that should be acted\non.\'\'\n\n\n\nThe Sheriff\'s Department ignored "strong evidence" that Sanchez should have\nbeen turned over to immigration officials and deported, according to\nClinton.\n\n\n\nIn a similar vein, Sen. Dianne Feinstein (D-Calif.) issued a statement\nTuesday saying that she has personally been investigating the circumstances\nsurrounding Kathryn Steinle\'s fatal shooting July 1.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI strongly believe that an undocumented individual, convicted of multiple\nfelonies and with a detainer request from ICE, should not have been\nreleased," she said. "We should focus on deporting convicted criminals, not\nsetting them loose on our streets."\n\n\n\nFeinstein also wrote to San Francisco Mayor Ed Lee to express her "deep\nconcern" about Sanchez\'s release, adding that it "led to last week\xe2\x80\x99s tragic\ndeath." Her letter "urged" Lee to "prevent such a tragedy" from reoccurring\nby joining the Department of Homeland Security\'s Priority Enforcement\nProgram, which would enable local law enforcement agencies to "provide\nnotice to ICE before releasing aliens with long criminal records."\n\nThe San Francisco mayor\'s office said it has reached out to Department of\nHomeland Security officials to determine if there\'s a way to cooperate with\nfederal immigration officials while still maintaining the sanctuary policy.\n\n\n\n"Mayor Lee shares the senator\'s concerns surrounding the nature of Mr.\nSanchez\' transfer to San Francisco and release,\'\' said Christine Falvey, a\nspokeswoman for the mayor. "As the mayor has stated, we need to gather all\nof the facts as we develop potential solutions.\'\'\n\n\n\nDemocratic Sen. Barbara Boxer, also from Northern California, said she\nasked Gov. Jerry Brown if state law was followed in the release of Sanchez.\n\n\n\n"For decades, I have supported deporting violent criminals, and I have\nalways believed that sanctuary should not be given to felons,\'\' Boxer said.\n\n\n\nSen. Ron Johnson (R-Wis) echoed the same sentiment.\n\n\n\n"He had a criminal warrant but was released into the general society to\ncommit a murder. Does that make any sense to you?\'\' Johnson, who chairs the\nSenate\'s homeland security committee, demanded to know at a hearing.\n"Because I\'ll tell you it doesn\'t make any sense to the American public.\'\'\n\n\n\nPhilip Miller, an official with U.S. Immigration and Customs Enforcement,\nblamed San Francisco, saying officials there did not honor a federal\nrequest, known as a "detainer," to keep Francisco Sanchez in custody.\n\n\n\nSanchez, who is from Mexico and is in the United States illegally,\nallegedly shot and killed 32-year-old Kathryn Steinle last week as she was\nsightseeing with her father along a popular local pier.\n\n\n\n"In that particular case our detainer was not honored,\'\' Miller said. "San\nFrancisco sheriff\'s department did not honor our detainer.\'\'\n\n\n\nSan Francisco Sheriff Ross Mirkarimi has defended his office\'s decision,\nsaying ICE should have issued an arrest warrant earlier. Miller declined\nafter the hearing to comment on that assertion. But Virginia Kice, a\nspokeswoman for ICE told NBC Bay Area this week that "obtaining judicial\nwarrants is not only unnecessary, it would place an immense burden on both\nICE and the federal courts." She added that last year, ICE deported more\nthan 177,000 immigrants with criminal convictions.\n\n\n\nSteinle\'s death has offered ammunition to GOP critics of Obama\nadministration policies, including presidential candidate Donald Trump,\nwho\'s cited it to justify his claims that many immigrants are criminals.\nSanchez has a long criminal history, but mostly for drug use, dating back\nto the 1990s, federal records show.\n\n\n\nAt the same time it plays into a larger, politically charged immigration\ndebate between federal authorities and local jurisdictions.\n\n\n\nHundreds of local jurisdictions have refused to participate in a disputed\nfederal program, Secure Communities, that allows local authorities to turn\nover information on immigrants they pick up to the federal government. San\nFrancisco takes it farther than many, even boasting of itself as a\n``sanctuary city\'\' that protects immigrants.\n\n\n\nPresident Barack Obama announced last fall he was ending the Secure\nCommunities program and replacing it with a new approach meant to address\nconcerns about immigrants being targeted.\n\n\n\nBut that has sparked more criticism from Republicans who embraced Secure\nCommunities as an effective law enforcement tool and oppose Obama\'s\nattempts to change immigration law through executive actions without\nCongress\' consent.\n\n\n\nHouse Judiciary Chairman Bob Goodlatte, R-Va., announced Tuesday he would\nbring Homeland Security Secretary Jeh Johnson before his committee next\nweek to answer questions on the matter.\n\n\n\n"Just recently, we were reminded that the Obama administration\'s reckless\nactions, such as permitting sanctuary city policies, lead to tragic and\ndeadly consequences,\'\' Goodlatte said.\n\n\n\n*Hillary Clinton Hands Jeb Bush A Present On Immigration\n<http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2015/07/07/hillary-clinton-jeb-bush-immigration_n_7747652.html?1436306696>\n// HuffPo // Igor Bobic \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nHillary Clinton denounced Donald Trump\'s controversial comments about\nimmigrants in her first national interview as a 2016 presidential\ncandidate. But in the process, she inadvertently handed Republican rival\nJeb Bush a present on a silver platter.\n\n\n\nThe Democratic front-runner told CNN\'s Brianna Keilar Tuesday that she was\n"very disappointed" with the celebrity hotelier for calling some Mexican\nmigrants rapists and criminals. She criticized the rest of the 2016\nRepublican presidential candidates for not moving quickly enough to\ndistance themselves from Trump and noted their opposition to comprehensive\nimmigration reform.\n\n\n\n"He doesn\'t believe in a path to citizenship. If he did at one time, he no\nlonger does," she said of Bush, the former governor of Florida.\n\n\n\nThe broadside could hurt Bush among Hispanic voters if Clinton succeeds in\nportraying him as opposed to immigration reform. It\'s a smart, long-term\nplay against a well-funded Republican with a decent chance of winning the\nnomination.\n\n\n\nFor the moment, however, Bush faces more immediate challenges as he\ntraverses early primary states. Chief among them is his effort to win over\nconservatives who believe that he supports granting undocumented immigrants\n"amnesty." In fact, Bush says that undocumented workers should be able to\nearn legal status, \xe2\x80\x9cnot necessarily citizenship.\xe2\x80\x9d Clinton, however, says\nthat anything short of a path to citizenship for undocumented immigrants is\n"code for second-class status."\n\n\n\nImmigration remains one of the most divisive topics among Republicans in\nthe early caucus state of Iowa, but there are still far more who oppose a\npath to citizenship than support it. According to a Quinnipiac University\npoll released Monday, 46 percent of likely Republican caucus goers in Iowa\nsaid undocumented immigrants should be required to leave the country, while\n34 percent said they should be allowed to stay with some sort of path to\ncitizenship.\n\n\n\nAny reminder that Bush opposes "amnesty" is good news in Iowa -- regardless\nof whether it comes from the candidate or his potential Democratic rival.\n\n\n\n*Hillary Clinton Piles On San Francisco Officials, Putting Sanctuary Cities\nUnder Even More Heat\n<http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2015/07/07/sanctuary-cities_n_7749406.html>\n// HuffPo // Elise Foley \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nAfter a deadly shooting in San Francisco, allegedly by a man who had been\ndeported five times, lawmakers are calling on the county to drop its policy\nagainst cooperating with immigration enforcement.\n\n\n\nPresidential candidate Hillary Clinton became the most high-profile\nDemocrat to wade into the debate on Tuesday, telling CNN that San Francisco\nshould have worked with agents at Immigration and Customs Enforcement.\n\n\n\n"The city made a mistake, not to deport someone that the federal government\nstrongly felt should be deported," she said in an interview. "So I have\nabsolutely no support for a city that ignores the strong evidence that\nshould be acted on."\n\n\n\nSen. Dianne Feinstein (D-Calif.), meanwhile, sent a letter on Tuesday to\nSan Francisco Mayor Ed Lee urging him to cooperate with ICE, implying the\ncounty\'s failure to do so allowed for the shooting of 32-year-old Kathryn\nSteinle, allegedly at the hands of a previously deported undocumented\nimmigrant named Francisco Sanchez.\n\n\n\nGOP lawmakers, who are more prone to support a greater federal thumbprint\non detention policy, have decried San Francisco leaders for acting\nirresponsibly. One of them, Rep. Duncan Hunter (R-Calif.), said he plans to\nintroduce a bill penalizing cities that do not cooperate with ICE.\n\n\n\nWith the debate around immigration already red hot due to the charged\nrhetoric of the 2016 campaign, the incident in San Francisco could end up\nprompting a shift in recent trends in detention policy. For years, local\ncommunities have been limiting their collaboration with immigration\nenforcement officials, with more than 300 cities and counties adopting\npolicies against fully complying with ICE\'s requests. Some, like San\nFrancisco, barely deal with the agency at all, while others limit\ninteractions except in cases of more serious crimes.\n\n\n\nThe widespread resistance led the Obama administration to announce in\nNovember that it would drop the Secure Communities program, which asked\npolice to hold individuals for ICE so they could be picked up for\ndeportation purposes.\n\n\n\nThe immediate fallout from the shooting in San Francisco appears to be a\nchange in those particular political winds.\n\n\n\nBut the debate remains a sensitive one, with activists and even local\nofficials warning that a greater federal role could harm other law\nenforcement activities, drain resources and spark court challenges.\n\n\n\nAt issue is whether local law enforcement, at the request of ICE, should --\nor even legally could -- hold individuals who it otherwise would have\nreleased. Immigration advocates have warned that doing so creates fear in\nthe undocumented community and sweeps up people for deportation because of\nlow-level crimes or arrests they are never convicted for.\n\n\n\nTo accommodate those concerns, the administration is pushing a new policy\ncalled the Priority Enforcement Program, which was announced last November.\nUnder PEP, according to the administration, ICE would target individuals at\nhigher priority for deportation, such as convicted criminals. The program\nalso will ask local law enforcement to notify the agency when it plans to\nrelease a suspected deportable immigrant, rather than for holds.\n\n\n\nThat program hasn\'t been rolled out nationwide, and an ICE official said\ntheir appeals to San Francisco officials to work with them haven\'t gone\nanywhere. But critics are charging that had ICE implemented PEP in San\nFrancisco sooner, Sanchez, who said he shot Steinle last Wednesday before\nsaying on Tuesday that he was not guilty, would not have been released into\nthe community.\n\n\n\nPrior to the shooting, Sanchez had been deported five times and had seven\nfelony convictions, according to authorities. Twice, ICE put in detainer\nrequests for him. The first was with the Bureau of Prisons, where he was\nserving a sentence for the federal crime of illegally re-entering the U.S.\nas a felon. Sanchez was transferred by the Bureau of Prisons to the San\nFrancisco sheriff\'s office because he had an arrest warrant for a\n20-year-old marijuana case. ICE then put in a request to the sheriff\'s\noffice to detain him. After the district attorney declined to prosecute\nthat charge, he was released in April.\n\n\n\nOfficials at the San Francisco County Sheriff\'s Office and ICE have since\nblamed each other for that release, with the local authorities saying ICE\nshould have gotten a judicial warrant if they wanted Sanchez to be held,\nand ICE claiming it was never notified that the man was about to be let go.\n\n\n\nWith the debate expanding beyond the particulars of what happened and into\nthe realm of public policy, critics of Secure Communities worry the tragedy\nin San Francisco will be used as a cudgel against cities that have tried to\nmove their police departments out of the immigration enforcement business.\nThey warn there are not just humanitarian and budget constraints to\nconsider, but constitutional complications as well.\n\n\n\n"I\'ve seen this happen over and over again where anti-immigrant groups try\nto use these types of horrible cases to change policies but there are\nconstitutional protections, and people cannot be held for immigration\nwithout a judge signing a warrant," said Angela Chan, a policy director at\nthe Asian Law Caucus.\n\n\n\nPolice chiefs could be an ally in pushing back against greater federal\ninvolvement in local immigration matters. Many have contended that they\nneed to strike a balance between acting as enforcement agents and\nperforming their duties to protect the public. Montgomery County Police\nChief J. Thomas Manger, also the president of the Major Cities Chiefs\nAssociation, said doing too much of the former risks hurting the\nrelationship law enforcement has with the broader community.\n\n\n\nMontgomery County officials announced last year that immigrants would no\nlonger be held for ICE without demonstration that the individual likely\ncommitted a crime. Manger approves of PEP and said his office notifies ICE\nwhen individuals are being released upon request. But the fact that\nindividuals are released and go on to commit crime is a risk in all law\nenforcement, he insisted, and not just specific to immigration.\n\n\n\n"I\'ve been a cop for 38 years," he said. "And for longer than I\'ve been a\ncop, [criminals] have been getting out of jail and doing bad things again.\nThe fact is that the law allows you to hold someone for a certain amount of\ntime and when the law says you\'ve got to release them, you\'ve got to\nrelease them.\n\n\n\n*Clinton says GOP field ranges from \'grudgingly welcome\' to \'hostile\'\ntoward immigrants\n<http://www.usnews.com/news/politics/articles/2015/07/07/clinton-in-iowa-warns-about-gop-control-of-white-house>\n// AP // Catherine Lucey & Ken Thomas \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nHillary Rodham Clinton said a Republican in the White House would mark a\n"big U-turn" for the nation and assailed the GOP presidential field\'s\nstance on an immigration overhaul.\n\n\n\nAsked about Jeb Bush, the Democratic presidential candidate said: "He\ndoesn\'t believe in a path to citizenship. I\'m not running my campaign\nfor the press, I\'m running it for the voters," she explained. "I totally\nrespect the press and what the press has to do. I wanted and was determined\nto have the time that I needed to actually meet and listen to people. I had\nnot been involved in domestic politics while I was Secretary of State, and\nI just wanted to get my own feel, my own time, face to face with people."\n\n\n\n"Everything has its own time and I\'m on my own rhythm," she said.\n\n\n\nWhile that may be true, avoiding the press had become a dominant theme of\nClinton\'s early days on the campaign trail. Clinton said she\'d always\nplanned "to spend the first 90 days... getting my feel of what was going on\nin the country," but her refusal to answer questions from reporters on the\ntrail was so frequent that it made headlines.\n\n\n\nAs Clinton told Keiler, "it\'ll be 90 days [since the launch of her\ncampaign] on Sunday," and the time to open up to the media has come. But if\nAmericans are expecting more transparency from Clinton, they may be sorely\ndisappointed.\n\n\n\n"I didn\'t hear a more open or transparent Hillary Clinton," Keilar said\nafter her interview. "I heard her not engaging on the issue of Bernie\nSanders. He\'s a self-described Democratic socialist. I asked her why is he\ngarnering this support, this enthusiasm, that you don\'t seem to among\nDemocrats. She wouldn\'t engage on that. Even on this concern of if she were\nto face off against Jeb Bush, and there would be this dynastic race between\na Bush and a Clinton... she wouldn\'t engage on that. She was very quick to\nmove on."\n\n\n\nKeilar bears some responsibility for that, of course. She hardly pressed\nClinton to answer the questions she was dodging and rushed from topic to\ntopic. If an interviewer is hoping to pin Clinton down on anything, she or\nhe will probably have to take a more Terry Gross-like approach.\n\n\n\nMore likely, however, is that Clinton herself will decide to be more\ntransparent. There are almost 500 days left till election day; if she is\nserious about "doing a lot more press," she\'ll need to come up with a\nbetter strategy than "dodge and defend."\n\n\n\n*Clinton says Puerto Rico should have access to U.S. bankruptcy laws\n<http://www.reuters.com/article/2015/07/07/us-usa-election-clinton-puertorico-idUSKCN0PH11920150707>\n// Reuters // Amanda Becker \xe2\x80\x93 June 30, 2015 *\n\n\n\nU.S. Democratic presidential candidate Hillary Clinton said Tuesday that\nPuerto Rico\'s public entities should be able to use U.S. bankruptcy laws to\nrestructure some $72 billion in debt.\n\n\n\nLike U.S. states, Puerto Rico, a commonwealth, cannot file for bankruptcy\nprotection. Unlike U.S. states, Puerto Rico\'s public entities, including\nmunicipalities, are not covered by U.S. Chapter 9 bankruptcy laws.\n\n\n\nPuerto Rico\'s non-voting delegate in the U.S. Congress has called for\nlegislation that would allow Puerto Rico to access the same bankruptcy laws\navailable to other municipalities, as has Puerto Rico\'s Governor Alejandro\nGarcia Padilla.\n\n\n\nThe U.S. Court of Appeals for the First Circuit late Monday affirmed a\nlower court decision to strike down Puerto Rican legislation aimed at\ngranting local municipalities the right to enter bankruptcy, but said\nexcluding the U.S. territory\'s public entities from federal bankruptcy law\nwas unconstitutional.\n\n\n\n"Congress and the Obama administration need to partner with Puerto Rico by\nproviding real support and tools so that Puerto Rico can do the hard work\nit will take to get on a path toward stability and prosperity," Clinton\nsaid in a statement provided to Reuters.\n\n\n\n"As a first step, Congress should provide Puerto Rico the same authority\nthat states already have to enable severely distressed government entities,\nincluding municipalities and public corporations, to restructure their\ndebts under Chapter 9 of the Bankruptcy Code," Clinton added.\n\n\n\nThe White House said last week that there is "no one in the administration"\nthat is "contemplating a federal bailout of Puerto Rico" but that the U.S.\nCongress should "take a look at" whether Puerto Rico\'s government-owned\ncorporations should be able to access Chapter 9 bankruptcy protection.\n\n\n\nCongressional Republicans largely oppose such a step. Republican\npresidential candidate Jeb Bush said in April that he thinks Puerto Rico\'s\npublic agencies should have the ability to use U.S. bankruptcy laws.\n\n\n\n"We\'re not talking about a bailout, we\'re talking about a fair shot at\nsuccess," Clinton said Tuesday.\n\n\n\nClinton said in the statement that the "inconsistent and incoherent"\napplication of U.S. federal law to Puerto Rico contributed to its economic\nsituation, noting high utility rates and unemployment have led to an\neconomy that has shrunk for eight of the last nine years.\n\n\n\n"One troubling example of this treatment is the lack of equity in federal\nfunding for Puerto Rico under Medicaid and Medicare," Clinton said of\nhealth insurance programs sponsored by the U.S. government.\n\n\n\nClinton, also a former first lady, is the front runner for the Democratic\nnomination ahead of the general election in November 2016.\n\n\n\n*Meme says Hillary Clinton\'s top donors are banks and corporations, Bernie\nSanders\' are labor unions\n<http://www.politifact.com/truth-o-meter/statements/2015/jul/07/facebook-posts/meme-says-hillary-clintons-top-donors-are-banks-an/>\n// Politifact // Louis Jacobson \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nAs Vermont Sen. Bernie Sanders gains ground on Democratic presidential\nfrontrunner Hillary Clinton, the two candidates\xe2\x80\x99 supporters have been\nsparring, including over campaign donations.\n\n\n\nRecently, a reader sent us a social media meme that paints Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s list\nof donors as dominated by corporate interests, whereas Sanders\xe2\x80\x99 top 10\ndonors come largely from labor unions -- a dichotomy that, to Democratic\nprimary voters, puts Sanders in a more favorable light.\n\n\n\n"Hillary: Top ten donor list. Representing banks, corporations and media,"\nthe meme reads, providing a top-10 list with dollar amounts. "Bernie: Top\nten donor list. Representing people." The meme is topped by each\ncandidate\xe2\x80\x99s presidential campaign logo. (See the meme below.)\n\n\n\nWe can\xe2\x80\x99t tell who produced this meme, but we thought it was worth a closer\nlook.\n\n\n\nWe\xe2\x80\x99ll start by noting that reasonable people can disagree about whether\nlabor unions represent "people," as the meme says, as opposed to just\nunionized workers, who are a relatively small subset of the entire\npopulation. We\xe2\x80\x99ll also note that while this meme may appeal to union\nsupporters and critics of Wall Street and big corporations, it also could\nbe used as evidence that Sanders is just as reliant on one type of donor --\nlabor unions -- as Clinton is on big corporations.\n\n\n\nWe found that the data cited in the meme refers to cumulative donations\nover the course of each candidate\xe2\x80\x99s political career as calculated by the\nCenter for Responsive Politics, not just fundraising from the current\npresidential cycle. (Clinton and Sanders have announced their fundraising\nhauls for the second quarter of 2015, but have not yet released the full\ndata that is due at the Federal Election Commission by July 15; a more\ncomplete analysis of the data will be compiled by the Center for Responsive\nPolitics after that.)\n\n\n\nFor Clinton, we found a high degree of similarity with the meme when we\nchecked the database on July 6.\n\n\n\nClinton\xe2\x80\x99s top 10 cumulative donors between between 1999 and 2016 were, in\ndescending order, Citigroup ($782,327), Goldman Sachs ($711,490), DLA Piper\n($628,030), JPMorgan Chase ($620,919), EMILY\xe2\x80\x99s List ($605,174) Morgan\nStanley ($543,065), Time Warner ($411,296), Skadden Arps ($406,640), Lehman\nBrothers ($362,853) and Cablevision Systems ($336,288).\n\n\n\nThat list is quite close to what the meme says. It includes five\nfinancial-services companies, two law firms that do a lot of corporate\nwork, two media conglomerates and one group, EMILY\xe2\x80\x99s list, that supports\nabortion-rights Democratic candidates. It\xe2\x80\x99s worth noting that Clinton was a\nsenator from New York, meaning that some of the donors on her list were not\nsimply Wall Street and corporate behemoths, but also constituents, based in\nNew York.\n\n\n\nThe database results for Sanders are also quite close to what\xe2\x80\x99s in the\nmeme. The data for Sanders goes back to 1989.\n\n\n\nHis top 10 are, in descending order, Machinists/Aerospace Workers union\n($105,000), Teamsters union ($93,700), National Education Association\n($84,350), United Auto Workers ($79,650), United Food & Commercial Workers\nunion ($72,500), Communications Workers of America ($68,000), Laborers\nUnion ($64,000), Carpenters & Joiners Union ($62,000), National Association\nof Letter Carriers ($61,000), and the American Association for Justice\n($60,500).\n\n\n\nIn the meme, the letter carriers\xe2\x80\x99 union makes the list, but the Center for\nResponsive Politics has the American Federation of State, County and\nMunicipal Employees cracking the top 10 instead. Either way, nine of the 10\nare unions, and the tenth is the national association representing\nplaintiffs\xe2\x80\x99 attorneys. During his career, Sanders has received strong\nsupport from progressive Democrats, so this pattern of financial backing is\nnot surprising.\n\n\n\nSo the meme is pretty accurate for both candidates. However, we see a few\nthings worth pointing out.\n\n\n\nAs we noted, this data refers to their entire political careers back to the\n1990s. Once the full presidential data is released, those figures may show\ndifferent patterns. "That is not made clear" in the meme, said Anthony J.\nCorrado, a campaign-finance expert at Colby College. "Most people would\nassume that this is money raised so far in the 2016 presidential campaign."\n\n\n\nAlso, the "donors" listed are not the ones who gave the money, since that\nwould be against the law. Rather, it was their PACs, employees and those\nemployees\xe2\x80\x99 families. In fact, due to how the forms are filled out, the data\nis less likely to capture individual donations from union members than from\nemployers of companies. Most individual donations are listed by employer,\nand if, say, a union carpenter lists his affiliation as his company, the\nfact that he\xe2\x80\x99s a union member wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t be recorded.\n\n\n\nFinally, lists such as this ignore that both candidates are collecting many\nsmall donations, too. According to the Clinton campaign, she raised roughly\n$50 million in contributions under $200 during her \'08 campaign. Data for\nthe 2016 cycle is not available yet.\n\n\n\nAll told, it\xe2\x80\x99s possible to look at the top donors on the two lists and say\nboth candidates are captive to a particular set of interest groups, said\nKyle Kondik, managing editor of Sabato\xe2\x80\x99s Crystal Ball at the University of\nVirginia Center for Politics. However, he added, "labor is a Democratic\nconstituency whose beliefs generally line up with Democratic policies, and\nwe\xe2\x80\x99re talking about a Democratic primary here. So all things being equal,\nSanders\xe2\x80\x99 donor list probably looks better, politically, than Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s."\n\n\n\nKondik added that, as the meme indicates, Clinton has a much larger\nreservoir of money than Sanders has. "The value of having a large financial\nadvantage over your competitors in a primary setting seems to be worth\noccasional questions about how the financial advantage was built," he said.\n\n\n\nOur ruling\n\n\n\nSocial media memes say that Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s top 10 donors are mainly "banks,\ncorporations and media," while Bernie Sanders\xe2\x80\x99 top 10 donors are labor\nunions. This contention fits quite closely with campaign data from the\nCenter for Responsive Politics. However, it\xe2\x80\x99s worth noting that this data\nrefers to cumulative donations as far back as the 1980s, rather than just\ndonations to their current presidential bids. The statement is accurate but\nneeds clarification, so we rate it Mostly True.\n\n\n\n*Clinton vows to make \xe2\x80\x98comprehensive\xe2\x80\x99 immigration reform cornerstone She told a story about the\n2009 United Nations Climate Change Conference in Copenhagen, Denmark.\nClinton and President Obama were trying to negotiate terms with India and\nChina\xe2\x80\x94two of the fastest-developing countries in the world\xe2\x80\x94for a climate\nchange agreement.\n\n\n\nThe problem: China and India\'s leaders were nowhere to be found. Clinton\nsaid she and Obama "sent out scouts," who found that the leaders were\nmeeting in a clandestine conference room. Clinton and Obama marched to the\nroom, she said, and pushed past Chinese security guards to confront the\nheads of state. As a result, the assembled countries signed an accord\noutlining emissions pledges and other goals for energy use, though much of\nthe text was nonbinding.\n\n\n\n"We would not be in as strong a position if the president had not pursued\neverything from auto emissions to utility controls," Clinton added on\nTuesday.\n\n\n\nAside from climate change, Clinton gradually began filling in some of the\ndetails of her economic and social agenda. And she opened up a little more\non Democratic politics and her own future.\n\n\n\nThe economy and immigration:\n\n\n\nClinton blamed Republican presidents for the recent economic crises in the\nU.S., and said that trickle-down economics needs to be "buried six feet\nunder."\n\n\n\n"There seems to be a pattern here, and we cannot afford to go back to the\nfailed economic policies of the past," she said. "We have to be committed\nto electing a Democrat who will build on what works with actual evidence\n... so that we build shared prosperity that everybody benefits from."\n\n\n\nOn income inequality and immigration reform, there is a yawning chasm\nbetween Republicans and Democrats, especially in Iowa. A recent Quinnipiac\nUniversity poll found that 70 percent of likely Republican caucus voters\nsay the government should not pursue policies to reduce income inequality,\nwhile 91 percent of their Democratic counterparts said the government\nshould pursue such policies.\n\n\n\nThe same poll found that 46 percent of Iowa Republicans say undocumented\nimmigrants living in the U.S. should be required to leave, while 83 percent\nof Democrats said the immigrants should be given a path to citizenship.\n\n\n\nClinton called the Republican discourse on immigration a "very stale,\ndestructive debate."\n\n\n\n"I don\'t care how many people running for president on the Republican side\ntry to demean immigrants, insult immigrants, cast aspersions on\nimmigrants," Clinton said. You voted for it once. Let\'s vote for it\nagain."\n\n\n\nEducation:\n\n\n\nClinton stressed public education, especially the need to improve the\ngovernment\'s Head Start early childhood program and to implement universal\npre-kindergarten.\n\n\n\n"If we do not have early childhood education, we will never get the results\nfor the vast majority of our children as we could," she said. Cory Booker (D-N.J.) and Rep. Mia Love (R-Utah).
