"I would hope that we would keep this\ndebate a debate about the issues, and I would prefer, not that I\'m able to\ntell a super PAC what to do, I would prefer that we didn\'t have any super\nPACs, frankly.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nThe ads in question, produced by the group Generation Forward, attacked\nSanders, a Vermont senator, for his mixed record on gun control, asserting\nthat he is \xe2\x80\x9cno progressive\xe2\x80\x9d on that issue. The ads were targeted to Web\nviewers in Iowa, the nation\xe2\x80\x99s first presidential caucus state.\n\n\n\nGeneration Forward is run by allies of O\xe2\x80\x99Malley, including a family friend\nand a former press aide. Federal law limits coordination between declared\ncandidates and independent groups set up to work for their election. Super\nPACs, which can take unlimited contributions, have flourished in the wake\nof the 2010 Supreme Court decision known as Citizens United.\n\n\n\nSanders has urged his allies not to form a super PAC and is one of the few\n2016 presidential candidates without one.\n\n\n\nIn recent weeks, Sanders has jumped in the polls in both Iowa and New\nHampshire, emerging as the leading alternative to Democratic frontrunner\nHillary Rodham Clinton, while O\xe2\x80\x99Malley\xe2\x80\x99s campaign has remained stalled in\nthe low single digits.\n\n\n\nDuring the radio interview that aired Tuesday, O\xe2\x80\x99Malley also elaborated on\nhis characterization of Sanders last week as a \xe2\x80\x9cprotest candidate\xe2\x80\x9d in an\ninterview with The Washington Post.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cHistory has shown usually the candidates that are surging in the summer\nare not the candidates who are surging in the primary,\xe2\x80\x9d O\xe2\x80\x99Malley said.\n\n\n\nHe made his comments in advance of a planned trip Wednesday and Thursday to\nNew Hampshire, the nation\xe2\x80\x99s first presidential primary state. O\xe2\x80\x99Malley has\nappearances scheduled in Manchester, Derry, Concord and Wolfeboro.\n\n\n\n*Martin O\xe2\x80\x99Malley racked up $339,200 in loans putting two kids through\ncollege. He wants to lighten the load for others.\n<http://www.washingtonpost.com/blogs/post-politics/wp/2015/07/08/martin-omalley-racked-up-339200-in-loans-putting-two-kids-through-college-he-wants-to-lighten-the-load-for-others/>\n// WaPo // John Wagner \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nDemocratic presidential hopeful Martin O\xe2\x80\x99Malley plans Wednesday to put\nforward an ambitious five-year goal of allowing students to graduate\ndebt-free from public colleges and universities across the country.\n\n\n\nThe proposition is deeply personal for O\xe2\x80\x99Malley: Aides say he and his wife\nhave already incurred $339,200 in loans to put the two eldest of their four\nchildren through private universities. And college affordability was a\nleading priority for O\xe2\x80\x99Malley during his tenure as Maryland\xe2\x80\x99s governor.\n\n\n\nThe issue is one being talked about a lot these days by Democrats,\nincluding the party\xe2\x80\x99s other White House candidates, as more and more\nstudents enter the workforce with hefty debt loads.\n\n\n\nO\xe2\x80\x99Malley, who plans to detail his plan during a morning event in New\nHampshire, will call on states to freeze tuition rates at public colleges\nand universities  -- as Maryland did for four years -- and propose other\nmeasures that would help those carrying debt.\n\n\n\nUnder O\xe2\x80\x99Malley\xe2\x80\x99s plan, a copy of which was shared with The Washington Post,\nstudents and parents would be able to refinance their debt at lower\ninterest rates. And O\xe2\x80\x99Malley would base the repayment terms for student\nborrowers on their income upon graduation.\n\n\n\nFor the long term, O\xe2\x80\x99Malley says he would set a goal of limiting college\ntuition to 10 percent of a state\xe2\x80\x99s median income at four-year institutions\nand 5 percent at two-year institutions. Federal matching grants would help\nstates that participate in reaching the goal.\n\n\n\nUnder his plan, O\xe2\x80\x99Malley would also increase Pell Grants and revamp federal\nwork-study programs to help cover non-tuition costs, such as room and board.\n\n\n\nAides declined to spell out the cost of O\xe2\x80\x99Malley\xe2\x80\x99s initiatives but\nsuggested they could be paid for by measures such as closing corporate tax\nloopholes and taxing capital gains at the same rate as earned income.\n\n\n\nSen. Bernie Sanders (I-Vt.), who\xe2\x80\x99s emerged as the leading alternative for\nthe Democratic nomination to Hillary Rodham Clinton, has proposed a grander\nidea: making four-year public colleges and universities free. His plan,\nwhich he estimates would cost $70 billion a year, would be paid for in part\nby a tax on Wall Street transactions by investments houses, hedge funds and\nother speculators.\n\n\n\nClinton is also expected to detail college affordability plans in coming\nmonths.\n\n\n\nIn recent years, O\xe2\x80\x99Malley\xe2\x80\x99s daughter Grace, 24, graduated from Georgetown\nUniversity, and another daughter, Tara, 23, graduated from College of\nCharleston. Aides said O\xe2\x80\x99Malley and his wife, a district court judge in\nBaltimore, have taken out nine loans totaling $339,200 to help pay for the\neducation of their oldest two children. The interest rates range from just\nover 6 percent to 8.5 percent, an aide said.\n\n\n\nWhile some provisions in O\xe2\x80\x99Malley\xe2\x80\x99s plan would not affect private\nuniversities, O\xe2\x80\x99Malley aides said those schools would have an incentive to\nkeep costs down as public colleges and universities become more affordable.\n\n\n\nIn an e-mail sent to O\xe2\x80\x99Malley supporters on Tuesday, Grace O\xe2\x80\x99Malley, now a\npublic school teacher in Baltimore, relayed her college-tuition story and\nurged others to do so on a Web page set up by her father\xe2\x80\x99s campaign.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI had to make a tough choice: do I go to the college we can afford or do I\ntake out loans to go to the college of my dreams?\xe2\x80\x9d she wrote. \xe2\x80\x9cAt the age\nof 18, I made the decision to follow my dreams. My family and I now face\nyears of debt -- and we know we\'re not the only ones.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n*Martin O\'Malley Calls For Debt-Free College Within 5 Years*\n<http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2015/07/07/omalley-debt-free-college_n_7748504.html>*\n// HuffPo // Tyler Kingkade \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015*\n\nDemocratic presidential candidate Martin O\'Malley on Wednesday will lay out\na plan providing debt-free access to a college degree for all students\nwithin five years. The former Maryland governor also will propose\nincome-based repayment options for borrowers who have private student loans.\n\n\n\nO\'Malley will unveil his higher education plans during an event Wednesday\nmorning in Manchester, New Hampshire. He will seek to cut tuition "to no\nmore than 10 percent of state median income at four-year public\nuniversities," and encourage "competency-based education strategies" that\nallow students to graduate quicker, according to campaign briefing\ndocuments. To cut non-tuition costs, O\'Malley will propose expanding Pell\ngrants and tripling the work-study program so that at least 2 million\nstudents can participate.\n\n\n\nDebt-free college has already become a major issue in the Democratic\npresidential race, with endorsements of the idea from Sen. Bernie Sanders\n(I-Vt.) and former Secretary of State Hillary Clinton. The issue has\nsnowballed, thanks in part to a push by progressive activists, as student\ndebt tops $1.2 trillion.\n\n\n\nThe idea was outlined in a white paper by the left-leaning think tank\nProgressive Change Campaign Committee, and has steadily gained steam among\nDemocrats.\n\n\n\nDebt-free college "should be one of the top issues talked about on the\ncampaign trail, in debates, in TV ads, and at the doors with voters of all\nages," said Adam Green, Progressive Change Campaign Committee co-founder,\ninsisting that such a plan would be a boon for the economy.\n\n\n\nO\'Malley\'s plan builds on his previous statements and follows Sen.\nElizabeth Warren\'s (D-Mass.) framework for debt-free college.\n\n\n\nO\'Malley\'s daughter, Grace O\'Malley, sent an email to campaign supporters\nTuesday mentioning that her family chose to take out student loans to\nfinance college. O\'Malley\'s family has $339,200 worth of Parent Plus loans\nfor their two daughters\' college educations, campaign aides said.\n\n\n\nNew Hampshire has consistently ranked near the top for states with the most\nstudent debt.\n\n\n\nTo address current debt, O\'Malley will propose allowing borrowers with\nprivate student loans to enroll in income-based repayment plans. Details\naren\'t yet being released, but aides said borrowers would enroll in a\nprogram that would essentially have them paying the government rather than\nbanks.\n\n\n\nThe Obama administration has rolled out programs for federal student loans\nthat tie payments to borrowers\' income. But no similar benefit exists for\nprivate loans. As a result, private student loan borrowers\' monthly\npaymentscan top $1,000, and there\'s no loan forgiveness programs. Private\nstudent loans make up about one-eighth of all national education debt.\n\n\n\nO\'Malley will call on states to freeze tuition at state colleges and\nuniversities and to restore funding to higher education, which has been\nslashed for decades. He wants to encourage higher education funding with\nfederal grants in a process still being worked out.\n\n\n\n"The cost would vary depending on states\' levels of funding, but we have to\ntake the burden off students and their families and go back to historical\nlevels of investment in our public institutions of higher ed," campaign\nspokesman Sean Savett said Tuesday. "Governor O\'Malley is considering a\nnumber of possible ways to cover the cost including closing the trust fund\nand carried interest loopholes, taxing capital gains at the same rate as\nearned income, and closing tax loopholes for corporations that ship jobs\noverseas."\n\n\n\n*O\'Malley to Lay Out Plan for Debt-Free College\n<http://www.nytimes.com/aponline/2015/07/08/us/politics/ap-us-dem-2016-omalley.html>\n// AP // July 8, 2015*\n\n\n\nCONCORD, N.H. \xe2\x80\x94 Democrat Martin O\'Malley is calling the high cost of\ncollege a "crisis" as he lays out a goal of debt-free tuition for all\nstudents at public colleges and universities within five years if elected\npresident.\n\n\n\nO\'Malley, a former governor of Maryland, will outline his plan Wednesday at\nan event in the early-voting state of New Hampshire. O\'Malley is struggling\nto catch fire with Democratic voters who are preoccupied with rivals\nHillary Rodham Clinton and Vermont Sen. Bernie Sanders.\n\n\n\nFocusing on college costs could help him make inroads with younger voters\nin New Hampshire, where the average student loan debt burden is the highest\nin the nation. But he\'s not alone in addressing the problem. Sanders is\ncalling for free college tuition and has introduced legislation in the\nSenate to tax financial transactions to pay for it. Clinton has emphasized\nthe need to lower college costs but has yet to be specific on policy.\n\n\n\nRoughly a dozen voters will share their struggles with student debt in a\ndiscussion with O\'Malley before he outlines his debt-free college plan.\n\n\n\nO\'Malley\'s plan relies in part on using federal matching dollars to\nencourage states to pursue some of his more ambitious goals, such as\nfreezing tuition rates and eventually reducing tuition at four-year public\nschools to 10 percent of states\' median incomes.\n\n\n\nThe plan calls on states to invest more money in higher education and\nmaintain those levels even as tuition goes down. New Hampshire invests\nminimally in its public colleges and universities, and state aid for higher\neducation is often on the chopping block in tight state budgets.\n\n\n\nO\'Malley\'s plan includes familiar policy ideas, such as allowing students\nto refinance their loans and automatically enrolling people in income-based\nrepayment plans.\n\n\n\nHe is also proposing an increase in Pell Grants and a tripling of the\nnumber of work-study jobs to help students cover college costs beyond\ntuition, such as room and board.\n\n\n\n*Martin O\xe2\x80\x99Malley Has the Right Solution for Puerto Rico\xe2\x80\x99s Debt Crisis\n<http://www.thenation.com/article/martin-omalley-has-the-right-solution-for-puerto-ricos-debt-crisis/>\n// The Nation // John Nichols \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nPuerto Rico is not Greece.\n\n\n\nBut the United States commonwealth is confronted with a debt crisis. It\nfaces the threat of a brutal round of austerity cuts, which could make a\nbad circumstance dramatically worse. If ever there was a moment that called\nfor enlightened leadership that recognizes both the economic and social\nchallenges facing the Puerto Rico, this is it.\n\n\n\nFormer Maryland governor Martin O\xe2\x80\x99Malley heard that call as the crisis\nbegan to come into focus last month and declared, \xe2\x80\x9cAs a nation we must help\nour fellow US citizens not only because it\xe2\x80\x99s the right thing to do, but\nbecause our region\xe2\x80\x99s economic stability depends on it.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nUrging the Obama administration and Congress to act \xe2\x80\x9cto avoid Puerto Rico\xe2\x80\x99s\neconomic collapse,\xe2\x80\x9d O\xe2\x80\x99Malley said:\n\n\n\nFirst, Puerto Rico should be able to negotiate with its creditors just as\nstates can under the U.S. Bankruptcy code. Congress should approve Resident\nCommissioner Pedro Pierluisi\xe2\x80\x99s legislation that would allow for this to\nhappen.\n\n\n\nSecond, as I\xe2\x80\x99ve stated before, the Department of Health and Human Services\nmust end the inequitable treatment of Puerto Rico under Medicare, Medicaid\nand the Affordable Care Act. High costs and low reimbursement rates are a\nhuge burden to Puerto Rico\xe2\x80\x99s budget and millions of U.S. citizens are at\nrisk of losing care.\n\n\n\nThese are two steps we can take today, but I urge the Administration and\nCongress to work with Puerto Rico on a path forward that both provides\nimmediate relief, and builds a foundation for sustainable, long-term\neconomic stability.\n\n\n\nRepublican Jeb Bush, a longtime advocate for Puerto Rican statehood, has\nspoken out for some time about the need to provide the commonwealth with\ngreater flexibility. Give Bush credit for that, especially as it is likely\nto put him at odds with many in his own party.\n\n\n\nWhat distinguishes O\xe2\x80\x99Malley\xe2\x80\x99s early and steady focus on Puerto Rico\xe2\x80\x94and\nmore broadly on the Caribbean\xe2\x80\x94has been the precision he has brought to it\nas a former mayor and governor. That\xe2\x80\x99s earned him significant attention\nfrom Puerto Rican media and media in the United States that bothered to pay\nattention to the crisis.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cAs a nation we must help our fellow U.S. citizens not only because it\xe2\x80\x99s\nthe right thing to do, but because our region\xe2\x80\x99s economic stability depends\non it.\xe2\x80\x9d \xe2\x80\x94 Martin O\xe2\x80\x99Malley\n\nNow, the crisis is back in the news.\n\n\n\nAfter lawyers for Puerto Rico failed on Tuesday to get the US Court of\nAppeals in Boston to reinstate a local law to help the commonwealth\nrestructure a crushing $72 billion debt burden, other candidates picked up\non the call, and they deserve credit for this.\n\n\n\nFormer Secretary of State Hillary Clinton said, \xe2\x80\x9cThe people of Puerto Rico\nare hurting right now under a weak economy that has been struggling for\nyears.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nClinton, who had expressed concern about Puerto Rico\xe2\x80\x99s circumstance\nearlier, provided more details, saying, \xe2\x80\x9cAs a first step, Congress should\nprovide Puerto Rico the same authority that states already have to enable\nseverely distressed government entities, including municipalities and\npublic corporations, to restructure their debts under Chapter 9 of the\nBankruptcy Code.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nLater in the day, Senator Bernie Sanders said, \xe2\x80\x9cI strongly believe Puerto\nRico should be afforded the same bankruptcy protections that exist for\nmunicipalities across the United States. We need to do everything we can to\nallow Puerto Rico to restructure its debt in a rational way that does not\nharm its people, ordinary investors or pension funds in the United States.\nChapter 9 protections would be a good first step.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nSanders added that \xe2\x80\x9cwe also should recognize that the reason Puerto Rico\nhas such unsustainable debt has everything to do with the policies of\nausterity and the greed of large financial institutions. Puerto Rico has\nbeen in a severe recession for almost a decade. Today, more than 45 percent\nof the people in Puerto Rico are living in poverty, the childhood poverty\nrate is greater than 56 percent and real unemployment is much too high. Our\ngoal must be not only to give Puerto Rico the flexibility it needs to\nrestructure its debt, but to make sure that it can rebuild its economy,\ncreate good-paying jobs and expand its tax base.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nThe right things are being said now. The volume is being amplified.\n\n\n\nWhen the call for a reasonable response was faint, however, O\xe2\x80\x99Malley was\nthe one who stepped up. And he framed a message that was humane and\nresponsible.\n\n\n\nThis is worth noting, because Puerto Rico\xe2\x80\x99s challenge is both fiscal and\npolitical. Political players in Washington have to be pushed to pay more\nattention to the island that is part of the United States but not a state.\nAs a commonwealth, Puerto Rico has a unique relationship with the United\nStates that creates both benefits and challenges. This has been especially\nevident as Puerto Rican officials have looked for options to restructure a\ndebt-repayment burden so overwhelming that it threatens to empty the\ncommonwealth\xe2\x80\x99s treasury, to cause profound hardship for island residents,\nand to leave officials with few options for renewing a battered economy.\n\n\n\nWhile states and mainland cities have the varying degrees of flexibility to\nrestructure debt burdens of the sort that Puerto Rico is facing, the island\nlacks them. At virtually every turn, Puerto Rican officials are prevented\nfrom taking steps that have the potential to stabilize its fiscal affairs\nwhile maintaining basic services\xe2\x80\x94the only rational and humane response to\nthe crisis caused by its inability to cover payments to bondholders who\ndelighted in speculating on financial instruments issued by the\ncommonwealth because the bonds had \xe2\x80\x9ctriple-tax-free\xe2\x80\x9d status that exempted\nthem from federal, state, and local income taxes.\n\n\n\nThere will be much resistance in Washington to doing right by Puerto Rico.\nIt is going to take consistent leadership to get the attention and the\naction that is necessary to get an equitable restructuring of debts. This\npolitical pressure is going to require both economic common sense and a\nsense of morality that recognizes that helping our fellow citizens is \xe2\x80\x9cthe\nright thing to do.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nO\xe2\x80\x99Malley has been out front on this one, applying the pressure. He deserves\ncredit for that, and encouragement to keep it up.\n\n\n\n*Martin O\xe2\x80\x99Malley: A Strong Foreign Policy Starts With a Global Middle Class\n<http://time.com/3947720/martin-omalley-foreign-policy-middle-class/> //\nTIME // Martin O\xe2\x80\x99Malley \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nI believe America\xe2\x80\x99s role in the world is to advance the cause of a global\nmiddle class.\n\n\n\nAfter more than 12 years on the battlefields of Iraq and Afghanistan, and\nafter a global financial crisis that decimated our middle class, it is\nunderstandable that many Americans would like to disengage from the world.\nBut our country\xe2\x80\x99s security and prosperity demand that we be more engaged in\nthe world, not less.\n\n\n\nThe first and foremost responsibility of the next Commander in Chief will\nbe to keep America safe from 21st-century threats: violent extremism;\nnuclear proliferation; pandemics; cyberattacks; rising inequality; failed\nstates; the mega-droughts, famines and floods caused by climate change; and\nmore refugees than at any time since World War II.\n\n\n\nWe may have the most sophisticated military in history, but we do not have\na silver bullet for these problems. So we must pursue a more collaborative,\nproactive, and farsighted foreign policy. We need new international\npartnerships to confront climate change and regional challenges, from the\nSouth China Sea to the sea lanes of the Middle East. We must create a new\nNational Security Act to develop a broader framework for our\nnational-security strategy. We must continue to adapt our military\xe2\x80\x99s force\nstructure and spending to meet today\xe2\x80\x99s threats. And we must establish a\ncybersecurity unit in every state\xe2\x80\x99s National Guard to better protect\nAmericans\xe2\x80\x99 personal data and critical infrastructure.\n\n\n\nMy vision for U.S. foreign policy focuses on the rise of a global middle\nclass, which is a moral, economic, and national-security imperative.\nEliminating the scourge of extreme poverty is a reflection of our most\ndeeply held values. Supporting economic development will help us build the\nnext generation of American political and economic partnerships. And\nprotecting the dignity of human lives in fragile states will reduce the\nthreat of being drawn into costly future conflicts.\n\n\n\nWe must also understand that comprehensive immigration reform is an\neconomic and national-security interest. And we must forge a New Alliance\nfor Progress based on shared interests in our own hemisphere, which we have\nneglected for too long. An early task should be to address the root causes\nof violence and instability in places like El Salvador and Honduras,\nheading off growing crises before they reach our borders.\n\n\n\nWe must listen to U.S. military leaders who have long recognized that\nclimate change is a national security threat. Tackling the climate\nchallenge will provide our nation the greatest business opportunity in 100\nyears. I strongly support an American Green Jobs Agenda. If we can put a\nman on the moon in a decade, we can power America with 100% renewable\nenergy by 2050. It\xe2\x80\x99s not the technology that\xe2\x80\x99s lacking. It\xe2\x80\x99s the political\nwill.\n\n\n\nAll of this is within our reach. But it will require new leadership.\nTwitter and Facebook are no substitute for personal relationships and human\nintelligence. We must recruit a new generation of Americans to exercise our\nglobal economic, diplomatic, military, and healing power in ways consistent\nwith our values. And we must give them the tools to engage a new generation\nof leaders abroad, often in hostile environments where we lack historic\nties.\n\n\n\nThe cornerstone of American strength in the world is economic strength at\nhome. Maintaining our security in the long run will require an economy that\nworks for all Americans. No fighter jet or troop battalion will protect us\nas much as a vibrant economy. A stronger middle class is the first garrison\nagainst any threat we might face.\n\n\n\nThe greatest power we possess as Americans is not military might, but the\npower of our own example. We must lead the world by strengthening the\nAmerican middle class and supporting the rise of a global middle class \xe2\x80\x94\nfree from want, and free from fear.\n\n\n\nThat will make us more prosperous and secure. That will give our children a\nbetter future with more opportunity. And that will make our planet\nhealthier, more peaceful, and more just.\n\n\n\nThese are the foreign policy and national security goals worthy of a truly\ngreat people.\n\n\n\n*O\'Malley Denounces Super PACs As One Supporting Him Goes After Sanders\n<http://nhpr.org/post/omalley-denounces-super-pacs-one-supporting-him-goes-after-sanders>\n// NHPR // Rachael Brindley \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nFormer Maryland Gov. Martin O\'Malley says he\'d prefer there were no super\nPACs, but stopped short of calling on one supporting him to stop airing\nnegative attack ads against Democratic rival Vermont Sen. Bernie Sanders.\n\n\n\n"I would hope that we would keep this debate a debate about the issues and\nI would prefer, not that I\'m able to tell a super PAC what to do, I would\nprefer that we didn\'t have any super PACs, frankly," he said.\n\n\n\nIn an interview with NHPR\'s Morning Edition, O\'Malley was responding to\nattack ads being aired by the Generation Forward PAC, which has been\ncritical of Sanders for not being progressive enough when it comes to gun\ncontrol.\n\n\n\nO\'Malley didn\'t say whether he supported or denounced the ads, only that he\ndisagreed with the Citizens United decision, saying that once you\'re a\ncandidate, "you\'re in a bit of a straight jacket. There are all sorts of\nrules and limitations, but super PACs have none."\n\n\n\nO\'Malley is scheduled to return to New Hampshire this week, as polls show\nhe\'s got a lot of ground to make up to catch Sanders and former Secretary\nof State Hillary Clinton. A recent poll showed O\'Malley with just 2 percent\nof support among Democratic voters.\n\n\n\nO\'Malley has acknowledged Sanders\' recent surge in the polls, but\nattributes that to him being a "protest candidate." When asked what he\nmeant by that, O\'Malley said," History has shown usually the candidates\nthat are surging in the summer are not the candidates who are surging in\nthe primary."\n\n\n\n"I\'m running for President of the United States, and I have 15 years of\nexecutive experience, getting things done," he said. "I have to offer\nprogressive values as well as an ability to actually deliver on the goals\nset, whether it\'s affordable college, reducing violent crime, increasing\njob creation, or defending the highest median income in the country through\na recession."\n\n\n\n*SANDERS*\n\n\n\n*Can Bernie Sanders Beat Hillary Clinton? Reporter\xe2\x80\x99s Notebook\n<http://www.nytimes.com/times-insider/2015/07/07/can-bernie-sanders-beat-hillary-clinton-reporters-notebook/>\n// NYT // Pat Leary \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nDeep down, does Bernie Sanders actually believe he can beat Hillary Rodham\nClinton for the 2016 Democratic presidential nomination?\n\n\n\nAfter watching and interviewing him over the last several weeks, it\xe2\x80\x99s clear\nthat the Vermont senator thinks he could win, yet also knows that it will\ntake the political equivalent of lightning in a bottle.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s one thing for people to say that the country is going in the wrong\ndirection, that we need to change directions,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Sanders told me\nrecently. \xe2\x80\x9cBut is there the energy to get seriously involved in the\ncampaign? Can the thousands of people coming to our events be turned into a\nreal political organization? Will the people showing up this summer also\nshow up to vote for our message next winter in the primaries?\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nPeople may be surprised to learn that Mr. Sanders isn\xe2\x80\x99t some starry-eyed\npolitical fantasist, despite his socialist leanings and visions of moving\nAmerica closer to a welfare-state system like those of Denmark and Sweden,\nwhich he praises as models of fair-minded government on the campaign trail.\n\n\n\nAfter more than 30 years as an elected official, he is shrewd enough to\nknow that the huge crowds he is drawing (including 7,000 people in\nPortland, Me., on Monday night) won\xe2\x80\x99t mean much if they don\xe2\x80\x99t support his\ncandidacy in the way that matters, by rallying support from friends and\nacquaintances, and, of course, voting for him when the time comes.\n\n\n\nOne of the problems for Mr. Sanders is that his political organization is\nstill relatively tiny (a few dozen paid staff members at this point,\ncompared to hundreds for Mrs. Clinton) and can only grow so fast. And it is\nnot growing as fast as the crowds showing up at his campaign events.\n\n\n\nWhy does that matter? Like another presidential candidate from Vermont,\nHoward Dean, in 2003, Mr. Sanders is using the summer before the primaries\nto build political momentum by holding events in reliably liberal enclaves\nwhere thousands of voters are flocking to his message, and the news media\nis spotlighting the big turnout.\n\n\n\nBut Mr. Sanders doesn\xe2\x80\x99t have big teams of campaign staff on the ground in\nPortland, Madison, Wis., Minneapolis and elsewhere who can perform\nlabor-intensive follow-up with virtually every voter who attended his\nrallies. That kind of outreach is a specialty of Mrs. Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s army of\norganizers and volunteers.\n\n\n\nGive us time, say Sanders advisers, who are at this point focusing manpower\nand money on the two early-voting states, Iowa and New Hampshire.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe have an incredibly great message, and a messenger that people are\nexcited about,\xe2\x80\x9d said Pete D\xe2\x80\x99Alessandro, who is overseeing the Sanders\ncampaign in Iowa. \xe2\x80\x9cBut the key is the extent to which we can turn a\ngrass-roots campaign into a winning campaign.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nFor Mr. Sanders to win the Iowa caucuses, which some Clinton allies and\nadvisers now see as a real possibility, his organization and the savvy,\nexperienced operatives running it will have to scale up substantially.\n\n\n\nIn the end, of course, there remains the threshold question: Do Americans\nhunger for radical change intensely enough, and in big enough numbers, to\ndefeat a popular, well-financed Democrat who is widely considered more\nmainstream and electable than Mr. Sanders?\n\n\n\n*Why we shouldn\xe2\x80\x99t just call Bernie Sanders a \xe2\x80\x98liberal\xe2\x80\x99\n<http://www.washingtonpost.com/blogs/the-fix/wp/2015/07/07/why-we-shouldnt-call-bernie-sanders-a-liberal/>\n// WaPo // Hunter Schwartz \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015*\n\n\n\nDemocratic presidential candidate Bernie Sanders is some progressives\'\ngreat hope to defeat Hillary Clinton in 2016. But to say he\'s a\ndown-the-line liberal would be to misread a political career the includes\nplenty of nuance.\n\n\n\nOver the weekend, Sanders spoke on gun control and the tax-exempt status of\nchurches, and if you were hearing him for the first time, you might think\nhe was a Republican. He defended gun owners on CNN\'s "State of the Union,"\nsaying 99.9 percent of them obey the law and that gun manufacturers\nshouldn\'t be held responsible for murderers "any more than you would hold a\nhammer company responsible if somebody beats somebody over the head with a\nhammer."\n\n\n\nOn removing the tax-exempt status for churches that don\'t recognize\nsame-sex marriage, he said he didn\'t know that he\'d "go there" and that he\nrespected "people who have different points of view."\n\n\n\nOf course, neither of these positions necessarily run counter to the\nDemocratic Party\'s principles -- Hillary Clinton isn\'t going after\nlaw-abiding gun owners, and Martin O\'Malley isn\'t campaigning on taking\naway churches\' tax-exempt status -- and Sanders\'s comments came in the\ncontext of his liberal bona fides, which he also mentioned. For example, he\nhas voted to ban semiautomatic assault weapons and create instant\nbackground checks, and he voted against the Defense of Marriage Act, which\nwas signed into law in 1996 by Democratic President Bill Clinton.\n\n\n\nBut there are certain things that might complicate Sanders for those on the\nleft -- and it wasn\'t just this weekend, either. In 1993, as a member of\nthe House, he voted against the Brady bill, which required federal\nbackground checks for most gun purchases. He also voted to allow people to\ntransport guns on Amtrak, and he previously said he didn\'t think stricter\ngun control would end mass shootings. (Sanders\'s home state of Vermont,\nwhile generally quite liberal, is also very pro-gun rights.)\n\n\n\nHis history with immigration reform is similar, with a mixed record of\nsupporting things like the Dream Act and the 2013 bill, but in 2007 helping\nto kill that comprehensive immigration reform deal by teaming with\nconservative Republican Sen. Charles Grassley (Iowa) on so-called "poison\npill" amendments. Other Democrats opposed the final bill, as Sanders did,\nbut almost all who did so came from the more moderate wing of the party.\n\n\n\nSanders might just become some GOP-leaning voters\' favorite 2016 Democrat\n-- and not just because he\'s giving Hillary Clinton a tough time. It\'s not\nhard to see some of his positions appealing to more libertarian voters like\nformer Ron Paul fans who prefer Sanders over Rand Paul. His arguments for a\nmiddle ground on some of our most controversial social issues also could\nappeal to voters frustrated by hyper-partisan politics.\n\n\n\nHe has surprised even himself with the turnout he\'s getting at some early\ncampaign events. The more than 2,500 people who showed up to a Friday rally\nin Iowa were part of the largest crowd for any candidate in Iowa this\ncycle. But he\'s not just spending all his time in Iowa or New Hampshire.\nSanders has had rallies in Colorado and Wisconsin, and he told The Nation\nthat he believes candidates should have a 50-state campaign strategy,\nrattling off red states he thinks Democrats, as "the party of working\npeople," should campaign in, including Mississippi, South Carolina and\nAlabama. On Monday, he drew 7,500 people closer to home in Portland, Maine.\n\n\n\nSanders is a socialist who championed progressive issues before they became\nmore mainstream, but it\'s also clear that he\'s an independent and not a\nDemocrat for a reason. He\'s beloved by liberal Democrats who feel Clinton\nis too moderate, but as his vision for a 50-state campaign and gun and\ntax-exempt comments show, he\'s making a play for people who might not\ndescribe themselves as "very liberal."\n\n\n\n*The issue on which Bernie Sanders aims for \xe2\x80\x98the middle\xe2\x80\x99\n<http://www.msnbc.com/rachel-maddow-show/the-issue-which-bernie-sanders-aims-the-middle>\n// MSNBC // Steve Benen \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nOne of the biggest political stories of the summer is the reception Sen.\nBernie Sanders is receiving on the presidential campaign trail. In a 2016\nfield filled with high-profile candidates, it\xe2\x80\x99s the Vermont Independent\nwho\xe2\x80\x99s drawing the largest crowds.\n\nThis was evident yesterday in Maine, which came on the heels of similarly\nsuccessful events in Iowa and Wisconsin last week. As Rachel noted on the\nshow last night, Sanders is \xe2\x80\x9chaving way more retail success on the campaign\ntrail than anyone else in either party \xe2\x80\x93 anyone.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\nSanders\xe2\x80\x99 early success seems baffling to much of the political world, but\nlet this be a lesson to observers: there are plenty of unapologetic\nliberals out there who are eager to celebrate Sanders and his vision.\n\nBut just away from the spotlight, there\xe2\x80\x99s still just one potential trouble\narea for the Vermonter. A few readers flagged this Facebook item yesterday\nfrom the Coalition to Stop Gun Violence, which wasn\xe2\x80\x99t pleased with comments\nSanders made in an interview on Sunday with CNN\xe2\x80\x99s Jake Tapper:\n\n\n\nU.S. Senator Bernie Sanders\xe2\x80\x99 characterization here of the National Rifle\nAssociation-drafted \xe2\x80\x9cProtection of Lawful Commerce in Arms Act\xe2\x80\x9d that he\nvoted for in 2005 is an utter fabrication. The bill has nothing to do with\nprotecting upstanding gun manufacturers and dealers. Instead, it gives\nNEGLIGENT manufacturers and dealers blanket immunity from civil lawsuits.\nThis law is THE REASON why two parents who lost their daughter in the\nAurora shooting had their suit thrown out and are now being ordered to pay\nmore than $200,000 in legal fees to gun companies that armed James Holmes.\n\nIt is an immoral law that denies victims and survivors their day in court \xe2\x80\x93\na fundamental democratic right \xe2\x80\x93 and Sanders\xe2\x80\x99 position is totally\nunacceptable. A big thanks to Jake Tapper for holding him accountable.\n\n\n\nSanders hasn\xe2\x80\x99t taken much heat from the left since launching his campaign,\nso it\xe2\x80\x99s worth pausing to appreciate what this is all about.\n\nIn the CNN interview, Tapper asked Sanders, \xe2\x80\x9cEarlier this year, the parents\nof one of the 12 innocent people killed during the Aurora movie theater\nshooting, they saw their lawsuit to hold ammunition sellers liable for the\nattack, they saw that dismissed. And one of the reasons was a law that you\nvoted for which protects manufacturers of firearms and ammunition from\nbeing sued. Why did you vote that way?\xe2\x80\x9d\n\nSanders stressed that the NRA is not a fan of his \xe2\x80\x93 he\xe2\x80\x99s voted, for\nexample, to close the gun-show loophole and in support of instant\nbackground checks \xe2\x80\x93 before explaining:\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cNow, the issues that you\xe2\x80\x99re talking about is, if somebody has a gun and it\nfalls into the hands of a murderer, and that murderer kills somebody with\nthe gun, do you hold the gun manufacturer responsible? Not anymore than you\nwould hold a hammer company responsible if somebody beat somebody over the\nhead with a hammer. That is not what a lawsuit should be about.\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd this is part, by the way, I may say, of \xe2\x80\x93 you know, folks who do not\nlike guns is fine, but we have millions of people who are gun owners in\nthis country; 99.9 percent of those people obey the law. I want to see real\nserious debate and action on guns. But it is not going to take place if we\nsimply have extreme positions on both sides. I think I can bring us to the\nmiddle.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nIt was this response that did not go over well with the Coalition to Stop\nGun Violence. The litigation strategy against gun manufacturers is an\nimportant idea for many gun-safety advocates, and Sanders seemed to dismiss\nthe idea as ridiculous.\n\nOverall, I\xe2\x80\x99m generally skeptical that gun policy represents a real threat\nto Sanders\xe2\x80\x99 support from the left. The senator\xe2\x80\x99s platform largely focuses\non economics, not social issues, and my hunch is that if someone were to\ntell the thousands of voters showing up for Sanders\xe2\x80\x99 events that he\xe2\x80\x99s a\nmoderate on guns, the vast majority wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t care.\n\nBut it\xe2\x80\x99s nevertheless a rare instance in which Sanders breaks with\nprogressive orthodoxy, and it\xe2\x80\x99s an issue on which Hillary Clinton is\nsquarely to the senator\xe2\x80\x99s left \xe2\x80\x93 a detail that Democratic voters may be\nhearing more about in the coming months.\n\n* Update: In the statement from the Coalition to Stop Gun Violence, the\ngroup notes that two parents who lost their daughter in the Aurora shooting\n\xe2\x80\x9care now being ordered to pay more than $200,000 in legal fees to gun\ncompanies.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\nA colleague reminds me, however, that this is not entirely correct \xe2\x80\x93 the\nparents have been ordered to pay \xe2\x80\x9creasonable\xe2\x80\x9d damages, and the $200,000\nfigure is the one the company has requested. The judge, however, has not\nyet set the actual amount, and as of now, the parents in the case haven\xe2\x80\x99t\nbeen ordered to pay anything.\n\n\n\n*Bernie Sanders is no Ron Paul: What the press gets all wrong about the\nVermont senator\n<http://www.salon.com/2015/07/08/bernie_sanders_is_no_ron_paul_what_even_the_left_gets_wrong_about_the_vermont_senator_partner/>*\n\n*He\'ll always be an underdog, but Sanders is a more viable candidate than\neven the left-wing media will acknowledge*\n<http://www.salon.com/2015/07/08/bernie_sanders_is_no_ron_paul_what_even_the_left_gets_wrong_about_the_vermont_senator_partner/>*\n// Salon // Zaid Jilani \xe2\x80\x93 July 8, 2015*\n\n\n\nAlterNet Monday night, Bernie Sanders drew 7,500 people in the town of\nPortland, Maine, a locale that only has a population of 66,000. The\nPortland rally was the latest in a series of high turnouts, as Sanders is\ndrawing more Americans to his events than any other candidate in either\nparty.\n\n\n\nIn response to the high turnouts at Sanders\xe2\x80\x99s events, many in the media\nhave sought to downplay his momentum by comparing him to former GOP\npresidential candidate Ron Paul, who also inspired an enthusiastic\nfollowing:\n\n\n\nThe message these outlets are promoting is that Sanders, like Paul, will be\nable to get an enthusiastic base but will ultimately fail in his quest for\nthe presidency and will only make only a minor impact on the debate. The\nimplication seems to be that Sanders\xe2\x80\x99 views are on the fringe, like Ron\nPaul\xe2\x80\x99s. But are they? Or is it just that he is the only one articulating\nthe need to address extreme inequality and expanding social security, which\nmillions of Americans support?\n\n\n\nThe media message seems to rely on the idea that the two men are similar\nbecause they spark genuine enthusiasm among their supporters \xe2\x80\x93 which is\nperhaps a sad commentary on American politics that there are so few\ncandidates who can do this that when they do they are instantly compared.\n\n\n\nBut the analogy doesn\xe2\x80\x99t really hold beyond that. In 2008, when Paul first\nran for the presidency, he had 130,000 donors through the fourth quarter\n(January 2008). Recall that this was a campaign that began very early, with\nPaul entering the race on an official basis in March 2007 after forming his\npresidential exploration committee in January of that year.\n\n\n\nSanders, on the other hand, has already collected 250,000 donors after\naround two months of campaigning. This means that the Vermont Senator is\ncollecting donors at nearly 8 times the rate that Paul did in his first run\nfor the presidency.\n\n\n\nThe biggest difference between the two is the ceiling of support they were\nable to hit. Paul, despite his enthusiastic and genuinely creative\nvolunteer and donor base, has advocated ideas like completely eliminating\nMedicare, Social Security, and Medicaid. Even among the GOP base, these\nideas are extremely unpopular.\n\n\n\nSanders, on the other hand, has since his time as Burlington, Vermont\xe2\x80\x99s\nmayor, promoted ideas that are mainstream and popular. Even in the House of\nRepresentatives between 1994 and 2006, one of the most right-wing\nlegislative bodies in American history, it was Sanders who passed the most\namendments of any member of Congress.\n\n\n\nThere is no doubt that he\xe2\x80\x99s an underdog, but Sanders\xe2\x80\x99s ideas are popular\nand he is gaining traction at a far quicker rate than Ron Paul did. It\xe2\x80\x99s\ntrue that both Paul and Sanders were insurgent candidates who drew\nenthusiastic supporters. The similarities end there.\n\n\n\n*Bernie Sanders\xe2\x80\x99 Plan To Make Solar Power More Accessible\n<http://thinkprogress.org/climate/2015/07/07/3677745/bernie-sanders-introduces-solar-legislation/>\n// Think Progress // Ari Phillips \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015*\n\n\n\nOn Tuesday, Vermont Senator and 2016 Democratic presidential candidate\nBernie Sanders introduced legislation aimed at making it easier for\nlow-income families to take advantage of solar power. The bill, called the\n\xe2\x80\x9cLow Income Solar Act,\xe2\x80\x9d came the same day that the Obama Administration\nannounced a similar program aimed at installing 300 megawatts of renewable\nenergy in federally subsidized housing by 2020.\n\n\n\nThe Sanders bill would aid in this effort by providing $200 million in\nDepartment of Energy loans and grants to help offset the upfront costs\nassociated with installing solar panels on community facilities, public\nhousing and low-income family homes, according to a press release. The\nprojects would also have to prioritize loans for female- and minority-owned\nbusinesses, as well as target specific regions including Appalachia, Indian\ntribal lands, and Alaskan native communities.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe scientific community tells us very clearly if we\xe2\x80\x99re going to reverse\nclimate change and the great dangers it poses for the planet we must move\naggressively to transform our energy system away from fossil fuels to\nsustainable energy,\xe2\x80\x9d Sanders said in a statement. \xe2\x80\x9cWe can achieve this\ngoal, save families money and protect the planet for future generations.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nAccording to the bill summary, homeowners with suitable roofs would receive\ngrants to help them afford solar panel installation while renters or others\nwithout appropriate siting options would get connected through alternative\nmeans such as community solar gardens. Solar gardens are designed for those\nwithout rooftop access as a way to connect to a shared solar system that\nguarantees their electricity comes from solar power.\n\nUsually these community solar gardens are one or two megawatts in size and\noperated by third-party solar providers and local utilities.\n\n\n\nEnvironmentalists are pleased that Sanders is running for president, as he\nis one of the climate change action leaders in the Senate.\n\n\n\nEnvironmental activist and founder of 350.org Bill McKibben recently\npraised Sanders as \xe2\x80\x9cthe ultimate what-you-see-is-what-you-get politician.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cBernie\xe2\x80\x99s been in the forefront of all the crucial environmental fights of\nrecent years, always willing to knuckle down and do the hard work of\nfighting the big corporations,\xe2\x80\x9d McKibben told the Burlington Free Press.\n\n\n\nAs ThinkProgress previously reported, after the 2014 election that put the\nGOP in charge of the Senate, Sanders pushed the chamber to go on the record\nas to whether climate change is happening, caused by human activity, and\nresulting in \xe2\x80\x9cdevastating problems in the United States and around the\nworld.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nIn 2015 he attended the People\xe2\x80\x99s Climate March in New York City and told\nDemocracy Now! that climate change is \xe2\x80\x9ca huge issue. It\xe2\x80\x99s a planetary\ncrisis. We\xe2\x80\x99ve got to act, and we have to act boldly.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nHe has also consistently opposed the Keystone XL pipeline and has talked\npublicly about the potentially disastrous environmental effects.\n\n\n\nWhile Sanders entered the race an extreme long shot, his popularity has\nswelled in the early days of the campaign. On a recent visit to Iowa, one\nof the early caucus states, Sanders drew big crowds as well as the\nattention of Democratic frontrunner Hillary Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s campaign. Sanders is\ngaining major traction in Iowa polling, and has surpassed Clinton among\nvery liberal voters.\n\n\n\n*Jimmy Carter: Bernie Sanders Is A \'Surprising\' Democratic Competitor\n<http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2015/07/07/jimmy-carter-bernie-sanders_n_7745548.html>\n// HuffPo // Paige Lavender \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nFormer President Jimmy Carter spoke with HuffPost Live about Sen. Fresh off news that\nSanders is now virtually tied with Hillary in New Hampshire, Claire\nMcCaskill went on Morning Joe on June 25 to declare that \xe2\x80\x9cthe media is\ngiving Bernie a pass \xe2\x80\xa6 they\xe2\x80\x99re not giving the same scrutiny to Bernie that\nthey\xe2\x80\x99re certainly giving to Hillary.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nThe irony here is thick. In their book\nHRC, Aimee Parnes and Jonathan Allen write that, \xe2\x80\x9c\xe2\x80\x98Hate\xe2\x80\x99 is too weak a word\nto describe the feelings that Hillary\xe2\x80\x99s core loyalists still have for\nMcCaskill.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nMcCaskill, in other words, is a great surrogate: someone eager enough to\nregain the Clintons\xe2\x80\x99 affection that she\xe2\x80\x99ll not only praise Hillary, but\nalso slam their opponents. On Morning Joe, she had two talking points.\nFirst, journalists are giving Sanders a pass. Second, Sanders is a\nsocialist, and thus can\xe2\x80\x99t win. Asked about Sanders\xe2\x80\x99 large crowds, McCaskill\ncompared him to Ron Paul and Pat Buchanan, other candidates who sparked\nenthusiasm among their supporters but couldn\xe2\x80\x99t win a general election\nbecause of their \xe2\x80\x9cextreme message.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nOn point number one, McCaskill is undeniably correct: Media coverage of\nSanders has been fawning, partly because many journalists harbor sympathy\nfor his anti-corporate message but mostly because they\xe2\x80\x99re desperate for a\ncontested primary. Given Sanders\xe2\x80\x99s strong poll numbers, the media would\neventually have gotten around to tearing down the man they pumped up. But\nTeam Clinton clearly wants to accelerate this process before Sanders gets\nany more momentum.\n\n\n\nMore intriguing is point number two. Sanders probably would be a\nproblematic general-election candidate. But the liberals flocking to his\nside don\xe2\x80\x99t much care. Nor are the Clintonites likely to scare off many\nliberals by reminding them that Sanders is a socialist. Most of them\nalready know. And far from hiding it, Sanders is quite effective when\nchallenged on this point. Right after he jumped in the race, George\nStephanopoulos gave Sanders exactly the treatment McCaskill is calling for\nnow. First, he reminded Sanders he was a socialist. Then, when Sanders\npointed to Scandinavia as his socialist model, Stephanopoulos snarked that,\n\xe2\x80\x9cI can hear the Republican attack ad right now: He wants America to be look\nmore like Scandinavia.\xe2\x80\x9d But Sanders was not cowed. \xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s right. What\xe2\x80\x99s wrong when they have a stronger\nmiddle class in many ways than we do?\xe2\x80\x9d It was the kind of performance more\nlikely to leave liberals inspired than alienated.\n\n\n\nMcCaskill grew even less effective when Mark Halperin did something TV\ninterviewers too rarely do: He demanded substance. Give \xe2\x80\x9cthree specific\npositions\xe2\x80\x9d of Sanders that \xe2\x80\x9care too far left,\xe2\x80\x9d he insisted. \xe2\x80\x9cI am not here\nto be critical of my colleague Senator Sanders,\xe2\x80\x9d McCaskill responded,\nabsurdly. But Halperin caught her, noting that, \xe2\x80\x9cWith all due respect, you\nalready were: You said he was socialist and not electable.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nThen things got interesting. The specifics McCaskill offered were that\nSanders \xe2\x80\x9cwould like to see Medicare for all in this country, have everybody\nhave a government-insurance policy,\xe2\x80\x9d that \xe2\x80\x9che would like to see expansion\nof entitlement,\xe2\x80\x9d and that \xe2\x80\x9che is someone who is frankly against trade.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nIf Hillary actually goes after Sanders on these specifics, the Democratic\nrace will get very interesting very fast. A debate about Obamacare versus\nsingle-payer health insurance, about expanding Social Security versus\nrestraining its growth, and about the merits of free trade would be\nfascinating. But I doubt it\xe2\x80\x99s a debate Hillary wants to have. She is, after\nall, running a campaign based on generating enthusiasm among the party\xe2\x80\x99s\nliberal core. By taking bold, left-leaning positions on immigration,\ncriminal justice, and campaign-finance reform, she\xe2\x80\x99s trying (and so far\nsucceeding) to erase her reputation from 2008 as a timid triangulator\nunwilling to offer big change. Yet the more Hillary emphasizes her\nopposition to single-payer health care, her opposition to expanding Social\nSecurity, and her support for free trade, the more she undermines her own\nstrategy. By taking on Sanders on these issues, Hillary also implicitly\ntakes on Elizabeth Warren, who has made expanding Social Security and\nopposing the Trans-Pacific Partnership two of her recent crusades.\n\n\n\nThe irony is that in 2008, when Hillary was trying to distinguish herself\nfrom her party\xe2\x80\x99s left base in order to appeal to general-election\nmoderates, an opponent like Bernie Sanders might have seemed like a\nblessing. In 2016, by contrast, when Hillary is running to the left,\nattacking him as too far left is dangerous.\n\n\n\nNo wonder McCaskill wants journalists to bury the curmudgeonly Vermonter.\nThe Hillary campaign knows how tricky it will be to bury him themselves.\n\n\n\n*This Could Be Bernie Sanders\' Biggest General Election Challenge\n<http://www.nbcnews.com/politics/2016-election/could-be-bernie-sanders-biggest-general-election-challenge-n388071>\n// NBC News // Mark Murray \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nIt\'s been the Summer of Bernie Sanders.\n\n\n\nThousands are turning out at his campaign events, his poll numbers are\nskyrocketing and the New York Times is now raising the question: What if\nBernie Sanders wins Iowa?\n\n\n\nBut here\'s a different question: Can he win a general election?\n\n\n\nWhile no national poll has yet to test Sanders in a trial heat against the\nRepublican field, a June 2015 Gallup poll found that being a self-described\nsocialist -- as Sanders is -- is more unpopular for a presidential\ncandidate than being an evangelical Christian, Muslim or atheist.\n\n\n\nAccording to the poll, 50 percent said they wouldn\'t vote for a socialist,\ncompared with 40 percent who wouldn\'t vote for an atheist, 38 percent for a\nMuslim and 25 percent for an evangelical Christian.\n\n\n\n\n\n"Bernie is too liberal to gather enough votes in this country to become\npresident," Sen. He drew crowds of thousands at several rallies in the\nlast week, a notable feat 16 months before a general election. His poll\nnumbers in the key early states of Iowa and New Hampshire show he is just a\nfew paces behind Hillary Clinton, climbing within ten points of the\npresumptive Democratic nominee in one recent poll. And more than 250,000\npeople have donated to his campaign.\n\n\n\nThey are surprising metrics of success for a politician who for decades has\nseen himself as an outsider.\n\n\n\nSanders, who calls himself a democratic socialist, has done it armed with\nthe promise of revolution. \xe2\x80\x9cThe only way that change takes place is when we\ndevelop that strong grassroots movement, make that political revolution,\nstand together,\xe2\x80\x9d Sanders said on Monday. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd then we bring about change.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nSanders had originally planned his Monday night rally in this seaside city\nof 66,000 people at a small venue on the water, but after thousands of\nRSVPs came back online, he was forced to reschedule the speech in a large\narena usually reserved for big musical acts and hockey games. Nearly 8,000\npeople showed up, flooding the standing room with Mainers touting an\neclectic mix of tribal tattoos, floral prints, polo shirts and New Balance\nsneakers.\n\n\n\nSanders\xe2\x80\x99 supporters found in Portland a candidate invigorated by the last\nmonths of success. With his left hand gripping the podium and his right\nhand dancing in the air as if holding a marionette, Sanders framed the\nrecent liberal groundswell as part of a long legacy of activism. He pointed\nto the labor movement of the early 20th century, the women\xe2\x80\x99s suffrage\nactivists and the civil rights movement as models for changing the country.\nHe called for equal pay, paid family leave, a higher minimum wage, breaking\nup the big banks, and a massive infrastructure rebuilding program, a la the\nNew Deal.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThere is nothing, nothing, nothing that we cannot accomplish!\xe2\x80\x9d said\nSanders.\n\n\n\nThe crowds have taken note of Bernie\xe2\x80\x99s sanguine outlook and call to action.\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s telling us that the people\xe2\x80\x99s movements\xe2\x80\x94the grassroots movements\xe2\x80\x94have\nsucceeded when people got off their asses and they went out and marched,\xe2\x80\x9d\nsaid James Murdoch, a self-employed designer and builder who attended the\nrally. \xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99re now getting to the point where people are getting involved\nand getting active again.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nPortland was just one leg on Sanders\xe2\x80\x99 packed schedule: after a Madison,\nWisconsin rally on Wednesday that drew some 9,500 people, Sanders spent\nthree days in western Iowa corn country, where in Council Bluffs, 2,500\npeople attended a rally, according to the campaign\xe2\x80\x94more than any other Iowa\nrally so far. (In Iowa he is trailing Clinton by 52-33.) He flew back to\nBurlington, and then drove with his wife and an aide the 250-odd miles to\nPortland.\n\n\n\nDespite some of the change in tone, Sanders\xe2\x80\x99 speeches are still largely\njeremiads on the perennial problems. Wall Street and the greed of the 1%\nare destroying America, Sanders says, climate change is wreaking drought\nand deadly heat waves, and misguided trade agreements are sending millions\nof jobs overseas to countries like China. There\xe2\x80\x99s only a short window of\nopportunity to stop global warming, and the middle class is in grave danger.\n\n\n\nAmong his fans, there\xe2\x80\x99s a new hint of faith that the gravity of the\ncampaign may have jolted something awake. People in the audience said\nafterward that Sanders had struck a chord, particularly for those\ndisappointed by the Obama years and cautious of the hope brand that\ndominated the 2008 campaign. \xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s saying the things that need to be said,\xe2\x80\x9d\nsaid Fran Falcone, a mental health counselor, of Sanders. \xe2\x80\x9cWe need to start\nreally looking at what\xe2\x80\x99s going in our country that\xe2\x80\x99s turned it into a place\na lot of us don\xe2\x80\x99t recognize.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nAfter the speech, Sanders dined at a Spanish-inspired restaurant a few\nblocks away on Portland\xe2\x80\x99s Congress Street. Word got around town he was\nthere, and a small crowd gathered to seem him before he went to bed and\nmade for Washington D.C. the next day for Senate duties.\n\n\n\nMeanwhile, two buddies drank beers on the upstairs terrace of an Irish pub\none block from the rally arena. They discussed the\nreality-check-and-momentum phenomenon. \xe2\x80\x9cCampaigns have cycles,\xe2\x80\x9d said\nPortland resident Doug Hall about Sanders, speaking over the house music.\n\xe2\x80\x9cThis is the wake-the-f***-up cycle.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nPaul Drinan, who runs a non-profit and also lives in town, agreed. \xe2\x80\x9cAt this\npoint in the game that\xe2\x80\x99s the appeal: there\xe2\x80\x99s no fluff in the message. He\xe2\x80\x99s\ntelling it like it is,\xe2\x80\x9d said Drinan. \xe2\x80\x9cBernie\xe2\x80\x99s riding the wave.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n*As Labor Grapples With Candidate Endorsements, Transit Union Head Applauds\nBernie Sanders\n<http://www.ibtimes.com/election-2016-labor-grapples-candidate-endorsements-transit-union-head-applauds-1996900>\n// IB Times // Cole Stangler \xe2\x80\x93July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nSen. Bernie Sanders, I-Vt., says he wants to fight the \xe2\x80\x9cbillionaire class,"\nthe signature phrase of a presidential campaign that\'s thrived by pitting\nbeleaguered American workers against the rich and powerful. And as the\nself-described socialist continues his steady rise in the polls against\nDemocratic primary opponent and presidential front-runner Hillary Clinton,\nhe\xe2\x80\x99s winning support from the American underdogs par excellence: trade\nunionists.\n\n\n\nNo major unions have made White House endorsements, and the national\nAFL-CIO has yet to formally back a candidate. Still, a couple of state\nlabor federations have passed resolutions backing Sanders\xe2\x80\x99 bid (even though\nthey were rebuked in an AFL-CIO memo for breaching the federation\xe2\x80\x99s\nendorsement process); thousands of rank-and-file union members have signed\nup with the grassroots Labor for Bernie network; and last week, the\nrecently retired head of one of the nation\xe2\x80\x99s largest unions joined Bernie\xe2\x80\x99s\ncampaign team as a volunteer.\n\n\n\nIn a recent interview with International Business Times -- before the\nAFL-CIO fired off its warning memo last week -- the head of the nation\xe2\x80\x99s\nlargest transit union cheered Sanders\xe2\x80\x99 \xe2\x80\x9cwillingness to get outside the\nbubble.\xe2\x80\x9d The Amalgamated Transit Union\xe2\x80\x99s Larry Hanley did not endorse the\nsenator, and the union, which represents some 200,000 people, hasn\xe2\x80\x99t\ndecided whom to back yet. But the ATU\'s Hanley credited Sanders for raising\nthe sorts of problems, beyond bread-and-butter labor ones, that he says\nhurt American workers: things like unnecessary military spending,\nenvironmental degradation and prohibitively costly college tuition. Hanley\nbecomes the first president of a major union to weigh in publicly -- and\ncandidly -- about the Democratic primary matchup.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThis model doesn\xe2\x80\x99t work,\xe2\x80\x9d said the outspoken labor leader in a\nwide-ranging conversation about national politics and the 2016 campaign.\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s not working for our unions, it\xe2\x80\x99s not working for our members, it\xe2\x80\x99s\nnot working for our people and we have to change the model.
