There\xe2\x80\x99s no reason why we\nhave to burden our kids with debt, why we have to make them come out of\ncollege with something comparable to a mortgage to pay before they get a\njob.\xe2\x80\x99 I mean, come on, this stuff is obvious.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe live in a bubble of false discussion, and both sides, Democrats and\nRepublicans, refuse to break out of that bubble,\xe2\x80\x9d Hanley continued. \xe2\x80\x9cI\nthink Bernie has shown more of a willingness to get outside the bubble,\noutside the box and have those discussions. As a consequence of that, I\nthink he\xe2\x80\x99s a very good addition to the race. I think hopefully that he will\nencourage people in the Democratic Party to remember where they came from\nand remember their roots.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nAt the same time, Hanley offered some praise for Clinton. A former bus\ndriver from the New York City borough of Staten Island, Hanley rose through\nthe ranks of the transit union before his election to the top office in\n2010. As he was serving as president of his New York City local, in 2000,\nhe supported the then-first lady\xe2\x80\x99s successful Senate campaign. \xe2\x80\x9cI have a\nlong history of fond affection for Hillary Clinton -- she has stood up and\ndone many things in her lifetime of a historic nature,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.\nNevertheless, Hanley added -- with a flair of ambiguity -- \xe2\x80\x9cthe truth as I\nknow it is much more frequently expressed by Bernie, and even more than\nBernie, by Elizabeth Warren.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nBut unions are in a pickle: Is it worth getting behind the underdog or does\nit make more sense to accept conventional wisdom and plan accordingly?\nAfter all, \xe2\x80\x9cif the election\xe2\x80\x99s between Hillary and just about any one of the\nRepublicans that have come forward,\xe2\x80\x9d Hanley said, \xe2\x80\x9cit\xe2\x80\x99s gonna look like\nheaven and hell.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m going to confess to being conflicted, and I think as a matter of fact,\nthe whole labor movement is conflicted over this,\xe2\x80\x9d Hanley said. \xe2\x80\x9cWhile we\nsee Bernie being a champion for many of our issues, we\xe2\x80\x99re anguished waiting\non Hillary to take the lead on that, too.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nIn the ATU at least, Hanley said, leaders are expressing more frustration\nwith the general political climate than during the last open Democratic\npresidential primary. (Exasperation, in general, jibes more with Sanders\xe2\x80\x99\ncalls for \xe2\x80\x9cpolitical revolution\xe2\x80\x9d than Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s mild-mannered liberalism.)\nIn 2007, a few years before Hanley took over the reins, the union endorsed\nHillary Clinton for president, eventually spending more than $70,000 on her\nfailed primary campaign.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cPeople are united in the notion that we can\xe2\x80\x99t accept the status quo, that\nthe Democratic Party no longer is the party of Franklin Delano Roosevelt,\nit\xe2\x80\x99s more like the party of Nelson Rockefeller and the Republicans are more\nlike the party of the Ku Klux Klan. That\xe2\x80\x99s kinda the way America\xe2\x80\x99s\nshifted,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cThere is a boil going on right under the surface in\nAmerica and the advantage Bernie has, by being willing to talk about this\nkind of stuff, is that he may just make that pot boil over.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n*Coons: "Not Confident" In Bernie Sanders\' Qualifications\n<https://www.bloomberg.com/politics/articles/2015-07-07/coons-not-confident-in-bernie-sanders-qualifications>\n// Bloomberg // Kendall Breitman \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nSenator Chris Coons is "not confident" that his colleague Senator Bernie\nSanders is presidential material.\n\n\n\n"I am not confident that he\'s got all the qualifications that the American\npublic will look for in its next commander-in-chief," Coons said Tuesday on\nBloomberg Politics\' "With All Due Respect," adding that the ultimate\njudgment will be left up to the electorate.\n\n\n\nCoons comments came after the Democrat was pressed on previous remarks from\nSenator Claire McCaskill - a Clinton ally - who on June 25 told MSNBC that\nSanders is a "socialist" who "is too liberal to gather enough votes in this\ncountry to become president."\n\n\n\n"I, quite frankly, am hoping for someone with more seasoning."\n\n\n\nCoons, who has a close relationship with his fellow Delaware politician and\npotential 2016 candidate Vice President Joe Biden, has yet to endorse any\nspecific candidate so far. Although he said believes Sanders has a\n"terrific record" on advocating for issues involving veterans, middle class\neconomics and social and economic justice, Coons made it plain that the\nindependent from Vermont, who caucuses with Senate Democrats, is not a\ncontender for his nod.\n\n\n\n"I, quite frankly, am hoping for someone with more seasoning, more\nexperience, who served both in the executive branch and the legislative\nbranch," Coons said. "I do think that the sort of experience that I think\nwe will see in the likely Democratic nominee - whether that ends up being\nJoe Biden or Hillary Clinton - would span both the congressional and\nexecutive branches and I think that\'s the sort of experience we should look\nfor in our commander in chief."\n\n\n\n*Fox News\xe2\x80\x99 big Bernie Sanders lie: The right\xe2\x80\x99s laughably lame effort to\nlink Donald Trump and Sanders\n<http://www.salon.com/2015/07/07/fox_news_big_bernie_sanders_lie_the_rights_laughably_lame_effort_to_link_donald_trump_and_sanders/>\n// Salon // Sean Illing \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nThe media cannot help comparing Donald Trump to Bernie Sanders. And the\ncomparison is not altogether wrong. Both candidates appeal to their\nrespective bases. Both are challenging their party\xe2\x80\x99s establishment choices.\nAnd both are drawing massive crowds while surging in national polls.\n\n\n\nThe left (understandably) cringes at such comparisons. Bernie Sanders,\nwhatever you think of him, is a serious person with real ideas. He\xe2\x80\x99s been a\npublic servant since 1981, when he was elected mayor of Burlington,\nVermont. He\xe2\x80\x99s now the longest-serving independent in the history of\nCongress. And his bid for the presidency, while a long shot, is clearly\nearnest.\n\n\n\nDonald Trump, on the other hand, is a clown \xe2\x80\x93 a pompous, spray-tanned\nclown. More important, he\xe2\x80\x99s not actually running for president. His\ncandidacy is a piece of performance art, a self-promoting circus. No one\npaying attention believes he wants to be president \xe2\x80\x93 I suspect he wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t\nrun at all if this were a real possibility. Trump is campaigning because he\ncan, because it bolsters his brand, and because people are dumb enough to\nlisten to him talk about things he doesn\xe2\x80\x99t understand. If anything, Trump\xe2\x80\x99s\ncampaign, much like Sarah Palin\xe2\x80\x99s, is a reminder of just how broken and\nstupid our political system has become.\n\n\n\nHowever wrong it feels, Democrats ought to embrace the juxtaposition of\nTrump and Sanders for at least two reasons. First, it\xe2\x80\x99s accurate. Both\ncandidates are indeed authentic representations of their party\xe2\x80\x99s base.\nTrump is a near-perfect distillation of the modern American right: The\nbravado, the bigotry, the raging idiocy, the false confidence, and the lack\nof ideas \xe2\x80\x93 it\xe2\x80\x99s all there in one gloriously manicured body.\n\n\n\nIt\xe2\x80\x99s not simply that Trump has bad ideas; it\xe2\x80\x99s that he doesn\xe2\x80\x99t have any\nideas at all. And he\xe2\x80\x99s quite explicit about this. His announcement speech\nwas essentially a stream-of-consciousness rant, totally bereft of anything\nresembling a policy proposal. His entire platform consists of him telling\nyou a) how rich and smart he is and b) how stupid and broke everyone else\nis. That\xe2\x80\x99s it. If Trump were laughed out of conservative town halls, that\xe2\x80\x99d\nbe one thing. But he\xe2\x80\x99s not. He\xe2\x80\x99s embraced. According to this recent CNN\npoll, Trump is second only to Jeb Bush among national conservatives. This\nmeans Trump\xe2\x80\x99s fevered ramblings are resonating with the Republican base,\neven if Trump himself doesn\xe2\x80\x99t actually believe anything he says.\n\n\n\nBernie Sanders may well represent the \xe2\x80\x9cextreme\xe2\x80\x9d left of the Democratic\nParty, but he has real ideas; arguments can be made against them, of\ncourse, but the point is that he offers something substantive against which\nto argue. Unlike Trump, he has an actual platform, spelling out what he\nwants to do and how he intends to do it. From infrastructural decay to\nclimate change to tax reform to higher education, Sanders is proposing\nsolutions. Conservatives may not like those solutions, but they at least\nhave to be reckoned with. This is a fundamental distinction between Trump\nand Sanders, one the GOP would prefer to ignore. Which leads me to the\nsecond reason why liberals should embrace Trump-Sanders comparisons.\n\n\n\nTo the extent that Trump and Sanders reflect the views of the right and\nleft wings of their parties, they vividly clarify just how different the\ntwo parties are. It says something significant about the Republican Party\nthat there\xe2\x80\x99s space for someone like Trump or Sarah Palin or even Herman\nCain in it. These people aren\xe2\x80\x99t credible candidates; they\xe2\x80\x99re\nproduct-pushing brands looking to capitalize on conservative credulity. I\ndon\xe2\x80\x99t believe the same can be said of Democratic candidates, no matter how\nwrong-headed you find their policy ideas.\n\n\n\nRepublican operatives know all of this to be true, which is why they\xe2\x80\x99ll do\neverything they can to equate Sanders and Trump. But they\xe2\x80\x99ll spin a false\nnarrative. They\xe2\x80\x99ll argue, as John Gibson on FoxNews.com does, that\nDemocrats should be \xe2\x80\x9cembarrassed\xe2\x80\x9d by Sanders for the same reasons\nRepublicans should be embarrassed by Trump. Nobody, especially Democrats,\nshould fall for this.\n\n\n\nThere are crucial differences between Trump and Sanders, some of which are\ncited above. But the most important difference here is between the two\nparties. Trump\xe2\x80\x99s circus act isn\xe2\x80\x99t possible in the Democratic Party. There\nare no celebrity candidates on the left \xe2\x80\x93 and certainly none capable of\npolling at the level Trump does. Democrats have had their share of bad\ncandidates over the years, but they\xe2\x80\x99re bad for different (and less\noffensive) reasons than GOP candidates. They\xe2\x80\x99re bad for reasons related to\ntheir ideas or campaign platform or something politically relevant.\n\n\n\nOnly in the Republican Party do unserious candidates emerge as contenders.\nOnly in the Republican Party are half-baked celebrities allowed to hijack\nthe process to promote their private careers. Only among conservative\nRepublicans are hucksters like Trump embraced. Democrats can\xe2\x80\x99t point these\ntruths out enough.\n\n\n\nThe Republican Party created the Frankenstein that is Donald Trump. They\xe2\x80\x99ve\ncultivated the idiocy he represents in their ranks for years. If Trump\nappeals to their base \xe2\x80\x93 and he obviously does \xe2\x80\x93 that tells you everything\nyou need to know about who they are and what they stand for.\n\n\n\nIt also tells you how little respect the GOP has for the political process.\nThere ought to be no place for Trump at this level of politics \xe2\x80\x93 in either\nparty. But there is, and it\xe2\x80\x99s telling that it\xe2\x80\x99s permitted only in one party.\n\n\n\n*UNDECLARED*\n\n\n\n*OTHER*\n\n\n\n*How durable is the Democratic advantage among Latinos?\n<http://www.washingtonpost.com/blogs/plum-line/wp/2015/07/07/how-durable-is-the-democratic-advantage-among-latinos/>\n// WaPo // Greg Sargent \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nIs the overwhelming advantage that Democrats appear to be building among\nLatinos durable? Or could it prove far more ephemeral than it appears?\n\n\n\nPut another way, can Democrats count on the 2016 GOP presidential ticket\nre-running Mitt Romney\xe2\x80\x99s historically bad performance among Latino voters?\nOr could a Jeb Bush (or, less likely in my view, Marco Rubio) general\nelection candidacy whittle away at the Dem edge among those voters and\nreverse gains that had seemed to be hardening? Folks with long memories\nwill recall that George W. Bush successfully pulled that reversal off in\n2000. Couldn\xe2\x80\x99t that happen again?\n\n\n\nThis is one of the big questions of 2016, and its answer could be key to\nthe campaign\xe2\x80\x99s outcome. Right now, there are plenty of reasons for\nDemocrats to be optimistic about it. But it\xe2\x80\x99s worth entertaining the\nalternate scenario.\n\n\n\nThe case for Dem optimism has been fortified by Donald Trump, who in recent\ndays has been spraying inflammatory quotes about immigrants around like a\ngarden sprinkler. It\xe2\x80\x99s true that a number of GOP candidates have condemned\nhis remarks. But as Michael Gerson details, Republicans still appear locked\nin a debate over the fundamental underlying question of whether their route\nto the White House lies in pumping up the white vote in the Rust Belt (a\nstrategy perhaps foreshadowed by Scott Walker\xe2\x80\x99s move to the right on\nimmigration) or in broadening their appeal beyond their demographic comfort\nzone (a strategy that Jeb Bush has urged on the party).\n\n\n\nAn additional reason for Dem optimism: Some Republicans are reportedly\nskeptical that the party should bother focusing its energy on nominating a\ncandidate who might appeal to Latinos, on the grounds that those voters\nagree with Democrats on many issues, so being pro-immigration reform (as\nJeb is) won\xe2\x80\x99t be enough anyway.\n\n\n\nBut some Democrats think their party should devote more time to worrying\nabout the possibility that someone like Bush could win over enough Latino\nvoters to make a decisive difference.\n\n\n\nSimon Rosenberg, the president of the NDN think tank, floats the\npossibility of a GOP ticket that includes Bush and Nevada governor Brian\nSandoval as vice president. Sandoval won a third of the Latino vote in his\n2010 race, despite striking a hard-ish line on immigration, from which he\nhas since backed off. Sandoval is relatively young. A Bush-Sandoval ticket\nwould be led by a man with a Mexican wife and Latino-American children, and\nbacked up by a man of Mexican descent \xe2\x80\x94 representing a bet that the GOP can\ncontest Florida and western states with large Latino populations by\nimproving its cultural appeal among those voters. Remember, Republicans\nonly need to marginally reduce their historically large 2012 deficit among\nLatinos to improve their chances in such states.\n\n\n\nSo Rosenberg thinks Dems should invest more now in using the Trump\noutbursts to do more damage to the GOP brand among Latinos, as a kind of\ninsurance policy against outcomes such as a Bush-Sandoval ticket. Rosenberg\nemails me:\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhile the Democratic advantage today is significant, what we don\xe2\x80\x99t know is\nwhat happens with an historically Hispanic and Spanish friendly GOP ticket\nof, let\xe2\x80\x99s say, Bush and Sandoval. One Bush already used a smart Hispanic\nstrategy to get to the White House. Given that, Democrats should be\nanything but confident and complacent right now. They need to be doing\nmore, now, to make it harder for any GOP ticket to dig out of the hole\nTrump and others have dug for the GOP.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nTo be sure, there are big differences between the current moment and the\nrun-up to the 2000 election. Dems are far more united behind immigration\nreform today than in the late 1990s, reflecting a changing Democratic Party\nincreasingly reliant on Latinos. Buzzfeed reports that the Hillary Clinton\ncampaign is developing a very comprehensive and aggressive plan for\nnational Latino outreach. She has already pledged to go farther than Obama\ndid on his executive actions on deportations. And today she renewed her\nsupport for comprehensive reform and attacked the GOP as backward on the\nissue. All of these things are signs of Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s commitment to the party\xe2\x80\x99s\nnew demographic realities.\n\n\n\nMeanwhile, House Republicans have steadily moved rightward on immigration,\npassing on a historic chance to act on the Senate reform bill and voting\nrepeatedly to roll back Obama\xe2\x80\x99s deportation actions. That has many Dems\nconfident \xe2\x80\x94 to a point.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe damage may be too great to the GOP brand,\xe2\x80\x9d one senior aide to a\nprominent Latino House Democrat says. \xe2\x80\x9cIt may take more than Bush-Sandoval\nto rehabilitate this huge mistake Republicans have been making. But we\ndon\xe2\x80\x99t know that. Personality, charisma, language, and the individual\ncandidates mean a lot.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nSo, yes, perhaps Republicans have moved so far to the right on immigration\nthat the party can\xe2\x80\x99t conceivably re-run the 2000 Bush immigration strategy,\nor perhaps even reconstituting that strategy wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t be enough to reverse\nGOP losses among Latinos at this point. But Democrats can\xe2\x80\x99t count on those\noutcomes.\n\n\n\n*Here\'s what Clinton, O\'Malley and Sanders told America\'s biggest teachers\nunion\n<http://www.washingtonexaminer.com/hillary-dems-court-americas-biggest-teachers-union/article/2567749>\n// The Washington Examiner // Jason Russell \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nDemocratic candidates for president didn\'t miss their chance to address\nover 7,000 members of the National Education Association, which will be a\npowerful player in the Democratic primary process. Hillary Clinton, Martin\nO\'Malley and Bernie Sanders all sent video messages to the teachers, who\nwere gathered at the NEA\'s Representative Assembly.\n\n\n\nIn her address, Clinton used a theme of teachers unlocking potential in\nstudents. She talked about how teachers had encouraged her and her mother\nat a young age. "Every semester, in schools across the country, you\nmultiply my mother\'s story by millions," Clinton told the teachers. "When\nwe invest in our children, we do invest in our country\'s future, and we\nneed to do more of that." Clinton promised high quality preschool, a\ndoubling of spending on the federal Head Start program, and making college\naffordable for every single person.\n\n\n\nSanders struck a more ideological tone. "We need some fundamental changes\nin our national priorities," Sanders said. "Instead of giving tax breaks to\nbillionaires, maybe we invest in our children, maybe we invest in\neducation." He promised to make progress on fixing No Child Left Behind, on\nuniversal pre-K and on free college tuition. He also called teachers the\nreal heroes and heroines of the country.\n\n\n\nO\'Malley tried to strike an optimistic note. "I believe, like you, that\nAmerica\'s best days can still be in front of us," O\'Malley said. He didn\'t\nmake any specific promises about what he would do as president, but\nO\'Malley touted the pro-union reforms he implemented in Maryland while\nserving as governor. For example, spending more on public education and\nmaking college more affordable. "This is what we do as Americans, to do\nmore in every generation, to give our children a future with more\nopportunity, rather than less."\n\n\n\nNEA President Lily Eskelsen Garcia was glad the three candidates took the\ntime to address the union\'s members. "Recommending a candidate for\npresident of the United States is a civic responsibility that educators\ntake very seriously," said Eskelsen Garcia. "Going through the process to\npick the right candidate that represents our values and sets the right\npriorities is critically important." Eskelsen Garcia has met privately with\nClinton, O\'Malley and Sanders as part of the NEA\'s endorsement process for\nthe 2016 presidential election.\n\n\n\nThe NEA is the nation\'s largest teachers union, with 3 million members.\n\n\n\n*GOP*\n\n\n\n*DECLARED*\n\n\n\n*BUSH*\n\n\n\n*Florida\xe2\x80\x99s Economic Leap Under Jeb Bush Helped By Housing Bubble,\nEconomists Say\n<http://blogs.wsj.com/washwire/2015/07/07/floridas-economic-leap-under-jeb-bush-helped-by-housing-bubble-economists-say/>\n// WSJ // Bob Davis \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nFormer Florida Gov. Jeb Bush says he can deliver 4% annual economic growth\nas president \xe2\x80\x93 about twice as fast as the U.S. has been growing recently.\nWhy is he so confident? During his 1999-2007 tenure as governor, Florida\ngrew 4.4%, his campaign boasts.\n\n\n\nToday it even unveiled a cute graphic illustrating the claim.\n\n\n\nThe trouble is, say some economists, Gov. Bush\xe2\x80\x99s Florida growth record was\nbased in large part on a housing bubble \xe2\x80\x93 national in scope but\nparticularly frothy in Florida \xe2\x80\x94 that exploded the year he left office in\n2007. Wells Fargo economist Mark Vitner, who has studied the Florida\neconomy since the 1980s, estimates that the housing bubble accounted for\nabout one-fourth of Florida\xe2\x80\x99s growth during Mr. Bush\xe2\x80\x99s tenure.\n\n\n\nSubtract that out and you are left with 3.3% annual growth, somewhat faster\nthan the 3% at which the U.S. economy grew annually during that period. (To\nbe sure, the U.S. growth record overall back then was also affected by the\nhousing bubble, though not as severely as Florida was.)\n\n\n\nMr. Vitner said that Mr. Bush deserves credit as governor for trying to\ndiversify the state\xe2\x80\x99s economy, particularly by luring biotech companies to\nthe state. He also says the U.S. could grow faster and maybe even at the 4%\nlevel that Mr. Bush has set as his target. But his Florida growth record\nisn\xe2\x80\x99t proof of that.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cFour percent growth was helped along by the housing boom,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.\n\n\n\nA spokeswoman for Mr. Bush said that  18%  of Florida\xe2\x80\x99s job growth during\nGov. Bush\xe2\x80\x99s two terms was in the housing or construction fields. \xe2\x80\x9cHis\noverall economic record is impressive,\xe2\x80\x9d spokeswoman Kristy Campbell said in\nan emailed response. That record  includes balancing the state\xe2\x80\x99s budget,\ncutting taxes and fast job growth, she said.\n\n\n\nMoody\xe2\x80\x99s Analytics chief economist Mark Zandi, a housing expert, says\nFlorida\xe2\x80\x99s economy in the early 2000s isn\xe2\x80\x99t a model for U.S. growth over the\ncoming years.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe growth in Florida wasn\xe2\x80\x99t sustainable,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt was something\ntemporary\xe2\x80\x9d due to the housing bubble.\n\n\n\nMoreover, Florida isn\xe2\x80\x99t representative of the U.S., he said, because its\npopulation grows more rapidly than the U.S. as a whole, giving it an\nexpanding pool of workers. That in itself can add to growth.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cFlorida isn\xe2\x80\x99t a useful analogy because of its unique demographic\nsituation,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s important for leaders to be aggressive [on the\neconomy] and set a higher bar,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Zandi said. \xe2\x80\x9cBut 4% is a stretch.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nIn an article in the Wall Street Journal last month, Mr. Bush\xe2\x80\x99s top\neconomic advisers, Columbia University Business School Dean Glenn Hubbard\nand former Federal Reserve Governor Kevin Warsh, argued that 4% growth was\nattainable with the right set of policies.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cSetting a goal of 4% growth  invites meaningful policy contributions from\nthose who would be our leaders,\xe2\x80\x9d they wrote.\n\n\n\n*Did Jeb Bush cut taxes each year as Florida governor?\n<http://www.baynews9.com/content/news/baynews9/news/article.html/content/news/articles/cfn/2015/6/25/politifact_did_jeb_b.html>\n// Politifact \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nOn the campaign trail, a recurring theme among Republican candidates is how\nthey have cut taxes and reduced the size of government. For former Florida\nGov. Jeb Bush, that message is a core part of his presentation.\n\n\n\nOn June 2 at Gov. Rick Scott\'s Economic Growth Summit in Orlando, Bush\nnoted how he cut taxes for Floridians. Bush said the following:\n\n\n\n"In Florida, for eight years we cut taxes every year, totaling $19 billion."\n\n\n\nPolitiFact Florida looked into Bush\'s record to see if his claim was\naccurate and reporter Joshua Gillin says Bush gets a HALF TRUE rating.\nGillin says there are tax cuts that Bush can take credit for and others\nwhere he cannot.\n\n\n\n"We took the detailed analysis provided by his campaign and showed it to\nseveral economists," Gillin said. "They responded that the methodology that\nthey used to get to the $19 billion figure was pretty clear. "One was the\nintangibles tax. This is the amount that you pay on investments and stocks.\nThe other was the federal estate tax. But when it came to education policy, some of\npresidential candidate\xe2\x80\x99s proposals had a familiar ring to them.\n\n\n\nMr. Rubio, the Republican from Florida, called for overhauling the college\naccreditation system, creating a pay scale for student loan repayment and\nexpanding investment in vocational training.\n\n\n\nMany of the details from those ideas sounded strikingly similar to policies\nthat President Obama has called for during his time in office.\n\n\n\nMr. Rubio called for creating \xe2\x80\x9ca new accreditation process that welcomes\nlow-cost, innovative providers\xe2\x80\x9d that would allow new competitors into the\neducation marketplace. In 2013, Mr. Obama proposed establishing \xe2\x80\x9ca new,\nalternative system of accreditation that would provide pathways for higher\neducation models and colleges to receive federal student aid based on\nperformance and results.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nOn Tuesday, Mr. Rubio proposed a progressive scale for student loan\nrepayments to ease burdens on people who take lower wage jobs when they\ngraduate. \xe2\x80\x9cThe more they make, the faster they pay back their loans; and\nthe less they make, the less strain their loans cause,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.\n\n\n\nLast summer, Mr. Obama made a similar appeal, devising a \xe2\x80\x9cpay as you earn\xe2\x80\x9d\nplan that give Americans who were repaying loans the chance to cap those\npayments at 10 percent of their incomes.\n\n\n\nThe senator also said that if he is elected president he would expand\napprenticeship programs and make vocational training more easily\naccessible. While the idea came without specifics of how this would be\nachieved, it did echo a proposal that Mr. Obama put forward at the end of\nhis first term that to ramp up spending on vocational training at the high\nschool and college level.\n\n\n\nWhile Mr. Rubio has worked with Democrats on education legislation in the\npast, not all of his ideas are popular with the opposing party. Critics\nargue that his plan to create \xe2\x80\x9cstudent investment plans\xe2\x80\x9d could make college\nmore expensive for some people, and the suggestion that he might eliminate\nthe Department of Education is likely a non-starter with liberals.\n\n\n\nHolly Shulman, a spokeswoman for the Democratic National Committee, also\nnoted that Mr. Rubio blocked a bill that would allow students to refinance\ntheir student loans, and opposed the president\xe2\x80\x99s plan to make community\ncollege debt-free to anyone who works.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cMarco Rubio has yet to articulate any new ideas,\xe2\x80\x9d Ms. Shulman said.\n\n\n\n*Marco Rubio Attacks Higher Education \xe2\x80\x98Cartel\xe2\x80\x99 and Jabs Rivals\n<http://www.nytimes.com/politics/first-draft/2015/07/07/marco-rubio-attacks-higher-education-cartel-and-jabs-rivals/>\n// NYT // Jeremy Peters \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nSenator Marco Rubio, laying out an economic blueprint that will be central\nto his campaign for president, called Tuesday for dismantling the \xe2\x80\x9ccartel\nof existing colleges and universities\xe2\x80\x9d that he said left too many students\nwithout viable career paths and burdened by tens of thousands of dollars in\ndebt.\n\n\n\nIn a speech that was part history lesson, part policy prescription, and\npunctuated with barbs at Hillary Rodham Clinton, Mr. Rubio spoke to a crowd\nof several dozen people at a technology center and put forward his vision\nfor the American economy if it is to thrive into the next century. He also\ntook veiled swipes at the Bush family.\n\n\n\nMr. Rubio, a Florida Republican, dismissed the idea of a minimum-wage\nincrease as \xe2\x80\x9cthinking small.\xe2\x80\x9d He said that big government had rigged taxes\nand regulations in favor of powerful interests. And he proposed an overhaul\nof higher education that would change the way colleges are accredited and\nstudent loans are repaid.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe do not need timid tweaks to the old system; we need a holistic\noverhaul,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Rubio said. \xe2\x80\x9cWe need to change how we provide degrees, how\nthose degrees are accessed, how much that access costs, how those costs are\npaid and even how those payments are determined.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nAs part of his higher education plan, Mr. Rubio has proposed two\ninnovations that are aimed at making student loans more affordable. First,\nhe said, he would put in effect an income-based payment system to allow\ngraduates earning lower salaries to repay creditors on a timetable that he\nsaid would cause \xe2\x80\x9cless strain.\xe2\x80\x9d Those who earn more would have to repay\ntheir loans at a faster rate.\n\n\n\nA form of income-based repayment plans for student loans already exists.\n\n\n\nMr. Rubio would also allow students to partner with investors who would\ncover the students\xe2\x80\x99 tuition in exchange for a percentage of their earnings\nfor a few years after graduation.\n\n\n\nThe speech mostly contained ideas that he had put forward before. But it\nwas a return to the campaign trail after almost two full months in which he\nwas on a coast-to-coast fund-raising tour.\n\n\n\nHe used his time in Chicago to take swipes at his opponents, some overt and\nothers more subtle. He referred three times to Mrs. Clinton, who is running\nher second campaign for the Democratic presidential nomination. \xe2\x80\x9cThe race\nfor the future will never be won by going backward,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt will\nnever be won by hopping in Hillary Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s time machine to yesterday.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nOther slights appeared aimed just as much at some of Mr. Rubio\xe2\x80\x99s Republican\nopponents, like former Gov. Jeb Bush of Florida. Mr. Rubio said the ideas\noffered by Mrs. Clinton \xe2\x80\x9cand other outdated leaders are narrow and\nshortsighted.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe have learned, painfully, that the old ways no longer work,\xe2\x80\x9d he said,\n\xe2\x80\x9cthat Washington cannot pretend the world is the same as it was in the\n\xe2\x80\x9980s, it cannot raise taxes like it did in the \xe2\x80\x9990s, and it cannot grow\ngovernment like it did in the 2000s.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nThose last two references \xe2\x80\x94 to raising taxes in the 1990s and expanding\ngovernment in the 2000s \xe2\x80\x94 were not coincidental. Mr. Bush\xe2\x80\x99s father,\nPresident George Bush, famously approved a tax increase in 1990 after\npromising to block any. And his older brother, President George W. Bush,\noversaw a significant expansion of the federal government after the Sept.\n11, 2001, terrorist attacks.\n\n\n\n*Five takeaways from Marco Rubio\xe2\x80\x99s speech on the innovation economy\n<http://www.washingtonpost.com/news/powerpost/wp/2015/07/07/five-takeaways-from-marco-rubios-speech-on-the-innovation-economy/>\n// WaPo // Steven Overly \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nMarco Rubio is pushing a series of changes to the nation\xe2\x80\x99s tax, immigration\nand education systems that the Republican presidential candidate contends\nwill better prepare Americans for an economy driven by rapid technological\ninnovation.\n\n\n\nThe ideas outlined by the Florida senator in a speech on Tuesday, which was\ndelivered at a co-working space for tech start-ups in Chicago, come as\nother presidential candidates are also trying to court the tech community\xe2\x80\x99s\nvote. Sen. Rand Paul (R-Ky.), Jeb Bush and Hillary Clinton have all met\nwith technology executives and enthusiasts in Silicon Valley in recent\nmonths, hoping to mine the wealthy sector for potential donors and voices\nof support.\n\n\n\nWith that audience in mind, Rubio\xe2\x80\x99s speech focused largely on policy issues\nthat are front of mind in tech circles, such as finding ways to get more\nhighly skilled immigrants into the country and overhauling the tax code.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cToday\xe2\x80\x99s Technological Revolution carries extraordinary opportunities \xe2\x80\x93\neven more, I believe, than the Industrial Revolution ever did. But we have\nnot yet seized these opportunities, nor is it guaranteed that we will,\xe2\x80\x9d\nRubio said. \xe2\x80\x9cWhether we do or do not will depend on the actions we take,\nthe leaders we choose, and the reforms we adopt.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nWhat follows are five takeaways from the policy pitch Rubio delivered on\nTuesday.\n\n\n\nImmigration\n\n\n\nRubio did not outline a comprehensive plan to address existing undocumented\nimmigrants, but said the system should prioritize those immigrants who\npossess the skills and education that many American employers desire.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThis requires reforming our legal immigration system to make it skill- and\nmerit-based rather than family-based, which will protect American workers\nand attract more talent to grow our economy and create jobs,\xe2\x80\x9d Rubio said.\n\n\n\nThat position should be well received among technology companies, which\nhave long pushed for visas to be made more readily available to immigrants\nwith science, technology, engineering and math degrees. Companies contend\nthere aren\xe2\x80\x99t enough American workers who possess those skills, and existing\nlaws make it expensive and difficult to recruit talent from overseas.\n\n\n\nEducation\n\n\n\nRubio also set his political sights on the U.S. higher education system,\nwhich he said is \xe2\x80\x9ccontrolled by what amounts to a cartel of existing\ncolleges and universities, which use their power over the accreditation\nprocess to block innovative, low-cost competitors from entering the market.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nHe vowed to establish a new accreditation process within his first 100 days\nin office that would be more welcoming to new players. Rubio also\nreiterated support for the \xe2\x80\x9cStudent Right to Know Before You Go Act,\xe2\x80\x9d which\nwould inform students how much money they can expect to earn from a given\ndegree prior taking out student loans.\n\n\n\nStudent Loans\n\n\n\nThe cloud of debt that follows many students after college prevents many\nfrom pursuing a higher education, Rubio told the audience. That\xe2\x80\x99s\nespecially true for low-income individuals and single parents, who most\nstand to benefit from a degree.\n\n\n\nRubio said he plans to implement income-based repayment of student loans,\nmeaning those who earn more money are expected to repay their loans faster.\nHe also called for the creation of Student Investment Plans that would\nallow wealthy individuals to invest in a young person\xe2\x80\x99s education in\nexchange for a cut of their future salary.\n\n\n\nFinally, he called for an expansion of vocational training and\napprenticeship programs so that students who don\xe2\x80\x99t pursue a college\neducation at least graduate from high school with certifications for\ntechnical jobs, such as as mechanics, electricians or welders.\n\n\n\nTaxes\n\n\n\nRubio criticized the country\xe2\x80\x99s current tax system for being unfavorable to\nlarge corporations and small businesses alike, a factor that he said\ncontributes to companies shifting their employees and headquarters overseas.\n\n\n\nHe pledged, if elected president, to make the corporate tax rate\n\xe2\x80\x9ccompetitive\xe2\x80\x9d with the 25 percent average found in other developed\ncountries. He also proposed eliminating tax rules that allow the United\nStates to levy taxes on money that companies earned overseas.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe have a tax code that punishes American companies for competing in the\nglobal economy, and a regulatory system that prevents small businesses \xe2\x80\x93\nthe primary engines of innovation and job creation \xe2\x80\x93 from competing against\nestablished players,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.\n\n\n\nHillary Clinton\n\n\n\nRubio\xe2\x80\x99s speech wasn\xe2\x80\x99t devoid of politics. Amid the policy proposals were\nseveral jabs at Democratic frontrunner Hillary Clinton, whom Rubio\nrepeatedly referred to as a sort of political relic who is too entrenched\nin the old ways of  Washington.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe race for the future will never be won by going backward. It will never\nbe won by hopping in Hillary Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s time machine to yesterday,\xe2\x80\x9d Rubio\nsaid. \xe2\x80\x9cShe seems to believe pumping more of today\xe2\x80\x99s money into yesterday\xe2\x80\x99s\nprograms will bring prosperity tomorrow. It will not.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n*Marco Rubio Outlines Economic Initiatives\n<http://www.wsj.com/articles/marco-rubio-outlines-economic-initiatives-1436289833>\n// WSJ // Patrick O\xe2\x80\x99Connor \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nFlorida Sen. Marco Rubio cast himself Tuesday as \xe2\x80\x9ca new president for a new\nage,\xe2\x80\x9d laying out a series of economic initiatives to boost growth and give\nlower- and middle-income Americans access to the training and education\nneeded to gain a foothold in the 21st-century economy.\n\n\n\nThe Republican candidate outlined the proposals in an economic speech in\nwhich he urged policy makers to help workers overcome challenges presented\nby globalization, the technology revolution that spawned the Internet, and\nthe automation displacing workers in all segments of the economy.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe path to the middle class is narrower today than it has been for\ngenerations, and the American dream so many achieved in the last century is\nin peril,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Rubio said, at a technology hub in Chicago\xe2\x80\x99s Merchandise\nMart where entrepreneurs congregate to work on new ventures. \xe2\x80\x9cIt is not the\nresult of a cyclical economic downturn that will naturally correct itself.\nIt is borne of a fundamental transformation.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nMr. Rubio and several of his GOP rivals have made the economy, particularly\nwage stagnation and the sense that working-class Americans are falling\nbehind, a central theme of their campaigns. Mr. Rubio is using his\nbackground as the son of a bartender and hotel maid to align himself with\npeople who haven\xe2\x80\x99t enjoyed the benefits of the economic recovery.\n\n\n\nSome candidates and their advisers believe the eventual nominee will be the\ncandidate who offers the best recipe to address these concerns.\n\n\n\nCapital Journal is WSJ.com\xe2\x80\x99s home for politics, policy and national\nsecurity news.\n\n\n\nMost of the remedies Mr. Rubio proposed are staples of his economic-policy\nplatform, including plans to reduce corporate tax rates to 25%, curb\nfederal regulations by putting a cap on how much they cost, and allow\ncompanies to bring overseas revenue back to the U.S. without an additional\ntax hit. He also would cut taxes on business investments and give the\npublic more access to the digital spectrum controlled by the federal\ngovernment.\n\n\n\nMr. Rubio, who authored a tax plan with Sen. Mike Lee (R., Utah), would\nleave the top individual tax rate at 35%, unlike some of his GOP rivals.\nNew Jersey Gov. Chris Christie\xe2\x80\x99s top tax rate would be 28%. Kentucky Sen.\nRand Paul has called for scrapping the current tax code and replacing it\nwith a 14.5% flat tax on all income, regardless of how much money a person\nmakes.\n\n\n\nTexas Sen. Ted Cruz, meanwhile, has pledged to abolish the Internal Revenue\nService entirely.\n\n\n\nMany candidates haven\'t yet offered detailed plans, including former\nFlorida Gov. Jeb Bush and former Secretary of State Hillary Clinton, the\nclear favorite for the Democratic nomination.\n\n\n\nA number of prominent conservatives have criticized Mr. Rubio\xe2\x80\x99s tax\nproposals, saying they would add to the deficit unless they were paired\nwith other policy changes to cut federal spending. Others disagree with his\ncalls to expand the child-tax credit, expressing doubt about whether his\n$2,500 credit would spur economic growth.\n\n\n\nOne cornerstone of the speech\xe2\x80\x94and Mr. Rubio\xe2\x80\x99s campaign\xe2\x80\x94was his vow to\nrevamp the higher-education system by expanding access to trade schools and\nfor-profit colleges and making it easier for students to secure federally\nprotected loans.\n\n\n\nOn Tuesday, he promised to \xe2\x80\x9cbust\xe2\x80\x9d the higher-education \xe2\x80\x9ccartel\xe2\x80\x9d dominated\nby \xe2\x80\x9cexisting colleges and universities.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nThe Florida senator also wants to let companies pay for employees\xe2\x80\x99\neducation, invest more in vocational training starting in high school, and\nrequire schools to tell prospective students how much they can expect to\nearn after graduation, depending on the degrees they pursue.\n\n\n\nMr. Rubio took shots at Mrs. Clinton and made veiled swipes at Mr. Bush\xe2\x80\x99s\nfather and brother. The government shouldn\xe2\x80\x99t raise taxes as it did under\nPresidents George H.W. Bush and Bill Clinton, he said, or \xe2\x80\x9cgrow government\xe2\x80\x9d\nlike it did under Jeb Bush\xe2\x80\x99s brother, President George W. Bush.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe race for the future will never be won by going backward,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Rubio\nsaid.\n\n\n\nOn Tuesday, Jeb Bush\xe2\x80\x99s campaign unveiled a new video calling him an\nexecutive who made \xe2\x80\x9ctough decisions\xe2\x80\x9d that spurred job growth and balanced\nthe state\xe2\x80\x99s budget\xe2\x80\x94a not-too-subtle contrast with Mr. Rubio and other\ncurrent and former senators in the race.\n\n\n\n*Rubio rips GOP, Clinton\n<http://www.arkansasonline.com/news/2015/jul/08/rubio-rips-gop-clinton-20150708/>\n// AP // Steve Peoples \xe2\x80\x93 July 8, 2015*\n\n\n\nThe country\xe2\x80\x99s future can\xe2\x80\x99t thrive \xe2\x80\x9cby hopping in Hillary Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s time\nmachine to yesterday,\xe2\x80\x9d Sen. Marco Rubio said Tuesday in Chicago.\n\n\n\nCHICAGO -- Sen. Marco Rubio of Florida, a Republican presidential\ncandidate, called for lower corporate tax rates, looser Internet regulation\nand broader college accreditation in an economic policy speech Tuesday.\n\n\n\nRubio jabbed at fellow Republicans, primarily for letting government grow\nso much in the 2000s, and Democrats, for policies that he said stifle job\ngrowth and "snuff out innovation" -- namely, their push for a higher\nminimum wage and for tax increases on the wealthy.\n\n\n\n"We need in this country a new president for a new age," the Florida\nsenator said from the downtown Chicago offices of a digital startup. The\nnation would be better served, Rubio said, by embracing the "technological\nrevolution."\n\n\n\nThe forward-looking theme of Rubio\'s address mirrors his campaign, which\naims to distinguish him from leading competitors in both parties --\nincluding Republican Jeb Bush and Democrat Hillary Rodham Clinton, whose\nfamilies have been mainstays in American politics for decades.\n\n\n\nHe repeatedly criticized Clinton, the former secretary of state who is\nseeking the Democratic nomination.\n\n\n\n"The race for the future will never be won by going backward," Rubio said.\n"It will never be won by hopping in Hillary Clinton\'s time machine to\nyesterday."\n\n\n\nAnd while not naming Bush, a former Florida governor, Rubio lashed out at\nthe policies enacted when Bush\'s father and brother served in the White\nHouse.\n\n\n\n"We have learned, painfully, that the old ways no longer work -- that\nWashington cannot pretend the world is the same as it was in the 1980s, it\ncannot raise taxes like it did in the \'90s, and it cannot grow government\nlike it did in the 2000s," he said.\n\n\n\nWhile his campaign billed the Chicago speech as a major address, most of\nthe "innovation agenda" he outlined represents policies he has proposed\npreviously.\n\n\n\nRubio called for changes to the tax code that would lower the corporate tax\nrate, establish a "territorial tax system" and allow "immediate, 100\npercent expensing," which would permit businesses to take deductions on\ncapital investments all at once.\n\n\n\nHe previously released a detailed tax plan that would reduce all corporate\ntaxes to 25 percent and cut taxes on business investment.\n\n\n\nRubio also promoted a plan to modernize the national laboratory system in\nline with a proposal he introduced with Sen. Chris Coons, D-Del., earlier\nin the year. And he reiterated his opposition to so-called Net neutrality,\nwhich aims to prevent Internet service providers from setting different\ndownload speeds for different types of content.\n\n\n\nAnd as he often does, Rubio said an immigration overhaul is necessary "to\nprotect American workers and attract more talent to grow our economy and\ncreate jobs."\n\n\n\nOn higher education, Rubio vowed to "bust the cartel" of existing colleges\nand universities by creating a new accreditation process. His campaign said\nRubio would allow lower-cost alternative education providers, such as\nonline academies, to earn accreditation.\n\n\n\nDemocratic National Committee spokesman Holly Shulman said Rubio "continues\nto peddle the same failed Republican policies that cripple the economy and\nsqueeze the middle class."\n\n\n\nRubio, 44, is among more than a dozen candidates seeking the 2016\nRepublican presidential nomination. He is also one of the youngest\ncandidates in the race.\n\n\n\nHe appeared in Chicago hours before he was to begin his first extended\ncampaign swing through an early voting state. He was scheduled to campaign\nin Iowa, the first-in-the-nation caucus state, through Thursday.\n\n\n\n*Marco Rubio Economy: \xe2\x80\x98The old ways no longer work\xe2\x80\x99\n<http://bigstory.ap.org/article/129f5e07bbef4b1db8d0bbc3bf895837/rubio-economy-old-ways-no-longer-work>\n// AP // Steve Peoples \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nWith an eye on the future, Florida Sen. generational themes of his announcement speech three\nmonths ago, Marco Rubio laid out an economic plan Tuesday that sought to\ndistinguish himself as \xe2\x80\x9ca new president for a new Hiking the minimum wage by a few dollars will not save the\nAmerican Dream; it will accelerate automation and outsourcing. Increasing\ntaxes and regulations will not promote fairness or opportunity; it will\nsnuff out innovation and crush small business.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nWhen he turned to higher education, Rubio again slammed Clinton and her\nideas as \xe2\x80\x9coutdated\xe2\x80\x9d and \xe2\x80\x9cshortsighted,\xe2\x80\x9d and he called for breaking up the\nhigher ed \xe2\x80\x9ccartel\xe2\x80\x9d \xe2\x80\x94 he promised a \xe2\x80\x9cholistic overhaul\xe2\x80\x9d of how colleges and\nuniversities control tuition and financial aid, offer instruction and\nprovide degrees.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cOur higher education system is controlled by what amounts to a cartel of\nexisting colleges and universities, which use their power over the\naccreditation process to block innovative, low-cost competitors from\nentering the market,\xe2\x80\x9d Rubio said.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cWithin my first 100 days, I will bust this cartel by establishing a new\naccreditation process that welcomes low-cost, innovative providers. This\nwould expose higher education to the market forces of choice and\ncompetition, which would prompt a revolution driven by the needs of\nstudents \xe2\x80\x94 just as the needs of consumers drive the progress of every other\nindustry in our economy.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nRubio, however, has come under fire for supporting a segment of the higher\neducation system that some see as predatory \xe2\x80\x94 for-profit colleges.
