accused it of lying about\njob placement rates.\n\n\n\nIn a question and answer session following the speech, which took place at\n1871, a digital startup incubator inside the city\xe2\x80\x99s old Merchandise Mart,\nRubio explained that the old measures of economic stability such as the\nunemployment rate are no longer as indicative of the true state of the\nworkforce because so many people are underemployed and others who have jobs\ncontinue to struggle with the skyrocketing cost of child care.\n\n\n\nHe also lamented that so many young people have graduated from college with\nstudent loan debt only to find that their degrees are misaligned with the\nkinds of jobs a rapidly changing economy is creating.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cAll the things we once told people they needed to do to succeed no longer\nwork,\xe2\x80\x9d Rubio said. \xe2\x80\x9cNo one has explained why the old ways no longer work\nand what the new ways should be.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n*Marco Rubio is about to give a major economic speech that he hopes will\nkick-start his campaign\n<http://www.businessinsider.com/r-republican-white-house-contender-rubio-to-deliver-economic-speech-2015-7#ixzz3fGu6OY65>\n// Reuters // James Oliphant \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nPresidential candidate Marco Rubio will deliver an economic speech in\nChicago on Tuesday with the goal of separating himself from the packed\nfield of Republican candidates and kick-starting his campaign into a more\nactive, visible phase.\n\n\n\nRubio, a senator from Florida, has spent much of the last several weeks\neither bogged down in a U.S. Senate preoccupied with a Pacific Rim trade\ndeal or out of the public eye raising money.\n\n\n\nBut after his Chicago speech, Rubio will visit Iowa and then Nevada, both\nof which hold key nominating contests early next year. His campaign says to\nexpect further travel, likely to New Hampshire.\n\n\n\nWith his Cuban-American background, youth and compelling biography, Rubio,\n44, has long been viewed by campaign analysts as one candidate in the\never-growing field of 14 who could break out from the pack.\n\n\n\nAs yet, however, there is little sign of that. State polls in early primary\nstates, save for his home state of Florida, have typically shown Rubio\nstruggling to crack double-digits. A Reuters Ipsos poll showed Rubio\ndrawing support from 9.6 percent of likely Republican primary voters\nnationally - behind former Florida Governor Jeb Bush, the nominal\nfront-runner, and reality show star Donald Trump.\n\n\n\nRubio is expected to use his speech in Chicago to defend his tax-reform\nplan, which has been criticized in conservative circles, and touch upon\nthemes that some economists say sound unusual coming from a Republican\npresidential hopeful.\n\n\n\nRubio has used previous campaign events to discuss the plight of working\nmothers, middle-class families and college students, wading into topics\nthat Democrats often emphasize. He has questioned whether a traditional\ncollege education provides a good bargain for some students who he says\nwould benefit more from skills-based training.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cOnly through an innovative economy can we translate new technologies into\nnew middle-class jobs,\xe2\x80\x9d Rubio will say Tuesday, according to excerpts of\nhis speech released ahead of time, \xe2\x80\x9cand only through a revolutionized\nhigher education system can we equip all our people to fill those jobs.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nJames Pethokoukis, a scholar at the right-leaning American Enterprise\nInstitute, said Rubio deserved credit for trying to develop an agenda that\ngoes beyond criticizing President Barack Obama and the leading Democratic\ncontender, Hillary Clinton.\n\n\n\nBut Pethokoukis, like several conservatives, was critical of Rubio\xe2\x80\x99s tax\nplan, which would simplify the federal tax code and offer new tax credits\nto families with children. Unlike some plans floated by Rubio\'s rivals, his\nplan would not significantly lower the top-tier income tax rates, though it\nwould cut the corporate tax rate.\n\n\n\n*Rubio: College \'cartels\' need busting in new economy\n<http://www.cnn.com/2015/07/07/politics/rubio-higher-education-overhaul/>\n// CNN // Tom LoBianco \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nSen. Marco Rubio says that Americans need to train for a new economy with\nnew skills and that one of the first steps on that path requires busting\nthe university "cartel" that trains students for outdated jobs.\n\n\n\n"Our higher education system is controlled by what amounts to a cartel of\nexisting colleges and universities, which use their power over the\naccreditation process to block innovative, low-cost competitors from\nentering the market," Rubio said. He made his conservative populist pitch\nto technology leaders in Chicago on Tuesday morning, shortly before he\nheads off to Iowa for a three-day campaign swing.\n\n\n\nThe Florida Republican has crafted an image as a younger alternative to\nHillary Clinton -- which he continued Tuesday with jabs at "Clinton\'s time\nmachine to yesterday" -- but also implicitly contrasts himself with another\nfrontrunner, former Florida Gov. Jeb Bush.\n\n\n\nRubio promised that he would change student-lending rules to allow private\ninvestors to pay for individual students to attend college and overhaul how\ncolleges are accredited.\n\n\n\nThe concept of having individual donors fund students is being pushed by\nformer Indiana Gov. Mitch Daniels. Daniels was appointed Purdue University\npresident in 2012 by his appointees to the college\'s board of trustees,\nfollowing an eight-year run in office.\n\n\n\nSince then he has lobbied for sweeping conservative changes in higher\neducation.\n\n\n\nDaniels told Congress in March that students would have to repay the\nprivate loan through a portion of their income, but said that federal\nlegislation would be needed.\n\n\n\nRubio co-sponsored the measure earlier this year which would establish the\nframework for the private donor concept and referenced it again Tuesday\nduring his 20-minute speech.\n\n\n\nCandidates from both parties have been highlighting student debt (and\ncollege costs) as a major problem, but have very different ideas for\ntackling the problem.\n\n\n\nRubio has had his own struggles with student debt, detailed at length in a\nNew York Times investigation of his finances. Rubio started his political\ncareer, after graduating law school, with $150,000 in student loan debt,\nthough he\'s since wiped that out.\n\n\n\n*Marco Rubio\'s \'New\' Plan For Creating Jobs Is Actually Old And Borrowed\n<http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2015/07/07/marco-rubio-jobs_n_7744742.html>\n// HuffPo // Igor Bobic \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015*\n\n\n\nSen. Marco Rubio (R-Fla.) is casting himself as the youthful,\nforward-thinking presidential candidate of the future, a bold reformer\nawash with new ideas on how best to usher in a new American century.\n\n\n\nThe message is an overt criticism of Democratic presidential candidate\nHillary Clinton, who Rubio says offers nothing more than a "time machine to\nyesterday" with a vision he calls "narrow and shortsighted."\n\n\n\nYet many of the Florida Republican\'s own proposals, outlined in a speech he\ndelivered in Chicago on Tuesday, include ideas that Rubio and others have\nput forth before. That\'s not to say that the senator isn\'t bringing\nanything new to the table, but he is also touting his old proposals to draw\na contrast with Clinton and, more implicitly, Republican rival Jeb Bush,\nanother member of a political dynasty.\n\n\n\nRight off the bat, Rubio proposed to "cut our corporate tax rate to be\ncompetitive with the average of 25 percent for developed nations." He\npromised to "establish a territorial tax system," and to "allow immediate,\n100 percent expensing for businesses." And he said he would "put a ceiling\non the amount U.S. regulations" cost the economy through regulatory reform.\n\n\n\nThe proposals are standard fare among lawmakers who have been calling for\ntax reform for years. In 2012, GOP presidential candidates Newt Gingrich\nand Rick Santorum both supported the expensing of business capital.\nHowever, Rubio\'s tax plan, which he introduced with Sen. Mike Lee (R-Utah)\nearlier this year, ran into opposition from an unexpected quarter -- other\nRepublicans. As New York Magazine\'s Jonathan Chait wrote in April, the tax\ncut Rubio proposed is "so gargantuan that nobody in the party actually\nbelieves it."\n\n\n\nThe senator also promised to reallocate more of the government\'s wireless\nspectrum for commercial use by forcing federal agencies to sell their\nfrequencies to the highest bidder. He introduced a bill to do this in the\nSenate last year, attracting some bipartisan support. Congress has debated\nhow to make more of the spectrum more widely available through incentives,\nbut Rubio does appear to be one of the only lawmakers who supports doing so\nforcibly.\n\n\n\nMeanwhile, Rubio said he would reform the nation\'s legal immigration system\n"to make it skill- and merit-based rather than family-based." Immigration\nactivists worry such a focus would break up immigrant families. But the\nidea has roots in the sweeping, bipartisan immigration reform bill passed\nby the Senate that Rubio helped draft in 2013 -- and later renounced after\ntaking heat from conservatives who opposed the bill\'s proposed path to\ncitizenship for undocumented immigrants. The legislation would have created\na merit-based visa program that would score each applicant on criteria such\nas employment status, geographic location and family considerations. It\nwould have also increased the number of merit-based visas and green cards\nissued to keep the highest-skilled workers in the U.S.\n\n\n\nThe second half of Rubio\'s speech on job creation centered on ways to\nreform the country\'s education system. But most of the proposals rehashed\nhis 2014 plan for higher education. The senator promised to bust the higher\neducation "cartel" within his first 100 days in office by introducing\n"choice and competition" into the accreditation process. Rep. Paul Ryan\n(R-Wis.), a former Republican vice presidential nominee, proposed a similar\noverhaul in 2014. Like President Barack Obama, Rubio is also in favor of\nallowing students to get credentials outside of traditional universities\nand colleges.\n\n\n\nRubio said he would "make student loans more manageable by making\nIncome-Based Repayment automatic for all graduates, so the more they make,\nthe faster they pay back their loans; and the less they make, the less\nstrain their loans cause." Former Rep. Tom Petri (R-Wis.) advocated the\nidea of automatic income-based loan repayment as far back as 1983.\n\n\n\nThe Florida senator also said he would expand apprenticeship programs to\n"provide on-the-job training and help standardize skills by allowing\nstudents to learn methods from experienced workers and spread them\nthroughout the industry." Rubio already spoke about expanding apprentice\nprograms last year, and Hillary Clinton called for a tax credit to benefit\ncompanies that hire people as apprentices last month. In his State of the\nUnion address last year, Obama called for similar incentives to expand\napprenticeship programs, and there is currently a bipartisan effort in\nCongress to do so.\n\n\n\nSimilarly, Rubio\'s proposal to require lending institutions to "tell\nstudents how much they can expect to earn with a given degree before they\ntake out the loans to pay for it" already made headlines when he introduced\na bill to do so alongside Sens. Mark R. Warner (D-Va.) and Ron Wyden\n(D-Ore.) in 2013. Ditto for Rubio\'s "Student Investment Plan," which he\nunveiled last year and which would allow students to partner with corporate\ninvestors for tuition relief.\n\n\n\nThe new sheen fooled some news outlets, generating a wave of positive\ncoverage for the candidate on Tuesday. "Marco Rubio has a wild plan to have\ninvestors pay for college and make money off students\' future earnings,"\nread a headline on Business Insider. Such a tactic, if it continues to be\nrewarded, may be just what the candidate needs in order to distinguish\nhimself among a very crowded -- and more experienced -- Republican\npresidential field.\n\n\n\n*Rubio: Don\'t expect a Romney endorsement soon\n<http://thehill.com/blogs/ballot-box/gop-primaries/247076-rubio-dont-expect-a-romney-endorsement-soon>\n// The Hill // Jesse Byrnes \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nWhile Mitt Romney may have become the de facto standard bearer of the\nRepublican Party following his 2012 White House nomination, an endorsement\nfor any 2016 candidate is not on the horizon, Sen. Marco Rubio (R-Fla.)\nsaid Tuesday.\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, I don\'t think that\'s fair to say," Rubio said in interview Tuesday on\nFox Business Network when pressed whether Romney could be expected to\nendorse him.\n\n\n\n"I don\'t suspect Governor Romney will endorse anyone in this race. He\'s\nsomeone I admire. He\'s someone that I like very much," Rubio added.\n\nHost Neil Cavuto questioned Rubio about staying, along with his family, at\nRomney\'s New Hampshire home over the weekend. New Jersey Gov. Chris\nChristie, another 2016 GOP candidate, also stayed there with his family.\n\nWhen Romney ended a brief public flirtation with his own 2016 bid early\nthis year, he suggested that "one of our next generation of Republican\nleaders" would become the nominee, which many interpreted to be an implicit\nnod toward Rubio, now 44, the youngest candidate in the crowded GOP field\nled by former Florida Gov. Jeb Bush, 62.\n\nRomney and Bush reportedly met for lunch Monday with several members of\ntheir families in Maine, though Romney said last month he would likely not\nendorse a 2016 candidate until the Republican nominee is selected.\n\nRubio described conversations at the weekend sleepover as "pretty much\nnon-political" Tuesday, saying of Romney\'s clan, "I wouldn\'t read too much\ninto it. They\'re meeting with other people, and they\'ve been very gracious\nwith others as well."\n\nRomney, after helping many Republicans secure midterm victories last year,\nhas lately turned his attention to helping his party prepare for the\nlengthy 2016 presidential primary process and eventual general election.\n\nDuring an appearance on NBC\'s "Meet the Press" last month, Romney mentioned\nRubio, Bush, Wisconsin Gov. Scott Walker and Ohio Gov. John Kasich by name,\nsaying about a half-dozen candidates could be president.\n\n\n\nWalker and Kasich have not entered the race officially yet, but both are\nexpected to do so soon.\n\nRomney also hosted Rubio, Walker and Kasich at a retreat in Park City,\nUtah, in June.\n\n\n\n*Marco Rubio 2016 Campaign: Nonprofit Backing GOP Candidate Rubio Raises\nAlmost $16 Million\n<http://www.latinpost.com/articles/64620/20150707/marco-rubio-2016-campaign-nonprofit-backing-gop-candidate-raises-16.htm>\n// Latin Post // Andre Puglie \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nA nonprofit backing Marco Rubio has raised almost $16 million, parts of\nwhich the group plans to invest in television advertisements for the\nRepublican Florida senator\'s 2016 White House bid,\n\n\n\nAccording to Politico, The Conservative Solutions Project, which operates\nseparately from Rubio\'s political-action committee, disclosed that it was\non track to reaching its overall fundraising goal of $25 million.\n\n\n\n"With more than $15.8 million raised already, Conservative Solutions\nProject is nearly two-thirds of the way to our overall fundraising goal,"\nthe nonprofit\'s president, Pat Shortridge, said in a statement.\n\nHe added, "These funds will allow us to continue the fight to restore our\nmilitary and our nation\'s role in the world, and given the recent news\nabout the nation\'s stagnant economy, advocate for conservative solutions to\nan inefficient tax code and education reform so all Americans have a chance\nto pursue their dreams."\n\n\n\nConservative Solutions, which has already spent $1 million on television\ncommercials, said on Monday it would boost its advertising campaign to a\ntotal of $3.3 million, according to CNN. Some of the group\'s early spots,\nthe advertisements focused on Rubio\'s attacks on the Obama administration\'s\nproposed nuclear deal with Iran, an issue The New York Times called\n"critical" for some of the most generous GOP donors.\n\nThe group\'s announcement reveals that Rubio is "the biggest beneficiary so\nfar of a new and largely untested means for moving unlimited cash into\npresidential primary campaigns," The New York Times noted.\n\n\n\nMeanwhile, the Conservative Solutions Project is taking care of many\nactivities typically carried out by a formal presidential campaign, and\nthat includes what the paper called "extensive research on the Republican\nprimary electorate."\n\n\n\nSupporters of other contenders in the increasingly crowded field for the\nRepublican nomination -- including former Florida Gov. Jeb Bush, former\nTexas Gov. Rick Perry, Louisiana Gov. Bobby Jindal and former Arkansas Gov.\nMike Huckabee -- have set up similar groups and used them as "de facto\ncampaigns prior to their kickoff events," CNN noted.\n\n\n\n*Nonprofit with secret donors, linked to Rubio super PAC, raises millions\n<http://www.cbsnews.com/news/nonprofit-with-secret-donors-linked-to-rubio-super-pac-raises-millions/>\n// CBS News // Stephanie Condon \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nA relatively new nonprofit -- with the same name as a pro-Marco Rubio super\nPAC -- has raised nearly $16 million to spend on issue-related ads in the\n2016 election, the New York Times reports.\n\n\n\nThe robust fundraising haul illustrates how 2016 presidential candidates\nlike Rubio may benefit from the new crop of secretive nonprofits that are\nplaying a growing role in elections, thanks to a series of relatively\nrecent court rulings.\n\n\n\nThe organization Conservative Solutions Project has already spent $3.3\nmillion on television and radio advertising, the Times reports, focusing on\nRubio\'s attacks of the Obama administration\'s Iran nuclear negotiations.\nHowever, the group told the Times that it\'s not devoted to any particular\ncandidate.\n\n\n\nAs a tax-exempt "social welfare" organization -- in the 501(c)(4) category\n-- the group is allowed to spend unlimited sums of money on politics as\nlong as politics isn\'t its main focus. That\'s why its advertising will be\nlargely "issue based."\n\n\n\nIn most cases, these "social welfare" nonprofits aren\'t required to name\ntheir donors. A spokesman for Conservative Solutions Project told the Times\nit is unlikely to publicly name its donors.\n\n\n\nThe secretive nature of these groups has created the potential for\ncorruption, several public advocacy groups and politicians have argued.\nWhile Congress hasn\'t done much about the rise of these "dark money"\ngroups, leaders at the state level -- both Democrats and Republicans -- are\ntrying to rein them in.\n\n\n\n*Marco Rubio: \xe2\x80\x9cWe need a new president for a new age\xe2\x80\x9d\n<http://www.cbsnews.com/news/marco-rubio-we-need-a-new-president-for-a-new-age/>\n// CBS News // Sopan Deb \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nFlorida Sen. Marco Rubio pitched himself as the presidential candidate of\nthe future in a speech Tuesday, arguing he\'s better equipped than his\nrivals to govern a rapidly transforming and innovating America.\n\n\n\nRubio\'s choice of venue for the speech - his first major domestic policy\naddress since he announced his presidential campaign - was no accident. He\nspoke at 1871, an incubator for digital start-ups in Chicago.\n\n\n\n187s is a hub of "digital innovation," Rubio said -- an organization at the\nforefront of what the senator referred to as today\'s "technological\nrevolution." Among the apps that have sprung from 1871: Spot Hero - an app\nthat helps you find parking right away and Options Away, which allows\npassengers to hold a flight at a certain price without actually booking it.\nOne of Rubio\'s GOP primary rivals, Kentucky Sen. Rand Paul, spoke at the\norganization in the spring.\n\n\n\nIn his speech, Rubio, the second-youngest candidate in the GOP field at 43\nyears old, framed himself as the human embodiment of 1871 -- the only\npresidential candidate in the field with the perspective needed to lead the\ncountry in the 21st century. Even the title of the speech -- "Jobs For A\nNew American Century" -- hinted at Rubio\'s forward-looking message.\n\n\n\n"For the first fifteen and a half years of this century, Washington has\nlooked to the past," Rubio said. "Our economy has changed, but our economic\npolicies have not. And we have learned, painfully, that the old ways no\nlonger work - that Washington cannot pretend the world is the same as it\nwas in the \'80s, it cannot raise taxes like it did in the \'90s, and it\ncannot grow government like it did in the 2000s."\n\n\n\n"We need a new president for a new age," he added. "One with original ideas\nto unlock the two great doors to the future: the doors of innovation and\neducation."\n\n\n\nMuch of the speech laid out his platform on the economy and education.\n\n\n\nRubio proposed cutting the corporate tax rate to make the U.S. "competitive\nwith the average of 25 percent for developed nations." He called for\nestablishing a "territorial tax system," which he said would bring money\nback to the economy held overseas by companies not wanting to be taxed on\nforeign income. Critics allege that territorial taxing would encourage\ncompanies to increase capital abroad, which would then lower wages back\nhome.\n\n\n\nRubio cited several specific technologies on the horizon - self-driving\ncars, virtual reality, robotics - but said that we have "quite nearly the\nexact opposite" of a business-friendly economy. He noted that U.S.\ncorporate taxes are the highest in the developed world -- a claim that\nfact-checking organization Politifact has rated mostly true. The U.S. has\nthe highest statutory tax rate and the second highest effective rate, among\nadvanced industrialized nations.\n\n\n\nAt one point, Rubio managed to get a laugh from the 100 or so attendees in\nthe audience (some sporting Marco Rubio t-shirts) by joking that\nself-driving cars would be great for him, considering recent news reports.\nIt was a clear nod to a recent New York Times piece that explored his\nfamily\'s checkered driving history.\n\n\n\nIn his single reference to immigration policy, Rubio called for a shift to\na system based on merit - designed to attract the world\'s best and\nbrightest workers - rather than a system based on familial relations. He\ndid not mention his past support for a comprehensive immigration bill that\nincludes a path to citizenship -- a stance that has earned plaudits from\nimmigrant and Latino groups but one that has put him at odds with most of\nthe rest of the Republican primary field.\n\n\n\nOn the subject of education, Rubio proposed tackling the growing problem of\nhigher education debt by making income-based repayment automatic for all\ngraduates. He wasn\'t clear on whether this would include only federal\nloans. He also raised the idea of Student Investment Plans, which would\nallow investors to pay the cost of tuition for students and then take a cut\nof the students\' salary after college.\n\n\n\nHe didn\'t target any of his Republican primary opponents by name, but\nfocused his criticism on Democratic frontrunner Hillary Clinton.\n\n\n\n"The race for the future will never be won by going backward," Rubio said.\n"It will never be won by hopping in Hillary Clinton\'s time machine to\nyesterday. She seems to believe pumping more of today\'s money into\nyesterday\'s programs will bring prosperity tomorrow."\n\n\n\nRubio called for expanding access to vocational schools as early as high\nschool -- a proposal on which he and Clinton might be able to find common\nground. Last year, at Arizona State University, Clinton called for the\ncountry to "get back to really respecting vocational and technical work."\n\n\n\nThe Senator raced off to Iowa after the speech for a busy couple days of\ncampaigning. The trip marks Rubio\'s third visit to Iowa, site of the\nnation\'s first presidential nominating contest, in 2015.\n\n\n\nOf his previous two trips, one occurred after he announced his candidacy\nand one came in February on a book tour. Rubio\'s first event in Iowa this\ntime will occur in Des Moines at the Exile Brewing Company. He\'ll hold a\nhappy hour with the Bull Moose Club, a forum for Iowa Republicans under the\nage of 40, and he\'s hoping he\'ll find a receptive audience for his message\nabout the generational divide.\n\n\n\nOf the GOP\'s 2016 candidates, only retired neurosurgeon Ben Carson and\nformer Pennsylvania Sen. Rick Santorum have addressed the group thus far\nthis cycle.\n\n\n\n*Marco Rubio\xe2\x80\x99s Economic Plan Calls For Students To Sell Themselves To\nPrivate Investors\n<http://thinkprogress.org/election/2015/07/07/3677543/marco-rubios-economic-plan-calls-students-sell-private-investors/>\n// Think Progress // Alice Ollstein \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nFlorida Senator and Republican presidential candidate Marco Rubio described\nhis economic platform in a speech Tuesday in Chicago, touching on well-worn\nGOP priorities including slashing corporate taxes from 35 to 25 percent,\nfurther deregulating the private sector, restricting family immigration,\nand resisting calls to raise the minimum wage. Taking several specific\nshots at Democratic frontrunner Hillary Clinton, Rubio said his plan would\navoid \xe2\x80\x9cpumping more of today\xe2\x80\x99s money into yesterday\xe2\x80\x99s programs,\xe2\x80\x9d and bring\nthe U.S. into the future.\n\n\n\nIn the speech, Rubio also called for a \xe2\x80\x9crevolutionized\xe2\x80\x9d higher education\nsystem. If elected president, he promised to \xe2\x80\x9cbust\xe2\x80\xa6the cartel of existing\ncolleges and universities\xe2\x80\x9d by loosening the rules for accreditation so that\n\xe2\x80\x9cinnovative, low-cost competitors\xe2\x80\x9d can court students. But critics say the\ngovernment accreditation process is already far too loose, allowing\npredatory for-profit chains like Corinthian Colleges to win federal\napproval and funding even as they mislead students into paying for\nessentially worthless degrees.\n\n\n\nHe also touted the \xe2\x80\x9cStudent Right to Know Before You Go Act\xe2\x80\x9d he\nco-sponsored with Oregon Democrat Ron Wyden \xe2\x80\x94 a plan extremely similar to\none President Obama pushed for last year that ranks colleges by how much\ntheir tuition costs and how much money their graduates make.\n\n\n\nLamenting the \xe2\x80\x9cshadow of debt hovering over millions of graduates,\xe2\x80\x9d Rubio\nthen proposed a model already suggested by his rival Governor Chris\nChristie (R-NJ): allowing rich individuals or hedge funds to pay a students\ntuition and collect their investment back post-graduation.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt may result in a profit for the investor or it may not \xe2\x80\x93 but unlike with\nloans, none of the risk lies with the student,\xe2\x80\x9d Rubio said.\n\n\n\nHe expanded on this idea in a speech last year:\n\n\n\nLet\xe2\x80\x99s say you are a student who needs $10,000 to pay for your last year of\nschool. Instead of taking this money out in the form of a loan, you could\napply for a \xe2\x80\x9cStudent Investment Plan\xe2\x80\x9d from an approved and certified\nprivate investment group. In short, these investors would pay your $10,000\ntuition in return for a percentage of your income for a set period of time\nafter graduation \xe2\x80\x93 let\xe2\x80\x99s say, for example, 4% a year for 10 years.\n\n\n\nThis group would look at factors such as your major, the institution you\xe2\x80\x99re\nattending, your record in school \xe2\x80\x93 and use this to make a determination\nabout the likelihood of you finding a good job and paying them back.\n\n\n\nUnlike with loans, you would be under no legal obligation to pay back that\nentire $10,000. Your only obligation would be to pay that 4% of your income\nper year for 10 years, regardless of whether that ends up amounting to more\nor less than $10,000.\n\nBut these \xe2\x80\x9cStudent Investment Plans,\xe2\x80\x9d which also have the Orwellian name\n\xe2\x80\x9chuman capital contracts,\xe2\x80\x9d raise many serious concerns. For one, investors\nmay refuse to cover entire fields of students not likely to bring in the\nbig bucks after graduation, or would charge them a staggeringly high\npercentage of their income. For those backing this plan, such as the\nconservative think tank American Enterprise Institute (AEI), this poses no\nproblem.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cIsn\xe2\x80\x99t this \xe2\x80\x98unfair\xe2\x80\x99 to those wanting to be librarians, teachers, social\nworkers, etc., since they would have to forego more of their incomes to\nsatisfy the human capital contract? Not really,\xe2\x80\x9d writes AEI Adjunct Scholar\nRichard Vedder. \xe2\x80\x9cSociety puts a relatively low value on those jobs.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nAdditionally, following Rubio\xe2\x80\x99s math of 4 percent over 10 years, a graduate\nwould have to earn an extremely low salary for the investor not to make a\nprofit. Vedder and other advocates of the plan are less cautious, and have\nvoiced support for plans that take as high as 25 percent of a graduates\nsalary for multiple decades after they enter the workforce.\n\n\n\nThe National College Access Network and other groups have warned that such\na plan could cost students even more than high-interest federal loan\nprograms, diverting away money those graduates could have used to save for\nretirement or buy a house.\n\n\n\nRubio\xe2\x80\x99s proposal is similar to the \xe2\x80\x9cPay It Forward, Pay It Back\xe2\x80\x9d model\ncurrently being explored by the state of Oregon \xe2\x80\x94 with one crucial\ndifference. In Oregon\xe2\x80\x99s plan, the investor is the democratically-elected\nstate government, so when graduates repay their loans that money can go\nback into public education. Under Rubio\xe2\x80\x99s version, the money would go into\nthe pockets of investors.\n\n\n\n*Marco Rubio Outlines Domestic Policy Agenda, Jabs Clinton\n<http://www.nbcnews.com/politics/2016-election/marco-rubio-outlines-domestic-policy-agenda-jabs-clinton-n387996>\n// NBC News // Alex Jaffe \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nIn his first domestic policy-focused speech since announcing his bid for\npresident, Florida Sen. Marco Rubio on Tuesday outlined his vision for tax\nand higher education reform to usher in a "New American Century" marked by\ninnovation and prosperity.\n\n\n\nThe GOP presidential candidate told the audience at a digital startup\nco-working space in Chicago that while the future may look bleak today, his\nproposals would ensure America remains competitive globally.\n\n\n\nAnd he took direct aim at Democratic presidential front-runner Hillary\nClinton, framing her as a backward-looking foil to his forward-focused\nagenda.\n\n\n\n"The race for the future will never be won by going backward. It will never\nbe won by hopping in Hillary Clinton\'s time machine to yesterday," Rubio\ntold the crowd. "She seems to believe pumping more of today\'s money into\nyesterday\'s programs will bring prosperity tomorrow."\n\n\n\nThe Florida senator said technological innovation and globalization has\ncreated a situation in which "the path to the middle class is narrower\ntoday than it has been for generations, and the American Dream so many\nachieved in the last century is in peril."\n\n\n\nHigher-education "cartels" are a key inhibitor of upward mobility, he said,\npledging to overhaul the system in the first 100 days of his presidency by\n"establishing a new accreditation process that welcomes low-cost,\ninnovative providers."\n\n\n\nA President Rubio would also require schools to tell students how much they\ncan expect to earn from their degrees, and expand access to career and\nvocational schools as well as apprenticeship programs for training on the\njob.\n\n\n\nIn his remarks, he outlined a broad array of domestic reforms, from an\noverhaul of the business tax code to reforming the legal immigration system\nto bring in more high-skilled workers.\n\n\n\nHe argued in particular against raising the minimum wage, which he said\n"will accelerate automation and outsourcing" rather than improve the\nquality of life for Americans.\n\n\n\nInstead, Rubio proposes cutting the corporate tax rate to be competitive\nwith the average 25 percent rate for developed countries, creating a\n"territorial tax system" to prevent businesses from being taxed twice on\nprofits, and allowing businesses to take deductions on 100 percent of the\nfunds they invest back into business development and employee wages.\n\n\n\nHe also called for "reforming our legal immigration system to make it\nskill- and merit-based rather than family-based, which will protect\nAmerican workers and attract more talent to grow our economy and create\njobs."\n\n\n\nThe speech marked Rubio\'s reemergence on the campaign trail after weeks\nspent bogged down in Senate business on Capitol Hill and fundraising jaunts\nacross the nation. Rubio\'s campaign has yet to announce how much the\naggressive fundraising schedule earned his campaign, although a key outside\ngroup backing him announced Monday that it has raised $15.8 million to\ndate. In the latest NBC News/Wall Street Journal poll, 14 percent of\nRepublican primary voters identified him as their first choice for the\nnomination, placing him behind rivals Jeb Bush and Scott Walker.\n\n\n\nBut the speech, along with his campaign swing through Iowa and Nevada in\nthe coming days, is meant to catapult him back into the race and again\nhighlight what Rubio\'s aides and allies see as his greatest asset -- his\nyouthful appeal and unique personal narrative, in a field of older GOP\ncandidates.\n\n\n\n*PAUL*\n\n\n\n*Rand Paul, dorm room philosopher: Why his \xe2\x80\x9cslavery\xe2\x80\x9d nonsense is so\noutrageous\n<http://www.salon.com/2015/07/07/rand_paul_dorm_room_philosopher_why_his_slavery_nonsense_is_so_outrageous/>\n// Salon // Simon Maloy \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015*\n\n\n\nPresidential candidate Sen. Rand Paul has a tax plan he\xe2\x80\x99d like to sell you\non. The plan, which would put in place a 14.5 percent flat tax, was crafted\nwith the input of some of the wrongest people in the conservative economic\npolicy world, and it would redistribute wealth up the economic ladder while\ntossing a bone or two to the people at the bottom. But Rand is proud of it\nnonetheless, mainly because he thinks it\xe2\x80\x99s less slavery-like than your\naverage tax scheme.\n\n\n\nHere\xe2\x80\x99s what Paul said last week about taxation and \xe2\x80\x9cfreedom,\xe2\x80\x9d as reported\nby BuzzFeed:\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cNow you can have some government, we all need government,\xe2\x80\x9d the Kentucky\nsenator said while discussing Thomas Paine and the role of government at\nthe local public library. \xe2\x80\x9cThomas Paine said that government is a necessary\nevil. What did he mean by that?\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nPaul said he believes that \xe2\x80\x9cyou have to give up some of your liberty to\nhave government,\xe2\x80\x9d saying he was \xe2\x80\x9cfor some government.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m for paying some taxes,\xe2\x80\x9d continued Paul. \xe2\x80\x9cBut if we tax you at 100%\nthen you\xe2\x80\x99ve got zero percent liberty. If we tax you at 50% you are half\nslave, half free. I frankly would like to see you a little freer and a\nlittle more money remaining in your communities so you can create jobs.\nIt\xe2\x80\x99s a debate we need to have.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nThat was his big pitch \xe2\x80\x93 The Rand Paul tax plan: Only 14.5 percent slavery!\n\n\n\nThis is a dumb argument. And it\xe2\x80\x99s upsetting to hear this dumb argument\ncoming from someone who is trying to be president, but will go back to\nwriting and approving legislation if/when that doesn\xe2\x80\x99t work out. Taxation\nis not tantamount to slavery. The only thing that\xe2\x80\x99s comparable to slavery\nis actual slavery. You might not like it that a portion of your paycheck is\nsent to the feds and your state government, and you may disagree with how\nyour tax dollars are spent, but that is in no way comparable to being kept\nin bondage and having the fruits of your labor stolen from you.\n\n\n\nAny way you look at this argument, it\xe2\x80\x99s bad. When you\xe2\x80\x99ve staked out the\nposition that your effective tax rate is how you measure one\xe2\x80\x99s slave\nstatus, then you\xe2\x80\x99re arguing that a progressive tax structure means rich\npeople are less free than the lucky poor folks who would see a smaller\npercentage of their income go to the government. By this reading, a hedge\nfund billionaire who moves his assets offshore to avoid paying taxes is\nbasically Frederick Douglass. And when you refer to something as slavery,\nhow can you then make the case that there is an acceptable threshold for\nit? Why should 14.5 percent slavery be any more tolerable than 100 percent\nslavery?\n\n\n\nIt gets even worse when you remember that Rand Paul is trying to make\ninroads with black voters and repair his party\xe2\x80\x99s abysmally bad reputation\nwith African-Americans. Rand obviously understands at a certain level that\nslavery was a uniquely horrific crime, the memory of which still haunts our\npolitics. After the shootings in Charleston last month, Paul called for the\nConfederate flag to be removed from grounds of the South Carolina Capitol\nbecause \xe2\x80\x9cto every African-American in the country it\xe2\x80\x99s a symbolism of\nslavery to them and now it\xe2\x80\x99s a symbol of murder to this young man.\xe2\x80\x9d Here we\nare, just a couple of weeks later, and he\xe2\x80\x99s comparing the grotesque human\nrights violations represented by that flag to the banal act of filing your\nannual tax return.\n\n\n\nAnd this isn\xe2\x80\x99t Rand Paul\xe2\x80\x99s first foray into comparing policies he disagrees\nwith to slavery. In 2011, during a Senate hearing, he said that a \xe2\x80\x9cright to\nhealthcare\xe2\x80\x9d would, in effect, make slaves out of doctors such as himself:\n\n\n\nWith regard to the idea whether or not you have a right to health care you\nhave to realize what that implies. I am a physician. You have a right to\ncome to my house and conscript me. It means you believe in slavery. You are\ngoing to enslave not only me but the janitor at my hospital, the person who\ncleans my office, the assistants, the nurses. \xe2\x80\xa6 You are basically saying\nyou believe in slavery.\n\n\n\nOn the flip side of the \xe2\x80\x9cslavery\xe2\x80\x9d argument, Paul argued earlier this year\nthat the vaccination of children was \xe2\x80\x9can issue of freedom,\xe2\x80\x9d essentially\nsaying that parents should be free to have their kids be vectors for the\ncommunication of dangerous disease. (Before he was elected to the Senate,\nPaul went on Alex Jones\xe2\x80\x99 radio show and warned that mandatory vaccinations\nwere a precursor to martial law.)\n\n\n\nRand\xe2\x80\x99s been espousing this strain of dorm-room libertarianism for quite\nsome time, reducing complex policy issues to black-and-white questions of\n\xe2\x80\x9cfreedom\xe2\x80\x9d and \xe2\x80\x9cslavery.\xe2\x80\x9d He and others like him who carp on the slavery of\ntaxes and the tyranny of public health promotion are an obvious source of\nfrustration to other libertarians who would very much prefer that the\npublic faces of the \xe2\x80\x9cLibertarian Moment\xe2\x80\x9d stop making asses of themselves by\ncheapening the horror of America\xe2\x80\x99s slave past.\n\n\n\n*CRUZ*\n\n\n\n*Blogging Federal Judge Says Ted Cruz \xe2\x80\x98Not Fit to be President\xe2\x80\x99\n<http://blogs.wsj.com/law/2015/07/07/blogging-federal-judge-says-ted-cruz-not-fit-to-be-president/>\n// WSJ // Jacob Gershman \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nRepublican presidential candidate Ted Cruz raised eyebrows with his idea of\ngiving voters the power to oust Supreme Court justices from the bench.\n\n\n\nOne federal judge says he\xe2\x80\x99s so offended by the Texas senator\xe2\x80\x99s proposal\nthat he thinks it should disqualify him from the White House.\n\n\n\nThat\xe2\x80\x99s the opinion of U.S. District Judge Richard Kopf of Nebraska, a\npart-time blogger who has attracted his own share of controversy.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cMr. Cruz seeks to sacrifice the Supreme Court upon the altar of an extreme\nright-wing ideology. That makes him unsuited to become President,\xe2\x80\x9d wrote\nJudge Kopf on his personal blog, \xe2\x80\x9cHercules and the Umpire.\xe2\x80\x9d He titled his\npost, \xe2\x80\x9cSenator Ted Cruz is not fit to be President.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nHe was responding to Mr. Cruz\xe2\x80\x99s proposal for a constitutional amendment\nthat would end life tenure for Supreme Court justices and force the\njustices to face periodic judicial-retention elections to keep their jobs.\nThe Harvard-educated Texas senator, who once clerked for Chief Justice\nWilliam Rehnquist, said the court\xe2\x80\x99s recent rulings on Obamacare and gay\nmarriage rulings were examples of lawless judicial activism that retention\nelections would help to cure.\n\n\n\nRick Tyler, a spokesman for Mr. Cruz\xe2\x80\x99s campaign, took issue with Judge\nKopf\xe2\x80\x99s characterization of the senator\xe2\x80\x99s ideology.  In a statement emailed\nto Law Blog on Tuesday, he said:\n\n\n\nSenator Cruz cares deeply about The Supreme Court\xe2\x80\xa6He respects and admires\nmany of the Justices, some are his friends. He did not come to his\nconclusion about retention elections lightly. Quite the opposite. He wrote\na thoughtful essay on why he believed it was necessary. He understands and\nrespects why some would disagree. But what evidence does the judge offer to\nback up his assertion of \xe2\x80\x9cextreme right-wing ideology\xe2\x80\x9d? Or is he accustomed\nto render his verdicts without substantiation.\n\n\n\nOver at Volokh Conspiracy, attorney and law professor Orin Kerr wonders\nwhether Judge Kopf crossed a line:\n\n\n\nWhatever one thinks of the substance of Kopf\xe2\x80\x99s argument \xe2\x80\x94 both as to the\nproposal and the candidate \xe2\x80\x94 I\xe2\x80\x99m more interested in the ethical questions\nit raises. Canon 5 of the Code of Conduct for Federal Judges states:\n\n\n\nA judge should not . . . publicly endorse or oppose a candidate for public\noffice[.]\n\n\n\nDoes calling a candidate for public office \xe2\x80\x9cunfit\xe2\x80\x9d and \xe2\x80\x9cdemonstrably\nunsuited\xe2\x80\x9d for that office amount to \xe2\x80\x9coppos[ing] a candidate for public\noffice\xe2\x80\x9d?\n\n\n\nJudge Kopf responded to Mr. Kerr, saying he had a legal right to express\nthat opinion:\n\n\n\nFor me, it is enough to state that I did not label Senator Cruz unfit to\nserve in order to oppose his candidacy for political or partisan purposes\nbut rather to demolish and protect us all from his intemperate legal\nattacks on the Supreme Court. I remind you that I am not registered to\nvote, and I have not been registered to vote since I became a judge in\n1987. My comment on his legal fitness was inextricably intertwined with my\nright to speak publicy on legal matters and the administration of justice.\nThat said you are correct that I skated close to thin ice.\n\n\n\n*Blogging judge calls political candidate \xe2\x80\x9cunfit\xe2\x80\x9d for office\n<https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/volokh-conspiracy/wp/2015/07/07/blogging-judge-calls-political-candidate-unfit-for-office/>\n// WSJ // Orin Kerr \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nU.S. District Judge Richard Kopf is no stranger to controversy. At his\npersonal blog, Hercules and the Umpire, Judge Kopf has over time shared his\nsomewhat intemperate criticism of the Supreme Court, other judges,\nCongress, and lawyers practicing before him. His posts have generated no\nshortage of national press attention.\n\n\n\nIn a recent post, Kopf may have added another controversial notch to his\nblogging belt by proclaiming a political candidate \xe2\x80\x9cnot fit\xe2\x80\x9d for office. In\nresponse to recent Supreme Court decisions, Sen. Ted Cruz (R-Tex.) has\nproposed a constitutional amendment that would require Supreme Court\njustices to face periodic retention elections. Judge Kopf argues that\nCruz\xe2\x80\x99s attack on lifetime tenure reveals Cruz as \xe2\x80\x9ca right-wing ideologue\xe2\x80\x9d\nwho \xe2\x80\x9cis demonstrably unfit to become President.\xe2\x80\x9d In Kopf\xe2\x80\x99s view, it\xe2\x80\x99s\nobvious that lifetime tenure for federal judges is better than a system of\nretention elections. To argue otherwise would \xe2\x80\x9csacrifice the Supreme Court\nupon the altar of an extreme right-wing ideology.\xe2\x80\x9d \xe2\x80\x9c[A]s a federal judge,\xe2\x80\x9d\nKopf writes, that gives him \xe2\x80\x9cthe right . . . and dare I say the duty, to\nrespond to the proposal.\xe2\x80\x9d Cruz\xe2\x80\x99s proposal is so bad, Kopf reasons, that it\nmakes Cruz \xe2\x80\x9cunsuited to become President.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nWhatever one thinks of the substance of Kopf\xe2\x80\x99s argument \xe2\x80\x94 both as to the\nproposal and the candidate \xe2\x80\x94 I\xe2\x80\x99m more interested in the ethical questions\nit raises. Canon 5 of the Code of Conduct for Federal Judges states:\n\n\n\nA judge should not . . . publicly endorse or oppose a candidate for public\noffice[.]\n\n\n\nDoes calling a candidate for public office \xe2\x80\x9cunfit\xe2\x80\x9d and \xe2\x80\x9cdemonstrably\nunsuited\xe2\x80\x9d for that office amount to \xe2\x80\x9coppos[ing] a candidate for public\noffice\xe2\x80\x9d?\n\n\n\nIn response to commenter who raises this concern, Judge Kopf argues that he\ndid not violate Canon 5 because he was merely exercising his right to\ncomment on public matters:\n\n\n\nFor me, it is enough to state that I did not label Senator Cruz unfit to\nserve in order to oppose his candidacy for political or partisan purposes\nbut rather to demolish and protect us all from his intemperate legal\nattacks on the Supreme Court. I remind you that I am not registered to\nvote, and I have not been registered to vote since I became a judge in\n1987. My comment on his legal fitness was inextricably intertwined with my\nright to speak publicy on legal matters and the administration of justice.\nThat said you are correct that I skated close to thin ice.\n\n\n\nHe adds:\n\n\n\nIf Senator\xe2\x80\x99s Cruz\xe2\x80\x99s legal proposition was beyond the pale, and I have the\nright under the Code of Conduct to write on legal subjects, why is that I\nam prohibited from concluding that his legal assertions disqualify him from\npublic office? It seems to me that the two things are inextricably linked.\nI find it impossible to honestly separate the speaker from the speech in\nthis instance.\n\n\n\nAnd further:\n\n\n\nI might add that I stand by views after serving six years on the Judicial\nConference\xe2\x80\x99s Codes of Conduct Committee. That hardly makes me right, but it\ndoes reflect a serious study of the Code of the Conduct for United States\nJudges.\n\n\n\nHas Kopf skated close to thin ice, as he says, or has he skated over it and\nfallen through? Kopf was of course free to comment on the merits of Cruz\xe2\x80\x99s\nproposal. (For what it\xe2\x80\x99s worth, I agree that Cruz\xe2\x80\x99s proposal is a bad idea;\nI personally favor 18-year terms for Justices.) But I would think that the\nethical line is actually pretty clear. The ethics canons allow judges to\npublicly oppose a reform proposal but do not allow them to publicly oppose\na candidate for public office. The two may be related from the perspective\nof voters, as presumably they would want to vote against a candidate with\nbad ideas. Or at least they would weigh a bad idea against a candidate when\nthey decide who among the candidates in the race they should support. But I\ndon\xe2\x80\x99t think the two are intertwined for the judges who have to follow the\nethics canons.\n\n\n\nOr so it seems to me. I\xe2\x80\x99d be interested to know whether others agree or\ndisagree.\n\n\n\nUPDATE: Judge Kopf elaborates a bit on his position in the comment thread\nto his post:\n\n\n\n[W]hen a man of Senator Cruz\xe2\x80\x99s education and experience calls for a radical\nand fundamental attack on the Supreme Court he is not acting in political\nterms. If he is really serious about the amendment he is a threat to the\njudiciary that I love and respect and have devoted much of my life to\nserving. Therefore, his unfitness is a function of his threat to our\nConstitutional form of government\xe2\x80\x93it is in that sense that he is acting in\nan extra-political manner and that extra-political action entitles me to\ntake the public position that I have taken about his unfitness.\n\n\n\nThis reads like an explanation of why it\xe2\x80\x99s worth it to violate Canon 5\nrather than why it\xe2\x80\x99s not a violation in the first place.\n\n\n\nANOTHER UPDATE: In a new comment thread, Judge Kopf argues that he did not\nviolate Canon 5 at all. He writes, with emphasis in the original:\n\n\n\nI neither publicly endorsed nor publicly opposed Mr. Cruz for a public\noffice. Rather, I wrote that Senator Cruz \xe2\x80\x9cwas unfit.\xe2\x80\x9d \xe2\x80\x9cOppose\xe2\x80\x9d is a verb.\n\xe2\x80\x9cUnfit\xe2\x80\x9d is an adjective. While the words are similar, they are not in any\nsense the same.\n\n\n\nI appreciate the response, but I don\xe2\x80\x99t get this as an argument. First, I\ndon\xe2\x80\x99t think it takes a specific verb to oppose someone. Second, when you\nsay someone is \xe2\x80\x9cunfit for public office,\xe2\x80\x9d I have always understood that to\nmean \xe2\x80\x9cshould not be in public office.\xe2\x80\x9d I don\xe2\x80\x99t see how you can say someone\nshould not be in public office without opposing them for that office.\nThird, in defending his position Kopf also wrote:\n\n\n\nIf Senator\xe2\x80\x99s Cruz\xe2\x80\x99s legal proposition was beyond the pale, and I have the\nright under the Code of Conduct to write on legal subjects, why is that I\nam prohibited from concluding that his legal assertions disqualify him from\npublic office? It seems to me that the two things are inextricably linked.\nI find it impossible to honestly separate the speaker from the speech in\nthis instance.\n\n\n\nI read that as Judge Kopf saying that Cruz\xe2\x80\x99s views \xe2\x80\x9cdisqualify him from\npublic office.\xe2\x80\x9d I don\xe2\x80\x99t see how you can argue that a politician\xe2\x80\x99s views\n\xe2\x80\x9cdisqualify him from public office\xe2\x80\x9d without also opposing that politician\xe2\x80\x99s\nbid to the office.\n\n\n\n*Ted Cruz\'s angry allies\n<http://www.politico.com/story/2015/07/ted-cruzs-angry-allies-119827.html>\n// Politico // Katie Glueck \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nTed Cruz has methodically built a roster of state leaders to help him fire\nup social conservatives in the South. But\nat a state level, among those who oppose taking the flag down, \xe2\x80\x9cI just hate\nthat they\xe2\x80\x99re missing an opportunity \xe2\x80\x94 they\xe2\x80\x99re all missing an opportunity \xe2\x80\x94\nto stand with their brothers and sisters in the faith.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n*Ted Cruz partners with donor\xe2\x80\x99s \'psychographic\' firm\n<http://www.politico.com/story/2015/07/ted-cruz-donor-for-data-119813.html>\n// Politico // Kenneth Vogel & Tarini Parti \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nTed Cruz\xe2\x80\x99s presidential effort is working closely with a little-known\ncompany owned by one of his biggest donors that uses non-traditional\n\xe2\x80\x9cpsychographic\xe2\x80\x9d analyses of voters to try to win them over with narrowly\ntargeted micro-messages, POLITICO has learned.\n\n\n\nThe company, Cambridge Analytica, has sent staff to Cruz\xe2\x80\x99s campaign\nheadquarters in Houston to help set up an intensive data analysis operation.\n\n\n\nCambridge Analytica is connected to a British firm called SCL Group that\nprovides governments, political groups and companies around the world with\nservices ranging from military disinformation campaigns to social media\nbranding and voter targeting.\n\n\n\nSo far, SCL\xe2\x80\x99s political work has been mostly in the developing world \xe2\x80\x93\nwhere it has boasted of its ability to help foment coups. Cambridge\nAnalytica only entered the competitive U.S. political data market last year.\n\n\n\nCambridge Analytica is owned at least in part by the family of the press\nshy New York hedge fund manager Robert Mercer, multiple sources confirmed\nto POLITICO. The Mercers this year provided the lion\xe2\x80\x99s share of the $37\nmillion raised by a quartet of unlimited money super PACs supporting Cruz\xe2\x80\x99s\ncampaign for the GOP presidential nomination. Cruz\xe2\x80\x99s presidential campaign\nhas contracted with Cambridge Analytica to provide data services, and the\ncompany has had talks with at least one of those super PACs, according to\nsources.\n\n\n\nIt\xe2\x80\x99s not uncommon for political campaigns, parties and PACs to pay huge\ncontracts for data and other services to companies affiliated with their\nconsultants. But it\xe2\x80\x99s less common for such contracts to go to firms\naffiliated with the donors funding the whole enterprise.\n\n\n\nCruz spokesman Rick Tyler said the campaign\xe2\x80\x99s Director of Research and\nAnalytics Chris Wilson is using Cambridge Analytica to build models that\nidentify and sort persuadable voters in early primary states by six-key\npersonality types, which will be used to target the campaign\xe2\x80\x99s outreach.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99ve seen their product and its better than anything I\xe2\x80\x99ve ever seen,\xe2\x80\x9d said\nTyler. \xe2\x80\x9cWe know what a Cruz supporter looks like demographically \xe2\x80\xa6 and this\nallows us to go into Iowa and match those traits with likely caucus goers.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nThe group of super PACs supporting Cruz, Keep the Promise, did not respond\nto questions about their arrangements with Cambridge Analytica. The company\ndid not respond to interview requests, while a spokesman for the Mercer\nfamily declined to comment.\n\n\n\nIn recent years, the Mercer family \xe2\x80\x93 Robert Mercer, his wife Diana Mercer\nand their daughter Rebekah Mercer \xe2\x80\x93 have emerged as among the leading\nfinanciers of conservative causes and candidates.\n\n\n\nTheir quiet involvement in Cambridge Analytica \xe2\x80\x93 which is known in elite\nconservative finance circles but has yet to be reported \xe2\x80\x93 seems to mark a\ntransition from purely financing political campaigns to running their own\npolitical operation. It\xe2\x80\x99s a model that\xe2\x80\x99s been pursued to varying degrees by\nbillionaires ranging from the liberal hedge funder Tom Steyer to the\nconservative industrialists Charles and David Koch. It was made possible\npartly by the Supreme Court\xe2\x80\x99s 2010 Citizens United decision that opened new\navenues for unlimited political spending.\n\n\n\nWith their investment in Cambridge Analytica \xe2\x80\x93 and the Cruz campaign\xe2\x80\x99s\nembrace of their product \xe2\x80\x93 the Mercers also have become competitors in an\nincreasingly cut-throat conservative political data race. Some of the\nright\xe2\x80\x99s most influential and well-funded players \xe2\x80\x94 including the Koch\nbrothers\xe2\x80\x99 operation and the Republican National Committee \xe2\x80\x94 are jockeying\nfor market share and 2016 prospects in a political sub-industry expected to\nconsume a huge portion of the billions spent in the campaign. The result of\nthe competition could go a long way towards determining the winner of the\nWhite House and the Republican Party\xe2\x80\x99s direction after the election.\n\n\n\nSo far, most of Cambridge Analytica\xe2\x80\x99s work appears to have come from\ncampaigns and committees funded in large part by the Mercers. And sources\nfamiliar with the Mercer\xe2\x80\x99s political efforts said that Rebekah Mercer, who\nhas steered the family\xe2\x80\x99s political expansion, has made introductions\nbetween Cambridge Analytica and the political committees the family\nsupports.\n\n\n\nFederal Election Commission filings show that nearly 93 percent of the $2.6\nmillion Cambridge Analytica has received in traceable federal payments have\ncome from committees to which the Mercers donated generously. The payments\n\xe2\x80\x93 which all came last year and were for polling, micro-targeting,\nadvertising and other services \xe2\x80\x93 came from Cruz\xe2\x80\x99s leadership PAC and a\nhandful of GOP-aligned big-money organizations, including Ending Spending\nAction Fund, former U.N. Ambassador John Bolton\xe2\x80\x99s super PAC and a pop-up\nsuper PAC created to boost 2014 Republican Senate candidates.\n\n\n\nOther Cambridge Analytica clients included the campaigns of GOP Sens. Tom\nCotton of Arkansas and Thom Tillis of North Carolina, as well as\nunsuccessful GOP House candidate Art Robinson of Oregon. The Mercers\ncombined to donate nearly $3.3 million to those groups in 2014, according\nto FEC filings.\n\n\n\nRepresentatives from most of the groups and campaigns did not respond to\nquestions about whether there was any connection between their support from\nthe Mercers and their payments to Cambridge Analytica.\n\n\n\nGarrett Marquis, a spokesman for Bolton\xe2\x80\x99s super PAC, said the $340,000 his\ngroup paid to Cambridge Analytica in 2014 was money well spent.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s something that no one has done in politics. Period,\xe2\x80\x9d said Marquis.\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt was the most cost-effective, efficient way to reach voters. We were\nvery pleased.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nMarquis said the firm created five categories of potential voters,\nincluding \xe2\x80\x9csoccer mom\xe2\x80\x9d and \xe2\x80\x9cworking dads,\xe2\x80\x9d by layering responses to surveys\natop voter data, and then targeted voters based on which category they fell\nin. The firm\xe2\x80\x99s \xe2\x80\x9ccore offering,\xe2\x80\x9d according to its website, \xe2\x80\x9ccombines\nadvanced data analytics and the creation of a psychographic framework to\nhelp you gain increased insight into your target voter groups.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nBolton\xe2\x80\x99s super PAC spent $5 million on digital ads in 2014 on key Senate\nraces, and Cambridge Analytica boasts on its website that the online and\nDirect TV ad campaign it ran for Bolton\xe2\x80\x99s super PAC appealed \xe2\x80\x9cdirectly to\nthe personality traits, priority issues and demographics of specific\ngroups\xe2\x80\x9d that \xe2\x80\x9chad a real impact in sending Thom Tillis to the US Senate.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nIt\xe2\x80\x99s not clear precisely which services Cruz\xe2\x80\x99s campaign or its supportive\nsuper PACs will purchase from Cambridge Analytica, or how much the work\nwill cost. Bob Menendez and 36% disapproved, a dip from earlier surveys\nbefore the Democrat was indicted on corruption charges in April. Cory Booker\xe2\x80\x99s work,\nwhile 22% disapproved, down from a 51% approval rating in a May survey.\n\n\n\nThe telephone poll of registered voters had a margin of error of plus or\nminus 4.4 percentage points.\n\n\n\n*New Jersey Democrats troll Chris Christie\n<http://www.politico.com/story/2015/07/chris-christie-new-jersey-democrats-resign-119802.html>\n// Politico // Daniel Strauss \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nNew Jersey Democrats are planning to throw a monkey wrench into New Jersey\nGov.
