Dems Prod a Defiant Chris Christie to Resign\n<http://www.nbcnews.com/politics/2016-election/n-j-dems-prod-defiant-chris-christie-resign-n388176>\n// NBC News // Kelly O\xe2\x80\x99Donnell \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nNew Jersey Democrats are mounting a plan to push Chris Christie out of the\ngovernor\'s office, but Christie aides say it has "zero chance" of being\nsuccessful.\n\n\n\nAdvisers to the 2016 presidential candidate say that the governor will keep\non doing "hands on" work with the state government even as his political\nfoes mull legislation that would require any New Jersey governor seeking\nthe presidency - including Christie - to resign.\n\n\n\nIf that legislation passed, Christie would veto it. A veto override would\nrequire that enough Republicans in the legislature join with Democrats,\nsomething that has never happened during Christie\'s tenure.\n\n\n\n"It\'s impossible to respond to every bit of silly nonsense that comes from\nthis legislature," Christie deputy press secretary Brian Murray said in a\nstatement. "The Governor has been clear that he is never disconnected from\ndoing his job as governor."\n\n\n\nChristie\'s team also pointed on Tuesday to his work with Democrats in the\nstate House to provide a tax break for working families, suggesting that\nthe success of his earned income tax credit proposal shows that he\'s\nremained engaged with his home state -- and with the same Democrats\nprodding him to resign -- despite his frequent out-of-state travel.\n\n\n\nAsked by NBC\'s Matt Lauer last week if he would consider resigning his\noffice during his run for president, Christie replied "I can\'t imagine I\nwould, no."\n\n\n\nChristie is struggling with poor approval ratings at home. A Monmouth\nUniversity poll last week showed a majority - 57 percent - of New Jersey\nvoters say that he should resign now that he\'s made his White House bid\nofficial.\n\n\n\n*Webb: The real deal about Chris Christie\n<http://thehill.com/opinion/david-webb/247127-david-webb-the-real-deal-about-chris-christie>\n// The Hill // David Webb \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nHe\'s announced. I\xe2\x80\x99m telling it like it is.\n\n\n\nNew Jersey Gov. Chris Christie officially made his bid for the GOP\nnomination \xe2\x80\x94 and eventually the White House \xe2\x80\x94 in his hometown of\nLivingston, N.J., and then he went straight to New Hampshire.\n\n\n\nThe instant pundit debate over whether Christie can win primaries and win\nover the Republican base is interesting, but no different from the debate\nover other GOP candidates. They all have their challenges, their pros and\ncons.\n\n\n\nThe town hall format is a strength, and that matters to Christie\xe2\x80\x99s campaign\nin a state like New Hampshire, where retail politics and grassroots\nengagement \xe2\x80\x94 or lack of it \xe2\x80\x94 can make or break a candidate. Christie had\ncrisscrossed the state prior to his announcement and will likely spend half\nof his time or more initially there. New Hampshire, unlike many of the\nSouthern states, has a broader representation of the general electorate\nacross the country.\n\n\n\nThe debate over the spouse of a candidate aside, clearly his wife, Mary\nPat, is an asset on the campaign trail as well. She is intelligent, warm\nand approachable. To some extent she puts a softer side on display for the\noften-brash Christie.\n\n\n\nBut the governor has a New Jersey problem. There will be a attacks based on\nthe state\xe2\x80\x99s credit downgrades, and issues over the Second Amendment, even\nabout immigration in the growth of the illegal alien population. Christie\nwill have to mount a vigorous defense and explanation based on being a\nRepublican governor in a Democrat-controlled state. The bad legacy left by\nformer governors Jim McGreevey and Jon Corzine will only matter to the\nvoters who know this legacy. The more conservative base of the Republican\nParty has questioned before and will continue to question the governor\xe2\x80\x99s\nconservative credentials.\n\n\n\nI won\xe2\x80\x99t discount a win or top-three placement in the primary for Christie\nin South Carolina, however. Sen. Lindsey Graham is not really a factor even\nin his own home state, and straight-talking politicians have appeal in the\nPalmetto State. By the time the primary arrives, if Christie is in the top\nfive, he will make a serious effort to win South Carolina.\n\n\n\nIowa has a staunch Republican base, which will be tough for Christie to win\nover, and Iowa is not as red as it\xe2\x80\x99s often portrayed, especially in the\n\ngeneral election. The big-money donors and political action committees know\nthis. A decent placement in third, or at least in the top five, in the Iowa\nprimary would keep the New Jersey governor in contention.\n\n\n\nThe money matters. Money not only allows for media campaigns and travel \xe2\x80\x94\nit also grants the ability to put teams in place in key primary states.\nAfter all, politics, once the shouting has subsided and the differences are\nhighlighted, is about the ability to mount a consistent and effective\nground game. It\xe2\x80\x99s not a question of whether someone like businessman Ken\nLangone can bundle money for Christie. He is a well-known fundraiser with a\nsignificant network. Christie has raised a lot of money, the most of any\nhead of the Republican Governors Association. That gives him access to\nmonetary and political capital. Count on him calling in these favors.\n\n\n\nWho has to attack Christie? First, those who need to draw a stark contrast.\nThe more socially conservative candidates will do this. They will attack on\nthe basis of Christie being a Northern, moderate Republican. The pushback\nfrom Christie will be that he is a pro-life Catholic. So this may be a\nwash.\n\n\n\nThe second group includes the candidates whose position he threatens.\nFormer Florida Gov. Jeb Bush, Sen. Marco Rubio (Fla.) and Donald Trump will\nhave to contend for some of the same voting block: moderate Republican and\nindependent voters. One of the defenses Christie will have against this\nwill be the fact that he worked with a Democrat-controlled legislature that\nhas a union man as president of the state Senate. Constitutional\nconservatives like myself understand that a governor has to sign what he or\nshe cannot veto.\n\n\n\nThe dread and often dead winter months will be hard for every candidate.\nPolitical fatigue will set in for even the hard-core base and many\nAmericans will turn instead to Thanksgiving, Christmas and the new year\nahead. Politicians may want to hibernate and prepare for the 2016 relaunch.\n\n\n\nSuper Tuesday is a long way away, but if Christie survives the winter\npolitical doldrums, it will become a much more exciting day. It\xe2\x80\x99s a\npolitical pundits dream, and for journalists a feeding frenzy.\n\n\n\nThe cynic in me still believes that presidential elections should begin on\nJan. 1 of the election year. But then again, like politicians, I am allowed\nto dream.\n\n\n\n*Chris Christie Administration Whistleblower To Justice Department:\nBridgegate Prosecutor May Be Compromised\n<http://www.ibtimes.com/chris-christie-administration-whistleblower-justice-department-bridgegate-prosecutor-1997095>\n// IB Times // David Sirota & Andrew Perez \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nWhen Chris Christie\xe2\x80\x99s administration quashed a grand jury\xe2\x80\x99s 43 indictments\nagainst the Republican governor\'s supporters in 2010, local prosecutor\nBennett Barlyn objected. He was soon fired. Barlyn says the move to throw\nout the Hunterdon County indictments may have violated federal law -- and\nthat ties between New Jersey U.S. Attorney Paul Fishman\xe2\x80\x99s office and Gov.\nChristie may have improperly prevented a probe from moving forward.\n\n\n\nBarlyn sent a letter to Attorney General Loretta Lynch on Monday,\nexpressing concern that \xe2\x80\x9capparent conflicts between Governor Christie\xe2\x80\x99s\nadministration and the U.S. Attorney\xe2\x80\x99s Office for the District of New\nJersey ... may be compromising the latter\xe2\x80\x99s independent role relating to\nthe enforcement of federal criminal law.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nIn February, International Business Times reported that investigators from\nFishman\xe2\x80\x99s office interviewed Barlyn about the events surrounding the\nquashed grand jury indictments. ABC News confirmed the IBTimes report. But\nFishman\xe2\x80\x99s office abruptly issued a statement appearing to clear Christie\nand declaring that no investigation was underway. Former U.S. attorneys\ninterviewed by IBTimes said such a statement pre-emptively exonerating a\npublic official is extremely unusual.\n\n\n\nBarlyn says in the letter to Lynch that this public backtracking\n\xe2\x80\x9cimmediately confirmed my suspicion that the interview was not conducted as\npart of a genuine inquiry, but was instead intended to placate me and\nforestall my efforts\xe2\x80\x9d to have the quashed indictments investigated.\n\n\n\nThe Justice Department and Fishman\xe2\x80\x99s office declined to answer IBTimes\xe2\x80\x99\nquestions about Barlyn\xe2\x80\x99s letter. Christie\xe2\x80\x99s office did not respond to\nIBTimes\' requests for comment.\n\n\n\nBarlyn first contacted Fishman\xe2\x80\x99s office last year with allegations -- made\nin the past by other former employees in the Hunterdon County prosecutor\xe2\x80\x99s\noffice -- that the Christie administration had illegally thrown out grand\njury indictments against supporters, including the local county Sheriff\nDeborah Trout and Undersheriff Mike Russo. Barlyn has maintained he was\nfired after raising objections and has filed a wrongful termination lawsuit.\n\n\n\nBarlyn\xe2\x80\x99s case was assigned to investigator Thomas Mahoney, who was hired by\nChristie in 2006 when Christie was New Jersey\'s U.S. attorney.\n\n\n\nDespite his ties to Christie, Mahoney was permitted to not only be the\npoint person on Barlyn\xe2\x80\x99s case but also be a \xe2\x80\x9csupervisory criminal\ninvestigator\xe2\x80\x9d on the probe of lane closures at the George Washington Bridge\nby officials at the Port Authority of New York and New Jersey. The\n"Bridgegate" investigation generated a guilty plea and two indictments of\nformer top Christie allies, but the governor was not implicated.\n\n\n\nDuring a Bridgegate press conference in May, Fishman was asked if his\noffice faced any challenges in remaining independent. \xe2\x80\x9cThere\xe2\x80\x99s nobody who\nwas working on this case in my office -- no lawyers working on this case in\nmy office -- who was hired by Gov. Christie,\xe2\x80\x9d Fishman said.\n\n\n\nA representative for Fishman later clarified that Mahoney had worked on the\ncase but said that \xe2\x80\x9che is not a lawyer.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nIn fact, according to records obtained by IBTimes, roughly 40 percent of\nthe current U.S. attorney\xe2\x80\x99s office is made up of personnel hired by\nChristie.\n\n\n\nBarlyn\xe2\x80\x99s letter to Lynch is the latest incident to raise questions about\nFishman\xe2\x80\x99s independence from the governor.\n\n\n\nIn diaries released in early 2014, Hoboken\xe2\x80\x99s Democratic mayor Dawn Zimmer\nsaid she feared bringing allegations of Christie administration misdeeds to\nFishman because \xe2\x80\x9cChristie has friends throughout [the U.S.] attorney\'s\noffice.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nIn June, Fishman\xe2\x80\x99s office requested that a federal court bar the public\nrelease of 1.5 million pages of documents obtained from the Christie\nadministration in the Bridgegate investigation.\n\n\n\nLawyers for one defendant in the case, former Port Authority official Bill\nBaroni, said Fishman\xe2\x80\x99s move to conceal the documents was designed to\nprevent the release of information they say could absolve their client and\npotentially incriminate others in the Christie administration.\n\n\n\nThe attempt to bar disclosure of evidence, Baroni\xe2\x80\x99s lawyers said, in part\nillustrates that \xe2\x80\x9csomething is afoot besides a paternalistic desire to\nprotect members of the governor\xe2\x80\x99s inner circle, alumni of this U.S.\nattorney\xe2\x80\x99s office, high-ranking Port Authority employees and others.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n*Governor Chris Christie: Media Should Apologize to Me for Bridgegate\n<http://newsbusters.org/blogs/randy-hall/2015/07/07/governor-chris-christie-media-should-apologize-me-bridgegate#sthash.Tju2N97O.dpuf\n//> // Newsbusters // Randy hall \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nDuring a Monday morning appearance on the MSNBC\'s Morning Joe program, New\nJersey governor Chris Christie was asked by panelist Katty Kay about his\nrole in the possible \xe2\x80\x9ccreation of a culture\xe2\x80\x9d in his administration that led\nto the Bridgegate lane closure incident, which took place in early\nSeptember of 2013.\n\n\n\nThe 2016 GOP presidential candidate responded to the obnoxious question by\ninstead calling the incident \xe2\x80\x9can exception, not the rule,\xe2\x80\x9d and stating that\npeople in the media should have stood up and said: \xe2\x80\x9cWe\'re sorry, governor,\nfor having jumped to conclusions;\xe2\x80\x9d and \xe2\x80\x9cnot only have accused you, but\nconvicted you.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nThe segment began with Kay asking Christie a question she undoubtedly\nwouldn\'t put to Democratic presidential front-runner and scandal-plagued\nHillary Clinton:\n\n\n\nIf you were running against yourself, wouldn\'t you say: \xe2\x80\x9cThis is somebody\nwho surrounds himself with people to whom the subliminal message is: \'We\nwill do whatever it takes to make sure that we are in the right position\npolitically, even if that means shutting down bridges?\'\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI don\'t necessarily want to know about it. I\'m not going to talk about it,\nbut that you allowed a culture in your office that would allow that kind of\nthing to happen?\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nChristie replied: \xe2\x80\x9cThat\'s where the people who accuse you of doing\nsomething wrong, when they\'re disappointed and find out that you didn\'t,\nthat\'s their refuge.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cRemember in the beginning,\xe2\x80\x9d he continued, \xe2\x80\x9cit was: \'He did this. He\ndirected it. He\'s this kind of guy.\' Then all of a sudden, you\'re not. Then\nthey say: \'OK, now what do we do?\'\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cSo instead of just standing up and saying what they should say, which is\n\'We\'re sorry, governor, for having jumped to conclusions; we\'re sorry for\nhaving prejudged this; we\'re sorry for having not only accused you, but\nconvicted you,\' they say: \'Oh, well, all right; now it\'s a culture.\'\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nThe governor continued:\n\n\n\nIt wasn\'t a culture because if it was, Katty, there would have been a lot\nof these incidents. There wouldn\'t have been 100 Democrats, elected\nDemocrats, supporting me for re-election.\n\n\n\nI wouldn\'t have gotten over a third of the Republican vote and 51 percent\nof the Hispanic vote if this was a pattern. It\'s not.\n\n\n\n"Exceptions happen; accidents, mistakes happen,\xe2\x80\x9d he stated. \xe2\x80\x9cYou still have\nto be accountable for them, but it does not mean there was a culture\nbecause if there was, there would be more than just one person in the\ngovernor\'s office. That\'s called an exception, not the rule.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nThe problems began on Monday, Sept. 9, 2013, when two of three eastbound\ntoll lanes on the George Washington Bridge were closed to morning rush hour\ntraffic, which was forced to use crowded state and interstate expressways\nuntil the road was re-opened the following Friday.\n\n\n\nAs NewsBusters previously reported, NBC\'s evening newscast devoted four\nminutes and 55 seconds to the \xe2\x80\x9cscandal\xe2\x80\x9d when it broke on January 8.\n\n\n\nAccording to Scott Whitlock, a senior news analyst for the Media Research\nCenter (the parent company of the NewsBusters website):\n\n\n\nIn less than 48 hours, ABC, CBS and NBC deluged viewers with coverage of\nChris Christie\'s traffic jam scandal, devoting a staggering 88 minutes to\nthe story.\n\n\n\nIn comparison, these same news outlets over the last six months have\nallowed a scant two minutes for the latest on Barack Obama\'s Internal\nRevenue Service scandal. The disparity in less than two days is 44 to one.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cFrom Wednesday through Friday morning, the latest on Christie\'s\nTraffic-Gate led 11 out of 13 news programs,\xe2\x80\x9d Whitlock noted. \xe2\x80\x9cNBC produced\nthe heaviest coverage, over 34 minutes. CBS followed close behind with more\nthan 30 minutes. ABC came in third with just under 23 minutes.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nHowever, when the Republican governor was cleared of any wrongdoing in the\nmatter, \xe2\x80\x9cABC and CBS  punted on the story and didn\'t cover it in their\nThursday night newscasts,\xe2\x80\x9d MRC news analyst Curtis Houck reported.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cNBC Nightly News did cover the story, however, but only in the form of a\nnews brief that lasted for 38 seconds,\xe2\x80\x9d he added, in which then-anchor\nBrian Williams stated:\n\n\n\nA major headline this evening in the federal investigation into New Jersey\ngovernor Chris Christie and his administration.\n\n\n\nFederal officials tell NBC News that, after nine months, investigators have\nconcluded there is no evidence that governor Christie had advance knowledge\nof any politically motivated scheme to shut down lanes on the George\nWashington Bridge, which is the world\'s busiest span.\n\n\n\nIt wouldn\'t be wise for Christie to hold his breath while waiting for an\napology from the people who used the incident to attack his popularity or\nhoping the press would pose a similar question to Hillary Clinton. There\nisn\'t a shade of purple deep enough to match the color of his face if he\ntried.\n\n\n\n*Why Chris Christie may have an edge in GOP race\n<http://www.cnbc.com/id/102815333> // CNBC // Mark Macias \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nDonald Trump just might be the second best thing that happened to New\nJersey Gov. Chris Christie.\n\n\n\nChristie recently announced he\'s running for president in 2016. Much of\nAmerica might not know it yet, but if you live in New York or New Jersey\nand watch the local news, you know that Christie has an explosive\ntemperament. You either love his brutal honesty or hate his bullying\nnature, but regardless of where you sit on the political couch, Christie\'s\nmouth can make any ear blush.\n\n\n\nFor the past 6 years, Christie has owned the local political show as the\nonly governor in the Tri-State area to speak his mind without reverence for\ndiplomacy or political correctness. He called a Navy Seal an "idiot" when\nhe challenged the governor publicly. When a teacher asked him why he said\ntheir schools and teachers were failing, Christie responded: "Because they\nare... I am tired of you people." And when another teacher questioned why\nshe wasn\'t paid fairly, Christie was brutally honest: "Well you know what?\nThen you don\'t have to do it."\n\n\n\nBut now, there is a new controversial presidential candidate who is already\novershadowing Christie. With Trump in the race, Christie suddenly seems\nmore palatable.\n\n\n\nEven the "Bridgegate" scandal, which accused Christie\'s administration of\nclosing the George Washington Bridge in retaliation to a local mayor, seems\nlike a school yard tussle compared to Trump and his fight with Macy\'s,\nUnivision, NBC, Mexico, China, etc.\n\n\n\nBut will that palatable perception last? Or better yet, will voters in Iowa\nbuy it?\n\n\n\nIf I were consulting Christie, I would say, as long as he can bite his\ntongue and control his temper between now and New Hampshire, he just might\nhave the political chops and finesse to charm his way with voters. Christie\nknows that deep, down inside, he can\'t be constantly combative if he\'s\ngoing to convince voters he should be in control of the nuclear button.\nHe\'s also smart enough to know he has to be good and liked if he is going\nto win the nomination.\n\n\n\nChristie is off to a great start by surrounding himself with smart\nstrategists who understand how the media works. Immediately after his\npresidential announcement, Christie did an interview with NBC\'s Matt Lauer,\nwhere he repositioned his temper as passion.\n\n\n\n"I\'m angry about the fact that taxpayers were being ripped off in New\nJersey," Christie told Lauer. "I\'m angry about the fact that our urban kids\ncan\'t get a good education. I\'m angry about those things \xe2\x80\x94 you\'re darn\nright I am. And I think America wants someone who\'s willing to fight for\nthat."\n\n\n\nBrilliant PR move: The sooner you address your point of weakness, the less\npersuasive your opponents sound. The person who tells the story first is in\nbetter control of the narrative. Christie didn\'t avoid the tough\naccusations like other presidential candidates have done. Instead, he\naddressed it straight on and unabashedly.\n\n\n\nNow, whether conservative voters buy into Christie\'s more moderate\npositions is another issue. He faces the same challenge that Rudy Giuliani\nhad when he ran for president in 2008: He\'s a moderate on social issues\nthat are crucial to the conservative base.\n\n\n\nSo, if Trump is the second-best thing to happen to Christie, what\'s the\nfirst? All of the other 13 GOP contenders combined.\n\n\n\nPublicity is difficult in any crowded field because it\'s harder to stand\nout from the pack. When smart phones first hit the market, it was easy to\nget publicity for mobile apps because they were rare. Today, the market for\nmobile apps is saturated, making it more difficult to get your story told.\nIt\'s the same for the GOP candidates. Fiorina, Carson, Graham, Pataki,\nPaul, Perry \xe2\x80\x94 for the typical voter, those names run together like a\nJindal, I mean jingle. This is where Christie will shine.\n\n\n\nHe understands, like Trump, how to move the media needle. He has governed a\nbig state, like Jeb Bush and Rick Perry. He has big donors behind him, like\nMarco Rubio. But unlike those other candidates \xe2\x80\x94 Trump, Bush, Perry and\nRubio - Christie doesn\'t have their baggage. No one will question\nChristie\'s bravado and experience against Rubio. Christie seems less\nvolatile than Trump, who seems to threaten a new company every day on the\ncampaign trail. Sure, Perry was the longest-running governor of Texas and\nBush was governor of a swing state, but Christie was elected governor twice\nin a blue state.\n\n\n\nBut much of the minutiae will be lost in the crowded presidential debates.\nWhen you have 10 candidates on one stage trying to explain a position in\nunder 90 seconds, the only thing voters will remember is how the candidates\ncame across. And who can forget how Christie comes across.\n\n\n\nAs long as Christie can be direct and respectful, he just might have a\nwinning edge to the nomination, assuming he can win over the conservative\nbase.\n\n\n\n*GRAHAM*\n\n\n\n*Lindsey Graham Protests \'Brad Pitt\' Debate\n<http://www.bloomberg.com/politics/articles/2015-07-07/lindsey-graham-protests-brad-pitt-debate>\n// Bloomberg // Ben Brody \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nRepublican presidential candidate Lindsey Graham is launching a protest of\nthe "Brad Pitt" debate.\n\n\n\nIn an e-mail Tuesday, the South Carolina senator urged supporters to sign a\npetition protesting the terms of an Aug.  6 debate, the first scheduled\nfaceoff among the Republican presidential contenders. Fox News, the debate\nsponsor, has said it will allow 10 candidates, based on their standing in\nthe polls.\n\n\n\nGraham, at distinct risk of being left out, suggesting Brad Pitt, the\nA-list star of movies like Fight Club and The Curious Case of Benjamin\nButton, "would have a better shot of being on the debate stage than real\ncandidates for president" because the current "criterion favors celebrities\nand candidates who have run previously with high name recognition."\n\n\n\nAnother celebrity-turned-presidential candidate, real estate mogul and\nreality TV star Donald Trump, has specific which polls it\nwill use.\n\n\n\nGraham receives support from about one percent of registered Republicans in\nswing states, according to a recent poll from Quinnipiac University,\nmeaning Of his five most expensive speeches,\nfour of them were for Christian entities, a POLITICO analysis of his\nfinancial disclosure form shows.\n\n\n\nBilled by the Washington Speaker\xe2\x80\x99s Bureau as an \xe2\x80\x9cinspiring storyteller\xe2\x80\x9d who\nis \xe2\x80\x9csoft-spoken yet charismatic\xe2\x80\x9d and capable of \xe2\x80\x9ccommanding the stage,\xe2\x80\x9d\nCarson\xe2\x80\x99s speaking fees varied widely, from $12,320 to $48,500.\n\n\n\nLast August, Hope Pregnancy Center in College Station, Texas, was one of\nthe organizations that doled out $40,500 \xe2\x80\x94 close to Carson\xe2\x80\x99s highest\nspeaking fee \xe2\x80\x94 for the neurosurgeon-turned-author to speak at a fundraiser\nand attend a private, 45-minute reception with donors beforehand. The\nfaith-based, pro-life organization works with women with unplanned\npregnancies.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe called the speaker\xe2\x80\x99s bureau and we were told that number,\xe2\x80\x9d explained\nTracy Frank, executive director of the center. \xe2\x80\x9cWashington Speakers Bureau\ndictated the terms \xe2\x80\xa6 We\xe2\x80\x99re not that sophisticated and stuff. I\xe2\x80\x99m going to\ncry if you\xe2\x80\x99re telling me he did others for a lot less.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nCarson gave 115 speeches for lower amounts in 2014 alone.\n\n\n\nFrank said she didn\xe2\x80\x99t negotiate with the Washington Speakers Bureau because\nof Carson\xe2\x80\x99s popularity. There were concerns about alienating\na general audience.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI just said, \xe2\x80\x98No problem, you can take it out,\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d Carson recalled in a\nrecent interview with The Daily Caller. \xe2\x80\x9c\xe2\x80\x98But take me out too, because it\nwon\xe2\x80\x99t be about me.\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd then they backed off.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nBased on his 1996 autobiography with the same title, the uplifting TV movie\ntells the story of Carson\xe2\x80\x99s path from inner-city Detroit to the Johns\nHopkins operating table, where he first successfully separated twins\nconjoined at the head.\n\n\n\nThe 2009 movie has helped make Carson, now running as an outsider for the\nRepublican nomination for president, famous: it has played in schools,\nchurches and on the Black Entertainment Television network (BET). Hundreds\nof thousands of DVDs have been sold. It streams on Netflix.\n\n\n\nIt could also help explain in part why Carson, who has never run for\noffice, is polling in second-place in evangelical-heavy Iowa and in third\nplace nationally, according to the Real Clear Politics polling average.\n\n\n\nBefore the movie deal was inked, Carson said he talked with as many as 15\ndifferent production companies. He wanted to make sure the film stayed true\nto life and didn\xe2\x80\x99t take artistic liberties.\n\n\n\nCarson was finally satisfied: \xe2\x80\x9cTNT and Sony said they would do it\naccurately, and that they would consult with me in the process.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt turned out to be a two-edged sword, because they were always calling\nme,\xe2\x80\x9d Carson said with a laugh.\n\n\n\nIn an interview with TheDC, Dan Angel, the executive producer of Gifted\nHands, said he made a promise to Carson. \xe2\x80\x9cI am going to tell your story\nfrom beginning to end and tell the truth. I\xe2\x80\x99m not going to add anything.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nCarson was active during production: Angel said he visited the set in\nDetroit, spending time with actor Cuba Gooding Jr., who played him.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cHe would be there every step of the way whenever we needed to talk to him\nabout reality checks,\xe2\x80\x9d Angel said of Carson. \xe2\x80\x9cWe would have Cuba Gooding\nJr. on the phone with him. And he gave complete access to his life, which\nis really important.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nGooding, through agent Adam Schweitzer, declined to be interviewed.\n\n\n\nBut in a 2009 appearance on CBS, the actor praised Carson. \xe2\x80\x9cI always say\nabout men like this: they\xe2\x80\x99re like God\xe2\x80\x99s tool,\xe2\x80\x9d Gooding said. \xe2\x80\x9cHe\xe2\x80\x99s really\ngiven him a gift and he\xe2\x80\x99s touched so many people.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nCarson says he was satisfied with the finished product. \xe2\x80\x9cI thought they did\na spectacular job. Cuba came and spent a couple days with me. with\nliberty and justice for everybody.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nMr. Carson called for a \xe2\x80\x9cproportional tax\xe2\x80\x9d of somewhere between 10 percent\nand 15 percent on individual and corporate income, and for the elimination\nof all tax deductions, including the cherished mortgage-interest and\ncharity-donation deductions.\n\n\n\nThe 63-year-old also came out against \xe2\x80\x9csanctuary cities\xe2\x80\x9d that refuse to\ncooperate with federal deportation efforts on immigration, following the\nslaying of a San Francisco woman, with which an illegal immigrant who had\nbeen deported five times has been charged.\n\n\n\nVoters in the early primary states are being pulled in various directions\nbecause of the sheer size of the GOP field.\n\n\n\nThat was a clear reminder of that Gov. Bobby Jindal of Louisiana also traveled through the state\non Tuesday.\n\n\n\nPolls show Mr. Carson, who has never held political office, is running\nthird nationally behind former Florida Gov. Jeb Bush and Gov. Scott Walker\nof Wisconsin. He is tied for second in Iowa, which kicks off the nomination\nrace, and is running in the middle of the pack in New Hampshire.\n\n\n\nThe Carson campaign announced earlier this month that it had pulled in $8.3\nmillion in its opening quarter and more than $10 million since he launched\nhis exploratory committee in early March.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe have easily what we need to run our are doing just\nfine because they forgot about one very important thing \xe2\x80\x94 the people.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nMr. Carson and his wife, Candy, celebrated his 40th wedding anniversary in\nnearby Nashua on Monday and followed that up Tuesday with five separate\nstops across the state.\n\n\n\nMr. Carson cast himself as an Washington outsider and drove home the idea\nthat he is taking the same for\nhealth savings accounts, as well as the ability for people to purchase\ninsurance across state lines.\n\n\n\nAsked about Social Security, he advocated for gradually raising the\nretirement age over time and said that he would offer a tax credit in\nexchange for people choosing to opt out of the program.\n\n\n\nOn immigration, he said he would seal the border and provide When\nGreece joined the euro, it benefited from the financial support of its more\nfiscally responsible neighbors in the euro zone. Rather than taking the\nopportunity to enact the structural reforms that could have increased\ngrowth \xe2\x80\x94 reforms that it still has not undertaken \xe2\x80\x94 Greece instead went on\na spending spree funded by other people\xe2\x80\x99s money.\n\n\n\nGreece has been cooking the books with complicated financial instruments\nfor years. But the problems don\xe2\x80\x99t stop there. Greece\xe2\x80\x99s Rubik\xe2\x80\x99s Cube tax\ncode and rampant corruption make tax evasion widespread. Golden parachute\npublic pensions that allow public sector workers to retire as early as 45\ndrain dollars out of the government coffers while incentivizing a still\nhealthy and work-age workforce to live on the public dime. It\xe2\x80\x99s hard to\nhave sufficient tax paying workers when about 75% of Greek public-sector\nemployees retire by the age 61.\n\n\n\nAfter taking office in January, the Alexis Tsipras administration reversed\npromised privatization of state-owned assets like the Port of Piraeus. In\n2011, the IMF predicted Greece could bring in 50 billion euros ($56\nbillion) from the sale of state assets, not to mention the savings from\nmoving those employees off the public wage and benefit system. To date, it\nhas raised about 3 billion euros.\n\n\n\nBusiness has no interest in creating jobs when crushed by government\nregulation. Tspiras promised to raise the minimum wage, despite the economy\nspiraling out of control. It\xe2\x80\x99s not surprising the March unemployment rate\nstood at 25.6%.\n\n\n\nThis is the European nightmare. The way of Greece is where Hillary Clinton\nand Bernie Sanders will take us. It\xe2\x80\x99s simple math: You can\xe2\x80\x99t spend more\nthan you take in. You can\xe2\x80\x99t make it impossible for business to thrive and\nexpect the economy to grow. No wonder the U.S. has had a disappointing\nabout 2% \xe2\x80\x9crecovery\xe2\x80\x9d growth. That\xe2\x80\x99s not an accident\xe2\x80\x94it\xe2\x80\x99s the result of\nfailed policies.\n\n\n\nClinton and Sanders are math deniers, like most of the Democrats in D.C.\nThey want to grow the government economy instead of the real American\neconomy. Rather than pursuing tax reform to improve growth or entitlement\nchanges to reduce future expenditures, Clinton and Sanders are focused on\nspending trillions on Obamacare, giving free college to everyone, and\nraising the federal minimum wage.\n\n\n\nThis was all on plain view in New Hampshire this past weekend, where\nClinton spent the weekend promoting a third term of President Barack\nObama\xe2\x80\x99s failed policies. The irony is that her dishonesty and lack of\ntransparency is a windfall for Sanders.\n\n\n\nSanders is rising in the polls. Why? Because he\xe2\x80\x99s honest. He freely admits\nthat he believes in socialism, and Democrats are flocking to the only\nhonest candidate running on their side. Sanders should write Clinton a\nthank you note.\n\n\n\nSanders may be saying what Clinton will not say, but the reality is they\xe2\x80\x99re\nboth socialists. And if you want a peek into our future with Clinton or\nSanders, then look at what\xe2\x80\x99s happening in Greece today. Sanders proudly\nsaid on Sunday that he wants to raise taxes.\n\n\n\nSanders and Clinton seem to believe prosperity lies in the hands of\ngovernment. We know it lies in the hands of our people.\n\n\n\nWe have to stop pretending. Greece pretended that debt didn\xe2\x80\x99t matter for\nyears. It pretended it could spend money it didn\xe2\x80\x99t have. It pretended that\nthere was some mythical pot of money in Athens that didn\xe2\x80\x99t exist. It\npretended that 1+1 didn\xe2\x80\x99t equal 2.\n\n\n\nThe politicians in Puerto Rico are no different. They are demanding that we\nchange U.S. laws so that they can file for bankruptcy. They are even\nthreatening to sway the presidential election in order to force candidates\nto agree with them. These are the same politicians that led the country to\nbankruptcy. Everyone knows exactly what is going on here \xe2\x80\x94 they are asking\nthe U.S. taxpayers to pay for a bailout. That\xe2\x80\x99s where this leads, and we\nshould be honest about it. I oppose this.\n\n\n\nUnfortunately, we better admit that our politicians in Washington are\ntaking us down the exact same road that Puerto Rico is on, and that Greece\nhas gone down. The federal minimum wage has strangled economic growth in\nPuerto Rico. The Puerto Rican government tried to throw money at the\nproblem with incentive programs to lure business \xe2\x80\x94 but that just cost money\nand didn\xe2\x80\x99t fix the structural problem, so the economy continued to stall.\n\n\n\nI know because in Louisiana we reversed decades of outmigration, and we\ncreated more than 90,000 jobs by reducing regulations and cutting taxes.\nLouisiana\xe2\x80\x99s economy boomed. We can do the same for America\xe2\x80\x99s economy. If\nyou want more borrowing and spending, then vote for the Democrats. Moves Event From Donald Trump Golf Course\n<http://www.nytimes.com/2015/07/08/sports/golf/pga-moves-event-from-trump-golf-course.html>\n// NYT // Brendan Prunty \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nAbout five years ago, when golf was going through an economic downswing,\nDonald Trump took the opportunity to buy in, scooping up failed properties.\nHe already had courses emblazoned with his name around the world, but\ncredibility? That eluded him.\n\n\n\nSoon major golf tours came calling, bringing big-money, high-profile events\nto his courses. Major championships \xe2\x80\x94 the prized possessions of every club\n\xe2\x80\x94 came next. Grand Slam of Golf \xe2\x80\x94 a year-end exhibition among the winners of\nthe four men\xe2\x80\x99s major championships \xe2\x80\x94 was scheduled for October at Trump\nNational Golf Club in Los Angeles.\n\n\n\nInstead, it will be moved to a yet-to-be-determined location.\n\n\n\nTrump said it was a mutually agreed upon move to protect his friends in the\norganization from dealing with potential backlash over his remarks, in\nwhich he said, referring to Mexican immigrants: \xe2\x80\x9cThey\xe2\x80\x99re bringing drugs.\nThey\xe2\x80\x99re bringing crime. They\xe2\x80\x99re rapists.\xe2\x80\x9d He later added, \xe2\x80\x9cAnd some, I\nassume, are good people.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nThe P.G.A. and L.P.G.A. issued statements on Tuesday, with the P.G.A.\nsaying \xe2\x80\x9cwe understand and support\xe2\x80\x9d the decision. Instead, Mexico was\nsending problems: rapists, criminals and drug runners, he said.\n\n\n\nFew of the workers at the construction site wanted to discuss Trump\'s\ncomments when asked about them a day after the Washington Post ran a\nfront-page story about the workers on the hotel development billed as a\n$200 million project.\n\n\n\nThe Post reported that several of the workers were immigrants and many were\ncitizens or working legally, but laborers also told the Post that many had\nfirst entered the U.S illegally.\n\n\n\nMany of the workers interviewed were from El Salvador or Honduras,\nreflective of the Washington, D.C., Latino population. Larger Mexican\nimmigrant populations are found in communities around the district.\n\n\n\nThose that did talk to reporters Tuesday said Trump was crazy or that he\nclearly didn\'t know that the people who work on his projects are decent\npeople.\n\n\n\n"They\'ve come here to work, to get ahead, not to do anything bad," one\nworker who would not divulge any personal information told NBC. "All the\nones I know, at least, are workers, not rapists."\n\n\n\nTheir stories as reported by the Post give a different view of immigration,\none that shows the complexity of the lives of people and their status in\nthe U.S. \xe2\x80\x94 here illegally, once here legally but now a citizen, a legal\nresident, here with temporary protected status.\n\n\n\nAlthough Trump has pegged them as problems, the workers\' toil away making a\nluxury hotel out of a historic building complex that houses the official\nBells of Congress gifted to the U.S. from Britain during the nation\'s\nbicentennial and a 315-foot clock tower dating to 1899.\n\n\n\nThere\'s no mistaking who is reaping at least some of the benefit of these\nlaborers\' work.\n\n\n\nThe blue banners atop fencing across the front of the construction site\nannounce the developer in large white letters: TRUMP.\n\n\n\nIt\'s a brand that Trump himself acknowledged is becoming increasingly\ntarnished. Often associated with success, wealth and excess, Trump\'s brand\nis increasingly being connected to racism and xenophobia.\n\n\n\nBusinesses have been severing ties with Trump, including NBC, Univision,\nMacy\'s and Serta Mattresses.\n\n\n\n"I didn\'t know it was going to be quite this severe," Trump said on "Fox &\nFriends" of the backlash since his statements.\n\n\n\nOn Tuesday, the Professional Golfers Association pulled this year\'s Grand\nSlam of Golf from Trump National course in Los Angeles.\n\n\n\n"I think Donald Trump knew he was going to be provocative and knew he was\ngoing to get pushback, but I believe he didn\'t think the pushback would\nactually come in the form of being dropped by sponsorships and contracts,"\nsaid political analyst Victoria Francesco de Soto.\n\n\n\n"Trump is losing out real money and his brand is being harmed," she said.\n"We all know Trump has that outrageous provocative brand, but it\'s going a\nbit deeper."\n\n\n\n*Take on Trump? While his negative characterization of illegal\nMexican immigrants has caused corporate partners to recoil, they have\nhelped him gain traction with the Republican base.\n\n\n\nTrump\xe2\x80\x99s nationwide support has increased to 12 percent, according to a\nrecent CNN/ORC poll, putting him in second place, behind former Florida\nGov. Jeb Bush. (That\xe2\x80\x99s\nthe longest amount of time allowed by United States law).\n\n\n\nWhile these policies may simply signal how much Trump values loyalty, one\nother important 401(k) feature is lacking in the plan: automatic\nenrollment. The\nPGA was one of the latest organizations to dump the bombastic businessman,\nannouncing on Tuesday that it would not hold its 2015 Grand Slam of Golf\ntournament at a Trump golf course in Los Angeles.\n\n\n\nAll told, the loss of income could add up to millions of dollars. But until\nTrump files detailed financial disclosure forms, it is difficult to\nestimate just how hard his profits may take a hit. Trump\'s assets tied to\nthe Miss Universe, Miss USA and Miss Teen USA pageants that he partially\nowns and were dropped by Univision and NBC are estimated to be around $15\nmillion.\n\n\n\nThat\'s a large sum of money but to a self-claimed multi-billionaire like\nTrump, it\'s small change. Trump says his net worth is close to $9 billion.\nAbout a third of that -- $3.3 billion -- is tied up in "real estate\nlicensing deals, brand and branded developments," according to a summary of\nTrump\'s net worth as of last year. The vast majority of the rest of Trump\'s\nassets are in residential and commercial properties, as well as real estate\ninvestments.\n\n\n\nSome experts say these assets would be largely shielded from the corporate\nbacklash. With a super\nPAC called \xe2\x80\x9cUnintimidated\xe2\x80\x9d \xe2\x80\x94 named for the biographical book Walker\npublished about his battles in Wisconsin \xe2\x80\x94 the candidate and his advisers\nare confident as they look ahead to the campaign.\n\n\n\nThey consider Walker uniquely equipped among the candidates to appeal\nacross the spectrum of the Republican Party. \xe2\x80\x9cThere are three legs of the\nstool,\xe2\x80\x9d campaign manager Rick Wiley said in an interview. \xe2\x80\x9cWe play in all\nthree. Who else does?\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nSome of Walker\xe2\x80\x99s competitors will no doubt try to prove his team wrong in\nthat.\n\n\n\nTea party activists, Wiley said, like Walker\xe2\x80\x99s fighting style and that he\nwon multiple elections while under siege. His roots as the son of a Baptist\nminister and his faith give him a reach into the GOP\xe2\x80\x99s social conservative\nwing.\n\n\n\nBeyond that, advisers argued that \xe2\x80\x94 as a second-term governor who has\nraised more than $80 million for his Wisconsin campaigns \xe2\x80\x94 Walker has\nappeal in establishment circles, even if he can\xe2\x80\x99t match Bush\xe2\x80\x99s fundraising\nprowess.\n\n\n\nWalker\xe2\x80\x99s path to victory, as outlined by his closest advisers, is not\nsignificantly different from that of his rivals, but his team says the\ncalendar sets up well for him.\n\n\n\nIowa is the key: Walker is leading the polls there and, as a neighboring\ngovernor, he has easy access to the state. His advisers expect him to win\nthe Iowa caucuses early next year, and they say he can follow that with\ntop-three finishes in New Hampshire and South Carolina. They also think he\ncan score an early victory in Nevada\xe2\x80\x99s caucuses.\n\n\n\nWalker\xe2\x80\x99s advisers doubt that anyone who doesn\xe2\x80\x99t win one of the four early\nstates will move to the heavy schedule of contests in March. They also\ndoubt that anyone will have enough delegates to clinch the nomination by\nthe end of March, and they anticipate that the race will drag on into May\nbefore there is a winner.\n\n\n\nThe enthusiastic reaction to Walker\xe2\x80\x99s speech at the January GOP forum in\nIowa produced some obvious dividends. The sudden and positive attention\nhelped with fundraising and grass-roots organizing. But the scrutiny that\ncame with it, compounded by Walker\xe2\x80\x99s wobbly handling of various issues,\nbrought the team its first crisis.\n\n\n\nAt the time, Walker was just beginning to build his campaign. He lacked the\ninfrastructure to deal with the self-inflicted wounds. \xe2\x80\x9cNone of our senior\nstaff had even been to Madison,\xe2\x80\x9d Wiley said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s amazing we survived.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nThe small team stepped up its recruiting and brought on policy advisers who\ncould provide Walker with briefings to become more fluent in key issues. By\nthe end of March, the campaign decided to scale back. For the next month or\nso, Walker made few public appearances, concentrating on policy briefings\nand fundraising meetings.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe had to slow it down,\xe2\x80\x9d Wiley said.\n\n\n\nWalker formed his first committee last winter, a \xe2\x80\x9c527\xe2\x80\x9d that allowed him to\nraise money but did not advocate directly for him as a candidate. The super\nPAC was formed in April. Walker has held at least 30 meetings with\nprospective donors since then, said longtime adviser Keith Gilkes, who\nheads the super PAC.\n\n\n\nThe combined take for the two committees during the first six months of the\nyear is expected to top $20 million when reports are issued later this\nmonth. The super PAC has commitments for an additional $5 million or so,\nGilkes said, and hopes to raise at least $20 million by the end of the\nyear, giving it $40 million to start with in 2016.\n\n\n\nWalker advisers said his past battles in Wisconsin have given him the kind\nof grass-roots foundation that no other candidate can match. He has a list\nof 300,000 or so donors, and his super PAC had more than 200 donors as of a\nfew weeks ago. Walker advisers said they think that is smaller than Bush\xe2\x80\x99s\nsuper PAC but larger than those of most of the other candidates.\n\n\n\nBeyond that, advisers said, Walker has a list of e-mail addresses that\nnumbers about 700,000. One adviser said that is substantially more than\nMitt Romney had by the time he had wrapped up the 2012 GOP nomination.\n\n\n\nWalker has come under fresh criticism recently for changing his position on\nimmigration \xe2\x80\x94 he once supported a path to citizenship for those here\nillegally \xe2\x80\x94 and for changing his tone, if not his position, on same-sex\nmarriage and abortion.\n\n\n\nGilkes said Walker has not changed his stance on those two issues, although\nhe suggested that the governor\xe2\x80\x99s priorities are more fiscal and economic\nthan social. \xe2\x80\x9cHis beliefs never change,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.\n\n\n\nAnother adviser said Walker\xe2\x80\x99s call for a constitutional amendment to give\nstates the right to define marriage would end up being a plus, saying Rubio\nand Bush probably hurt themselves among social conservatives by not\nreacting more vigorously to last month\xe2\x80\x99s Supreme Court decision that\nlegalized same-sex marriage.\n\n\n\nWalker advisers discount possible threats from others in the establishment\nwing such as Ohio Gov. John Kasich and New Jersey Gov. Chris Christie. Nor\ndo they see a major threat yet in Iowa from those competing hardest for the\nsocial and religious conservatives.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cMy feeling is every single one of the candidates is focused on Walker in\nIowa,\xe2\x80\x9d Gilkes said. \xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t think that\xe2\x80\x99s ever going to let up.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nWalker\xe2\x80\x99s team has conducted two focus groups in Iowa. It has concluded\nthat, although he is not well known, the governor has significant\nopportunities to expand his appeal. The focus group was shown various\nvideos about Walker and were receptive to the portrayal of his record in\nWisconsin. \xe2\x80\x9cWe have so much to work with,\xe2\x80\x9d Wiley said.\n\n\n\nFor months, Walker\xe2\x80\x99s team has been preparing for a race against Bush\xe2\x80\x99s\nmoney and Rubio\xe2\x80\x99s compelling personal story. Advisers said Walker\xe2\x80\x99s record\nas governor is more current than Bush\xe2\x80\x99s and draws a sharper contrast with\nPresident Obama. Rubio has attributes that Walker has spoken about\nfavorably in private conversations, but the governor\xe2\x80\x99s campaign advisers\nconsider the first-term senator far less tested.\n\n\n\nWalker\xe2\x80\x99s announcement tour will take him from Wisconsin to Nevada, South\nCarolina, New Hampshire and then back to Iowa for several days of\ncampaigning. In New Hampshire, he will hold one town hall meeting. He will\nreturn to that state later in the month for an event that includes a\nHarley-Davidson motorcycle ride.\n\n\n\nHis announcement speech will focus heavily on his record in Wisconsin,\nreprising his fights with unions. As for his promise to put forth \xe2\x80\x9cbig and\nbold\xe2\x80\x9d ideas, one adviser said not to expect that in the announcement. Any\nsuch policies will be introduced later in the year.\n\n\n\n*Tea partiers and liberals tell Gov. Scott Walker: \xe2\x80\x98No more games on Common\nCore\xe2\x80\x99\n<http://www.washingtonpost.com/blogs/answer-sheet/wp/2015/07/07/tea-partiers-and-liberals-tell-gov-scott-walker-no-more-games-on-common-core/>\n// WaPo // Valerie Strauss \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nGov. Scott Walker of Wisconsin, who is expected soon to announce his bid\nfor the 2016 Republican presidential nomination, has been inconsistent at\nbest on the Common Core State Standards, being for it before being against\nit. Now he is being called out on his Core position by an unusual coalition\nof groups and individuals \xe2\x80\x94 in an open letter titled \xe2\x80\x9cNo More Games on\nCommon Core\xe2\x80\x9d \xe2\x80\x94 that includes tea parties across Wisconsin as well as\nliberals and libertarians.\n\n\n\nThe group of signatories to the letter accuses the governor of pretending\nto be against Common Core but not taking the steps required to eliminate it\nin Wisconsin. A Walker spokesman says  the governor is acting to give\nWisconsin school districts the freedom to do what they want on the Core.\n(See full statement below.)\n\n\n\nHere\xe2\x80\x99s some Walker history regarding the Common Core:\n\n\n\nIn 2011, his first budget for Wisconsin called for creation of a test that\nwas aligned to the Core standards, which were in place in the state before\nhe became governor.  A reading task force he chaired issued a report in\nJanuary 2012 expressing support for the Core, and as the Milwaukee Journal\nSentinel reported here, Walker was seen as being \xe2\x80\x9con board\xe2\x80\x9d with the Core\nin the first half of 2013 by Alan J. Borsuk, an education fellow at\nMarquette University, in a Journal Sentinel commentary.\n\n\n\nBut things began to change in 2013, when his second budget, while not\nrescinding the standards, directed the state Department of Public\nInstruction to stop ordering districts to continue implementing the Core.\nIn January 2014, the Journal Sentinel reported, he said he was creating a\ncommission to take a new look at the standards, and in July of that year,\nhe called for the Core to be rescinded in Wisconsin. That seems pretty\nconcrete, but in early 2015, his message was that he didn\xe2\x80\x99t want Wisconsin\ndistricts required to use the Core if they didn\xe2\x80\x99t want to, which is less\nthan an full-out repeal.\n\n\n\nIn his latest budget request, Walker has defunded the Common Core\nassessment developed by the multi-state, federally funded Smarter Balanced\nAssessment Consortium and now has the state looking for a new\n\xe2\x80\x9caccountability\xe2\x80\x9d test. But there are questions about what the state is\nlooking for in a new test and whether it can still be aligned to the Common\nCore. If the new state accountability exam is aligned to the Core,\ndistricts would have little choice but to choose to implement the Common\nCore standards, even if they were permitted not to.\n\n\n\nOpposition to the Common Core has been rising for years from across the\npolitical spectrum with concerns including problems with the content of the\nstandards and the developmental inappropriateness of those for the earliest\ngrades, the design of the new tests, how the new exams were written and by\nwhom, and the federal government\xe2\x80\x99s funding of new standardized tests\naligned to the Core. Some far-right wing conservatives have taken criticism\nof the Core to ridiculous extremes; Phyllis Schlafly, for example, says it\nactively promotes gay marriage and Glenn Beck has called the standards\ninitiative \xe2\x80\x9cevil\xe2\x80\x9d and an attempt to impose \xe2\x80\x9ccommunism\xe2\x80\x9d on America.  The\nFreedom Project, affiliated with the radical right John Birch Society, has\nsaid the Core is an \xe2\x80\x9cabsolute appropriation of Soviet ideology and\npropaganda.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nBut a coalition of groups \xe2\x80\x93 mostly tea parties and other hard-right\nconservatives \xe2\x80\x94 have just issued the letter calling for Walker to take a\ndefinitive stand on Common Core and Core testing in language that was\nsensible enough for some liberals and libertarians to sign on. Here\xe2\x80\x99s the\nletter, and following it is the full comment from a Walker spokesperson in\nMadison.\n\n\n\n*Scott Walker hoping new bundlers help vault him over fundraising hurdles\n<http://www.cnn.com/2015/07/07/politics/scott-walker-campaign-fundraising-strategy/index.html>\n// CNN // Sara Murray \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nWhen you\'re up against a candidate who belongs to a political dynasty and\nhas a fundraising network that spans decades, there is perhaps only one\noption: Bring in new blood.\n\n\n\nAs Wisconsin Gov. Scott Walker readies his likely presidential campaign,\none of his biggest near-term hurdles is building a war chest that will\nallow him to face off against well-funded opponents.\n\n\n\nTo do that his team said it is targeting a new generation of bundlers by\ntapping into the network of more than 350,000 potential donors who\nsupported the governor in his recall election and turning to entrepreneurs\nwho\'ve launched new businesses in the last five to 10 years.\n\n\n\n"Our donor is not the tried and true Republican donor in New York City\nthat\'s given to everybody since Reagan," said Anthony Scaramucci, who is\nthe founder of investment firm SkyBridge Capital and is raising money for\nWalker. "We don\'t have the mercenary donor that\'s paying for past political\nfavors."\n\n\n\nJon Hammes, founder of a health care consulting company in Wisconsin, will\nserve a national finance co-chairman for the campaign, along with Todd\nRicketts, co-owner of the Chicago Cubs, according to a source familiar with\nthe plans. The move combines a veteran campaign fundraiser -- Hammes has\nraised money previous Republican nominees, including Mitt Romney and\nArizona Sen. John McCain -- with a big dollar donor who is still relatively\nnew to the political fundraising scene. This will be Ricketts\' first role\nwithin a presidential campaign.\n\n\n\nTheir goal is to build an army of bundlers like Genevieve Hillis, a\n34-year-old lobbyist in Chicago for a health care equipment company. Hillis\nhelped Walker raise money for his gubernatorial campaign and grew that\nnetwork of supporters during his recall election. Now she\'s preparing to\ntake on her biggest role yet in a presidential campaign, helping to bring\nin new donors and introduce Walker to potential high-dollar supporters he\nmight not otherwise meet.\n\n\n\n"I haven\'t encountered anybody that was a supporter in the recall that\nisn\'t going to be a supporter in the presidential," Hillis said, although\nshe acknowledged fundraising for a candidate in a crowded presidential\nfield is a different battle than raising money for a recall race outside of\nthe normal campaign cycle.\n\n\n\nWalker\'s team isn\'t above courting the moneyed donors other campaigns are\nchasing either. Hillis often speaks to potential donors who are drawn to\nWalker and might be inclined to give hundreds of thousands of dollars, but\nthey are also being courted by the Bush campaign. Her pitch: Let me get you\non the phone with the governor.\n\n\n\n"Scott is willing to have very frank conversations," Hillis said. "He\'s\nwilling to be educated on a subject and open to changing his mind. He\'s a\nreasonable person."\n\n\n\nWalker\'s allies said they don\'t expect him to be among the most flush in\nthe field this quarter. Former Florida Gov. Jeb Bush is expected to raise a\njaw-dropping sum for the quarter that ended June 30. Texas Sen. Ted Cruz\nand the super PAC supporting him claim to have raise nearly $50 million\ncombined.\n\n\n\nWhile the first reporting period is significant, members of Walker\'s team\nsaid they are focused on building a team of bundlers who can steadily\nbroaden his financial base by pitching the governor\'s message to an\never-widening circle of new donors.\n\n\n\n"I\'m looking for the people, men or women, that are focused on being\ninvolved in the process aggressively," said Michael Morgan, 44 years old,\nwho is raising money for Walker. "If that means raising thousands of\ndollars at the start, I\'m happy with it. Hopefully that will graduate to\ntens of thousands of dollars."\n\n\n\nMorgan is no stranger to political fundraising. He organized the finance\noperations for Sen. Mark Kirk\'s House and Senate bids and remains a staunch\nsupporter of the Illinois Republican. But Morgan\'s upcoming stint as one of\nWalker\'s finance co-chairs in Illinois will be his most prominent role in a\npresident campaign.\n\n\n\nWalker\'s "testing-the-waters committee," a precursor to his official\ncampaign, is asking bundlers to raise $27,000 by July 12th. Morgan said it\ntook him just four days to surpass that goal. All of the early contributor\nwere under the age of 50.\n\n\n\n"It\'s been a good pace I would say," Morgan said of his fundraising efforts\nso far. "Now that the announcement is imminent there\'s a lot more interest."\n\n\n\n*Scott Walker plans post-announcement blitz, NH stops\n<http://www.unionleader.com/article/20150707/NEWS0605/150709414#sthash.JJvNbTY3.dpuf>\n// Union Leader // Dan Tuohy \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nWisconsin Gov. The other\nRepublican yet to announce is Ohio Gov. John Kasich.\n\n\n\n*Scott Walker\'s Home Crowd Disadvantage\n<http://www.usnews.com/opinion/blogs/jamie-stiehm/2015/07/07/can-wisconsin-gov-scott-walker-win-over-home-state-crowd-in-2016-bid>\n// US News // Jamie Stiehm \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nUnder the July sun, you may spot political squalls on the horizon of this\ngreen city\'s Lake Mendota. That\'s what you get when a Republican red\ngovernor runs for president in a state that usually breaks Democratic blue\non the electoral map.\n\n\n\nWhether that governor would actually carry his own state \xe2\x80\x93 with a fairly\nliberal, active electorate \xe2\x80\x93 in the general presidential election in 2016\nis quite the parlor game.\n\n\n\nWord\'s going door to door in this capital city that Gov. Scott Walker is\nofficially running for president, with a launch planned on July 13. All the\ntalk about him walking the walk to the White House is getting real now,\nhere in the state where the Republican Party itself was founded in the\n1850s: Wisconsin. This is also a state, by the way, where the Progressive\nParty has deep roots.\n\n\n\nWalker plans to make political hay out of being the only Midwesterner in\nthe Republican presidential field, now top-heavy with Southerners. "Midwest\n[is] key to Walker strategy," the Wisconsin State Journal noted. Riding his\nHarley-Davidson (the company is headquartered in Milwaukee) is part of the\nplain folks image. Of course, if Ohio Gov. John Kasich jumps into the pool\nof contenders, that could change the Walker formula that starts with a\nstrong early victory in next-door Iowa come the frigid chill of February.\n(Only a Midwesterner knows how bad it can be.)\n\n\n\nBut feelings about Walker are decidedly mixed here in the state capital,\nwith some bitter memories of a movement to recall him that failed. Walker\nsurvived the challenge to his approach on collective bargaining with public\nemployees. The victory made him a conservative media darling in the\nnational spotlight a few years back. It also attracted checks from the\nconservative Koch brothers. Walker was subsequently re-elected governor,\nbut his support in Wisconsin has been "waning" recently, according to the\nWisconsin State Journal.\n\n\n\nHere\'s the irony: The harder Walker runs to the right to cement his\nposition as a conservative front-runner for his party\'s primary nomination,\nthe less popular he is at home, even with Republican state lawmakers. A\nmove to clamp down on the state\'s open-records law just went awry.The\nacademic community of the University of Wisconsin is warily anticipating\nyet another showdown: Walker may (or may not) declare war on the\ntraditional tenure system. That\'s sure to win him debating points and\nvotes, but might hurt him here at home. Another weakness Walker will likely\nbe forced to face: His 2010 campaign promise to create a ton of new jobs is\nfalling flat in Wisconsin\'s sluggish economy.\n\n\n\nWalker is not a guy people feel neutral about, a stand-out even in a\npolarized era. Curiously, his political idol is Ronald Reagan, yet he has\nnone of the genial charm that helped Reagan voters cross political lines.\nAs my dad, a Wisconsinite, observed, most politicians like to be liked, but\nnot Walker. Indeed the governor seems to relish his unpopularity with the\nother side, refusing to moderate harsh opposition to reproductive rights\nand to same-sex marriage. And he\'s enraged University of Wisconsin\nsupporters by suggesting budget cuts for the renowned research institution,\nwhile proposing the Milwaukee Bucks receive millions of public funds for a\nnew professional basketball arena.\n\n\n\nHere in bookish Madison, anyway, it balances out well: Many in the liberal\nprofessoriate love to hate Walker, and, by some law of political physics,\nhe loves to be hated by them. The governor\'s mansion in Maple Bluff is on\nthe other side of Lake Mendota from the university\'s colorful Memorial\nUnion Terrace.\n\n\n\nLucky. But watch for squalls.\n\n\n\n*The magical, disappearing Scott Walker conversation\n<http://www.msnbc.com/rachel-maddow-show/the-magical-disappearing-scott-walker-conversation>\n// MSNBC // Steve Benen \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nThe chief economist at the Heritage Foundation is itself an awkward title \xe2\x80\x93\nthe Republican think tank has moved away from its pretense of rigorous\npolicy analysis \xe2\x80\x93 but the job belongs to Stephen Moore. From last night\xe2\x80\x99s New York Times report: \xe2\x80\x9cSo, what exactly is Mr.\nWalker\xe2\x80\x99s current position on immigration? Asked if he supported any path to\ncitizenship or legal status for illegal immigrants, Mr. Walker\xe2\x80\x99s\nspokeswoman, AshLee Strong, did not directly respond.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n*Busted!: Walker Admits Role in Failed Government Secrecy Rule\n<http://talkingpointsmemo.com/livewire/walker-admits-role-open-records> //\nTPM // Tierney Sneed \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nAfter days of dodging questions about whether Wisconsin Gov. Scott Walker\n(R) was involved in a failed proposal to dismantle the state\'s open records\nlaw, the governor\'s office confirmed Tuesday that his office was involved\nin the measure.\n\n\n\n"Legislative leaders let us know that they were interested in making\nchanges to the open records law. In response, our staff provided input\nregarding these proposed changes," Laurel Patrick, the press secretary for\nthe governor, said in an email to TPM.\n\n\n\n"Our intent with these changes was to encourage a deliberative process with\nstate agencies in developing policy and legislation. This allows for robust\ndebate with state agencies and public employees over the merit of policies\nand proposed initiatives as they are being formed, while ensuring materials\nrelated to final proposals, as well as information related to external\nstakeholders seeking to influence public policy, would remain fully\ntransparent."\n\n\n\nThe admission came shortly after Republican legislative leaders said Walker\naides had been involved in writing the proposal, which would have removed\ncertain communications and other legislative documents from under the scope\nof the state\'s transparency laws and would have permitted lawmakers not to\ncomply with other kinds of public records requests.\n\n\n\nThe language was initially approved by a party-line vote in the\nlegislature\'s Joint Finance Committee late Thursday evening before the\nholiday weekend, as part of a larger budget package known as Motion 999. As\nbacklash began to mount, Walker, joined by top GOP state lawmakers,\nannounced Saturday that the provisions would be dropped from the package.\n\n\n\nScrutiny continued, however, as to whether Walker was behind the measure,\nas he faces a lawsuit for refusing to turn over certain documents in a\npublic records request.\n\n\n\nSome Republican lawmakers in the state have continued to defend the effort,\nand say they will try to move alterations to public records law forward as\nstandalone legislation that would go through the typical public review\nprocess, instead of attaching it to a budget bill.\n\n\n\n"Our focus remains on ensuring open and accountable government and we\nencourage public debate and discussion of any potential future changes to\nthe state\'s open records law," Patrick, the governor\'s spokeswoman, said in\nthe email\n\n\n\n*KASICH*\n\n\n\n*Kasich: Obama administration \xe2\x80\x98in love\xe2\x80\x99 with Iran deal\n<http://www.foxnews.com/politics/2015/07/07/kasich-obama-administration-in-love-with-iran-deal/>\n// Fox News \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nGov. John Kasich, R-Ohio, said on \xe2\x80\x9cSpecial Report with Bret Baier\xe2\x80\x9d Tuesday\nthat the Obama administration\xe2\x80\x99s push for a nuclear deal with Iran shows\n\xe2\x80\x9cit\'s very dangerous to fall in love with your own idea.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI think the administration has probably fallen in love with the fact that\nthey want to get an agreement, and when people are hyperventilating and\nunable to get one, sometimes they go and they sign something that they\nshouldn\'t,\xe2\x80\x9d said Kasich, who is expected to announce his intention to run\nfor president in the upcoming weeks.\n\n\n\nNegotiators from Iran, Britain, China, France, Germany, Russia and the\nUnited States meeting in Vienna did not meet their self-imposed deadline on\nTuesday for an agreement on a deal to curb Iran\xe2\x80\x99s nuclear program. He was actually a\nbig senior adviser to McCain. Last time I checked, he was the nominee a few\nelection cycles ago.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nMaking his pitch, Kasich referenced his re-election in 2014. \xe2\x80\x9cI won 86 out\nof 88 counties, 63 percent of the women vote, 51 percent of union\nhouseholds in one of the largest victories in Ohio history. There must be\nsomething that I\xe2\x80\x99m doing right there in order to do that in what\xe2\x80\x99s one of\nthe most pivotal states.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nKasich also portrayed himself as someone who gets the struggles of regular\npeople.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m John Kasich,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m not anybody else. I come from McKees\nRocks. My father carried mail on his back. I\xe2\x80\x99ve lived in a town where if\nthe wind blew the wrong way, people found themselves out of work. And I\nthink I understand the anxieties of people in this country, many of whom\nare middle class, who wonder if the American dream is over. And I don\xe2\x80\x99t\nbelieve that it is.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nAdded Kasich: \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99ve had a lot of blessings in my life. The Lord\xe2\x80\x99s been good\nto me. And I\xe2\x80\x99m going to do my best to lead and to improve people\xe2\x80\x99s lives\nwhether I sit in the White House or whether in the white house in Lanetta\nAvenue in Westerville Ohio in being governor.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nKasich said he is in town visiting former colleagues and for a meeting of\nhis new steering committee of lawmakers and members of the business\ncommunity this evening.\n\n\n\nThe governor said he brought his twin daughters along for the Washington\ntrip too. \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99ve learned an awful lot about Snapchat.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n*OTHER*\n\n\n\n*Candidates Start Showing Their Cards\n<http://www.bloomberg.com/politics/articles/2015-07-08/candidates-start-showing-their-cards>\n// Bloomberg // Joshua Gallu - July 8, 2015*\n\n\n\nKa-CHING! Some candidates and super-PACs just can\'t wait for the filing\ndeadlines to share their good new$.\n\n\n\nThe 2016 presidential money race is starting to take shape and early\nindications are that the road ahead will be lined with bullion.\n\n\n\nAmong the candidates who have shared fundraising numbers, ahead of filing\ndeadlines later this month at the Federal Election Commission, Hillary\nClinton, not surprisingly, leads the Democratic field with  her campaign\nand allied groups reporting a combined war chest of nearly $70 million.\nEven Bernie Sanders, who describes himself as an independent socialist,\nsays he has already lined up $15 million, from primarily smaller donations,\nto wage his campaign.\n\n\n\nIn typical form, candidates with good news have come out touting their\nnumbers ahead of the official July 15 reporting date. Ted Cruz, who critics\nsaid would have trouble finding well-heeled backers, is boasting  a $51.2\nmillion arsenal, most of which in super-PACs, which can accept unlimited\namounts of money but can\'t coordinate directly with the campaign. The chart\nbelow outlines numbers reported by the candidates themselves, super-PACs\nthat are explicitly allied with and validated by presidential campaigns and\nother groups, such as 501(c)4 organizations that raise money to help a\nfavored candidate.\n\n\n\nNow, all eyes are on Jeb Bush. According to Buzzfeed, Bush\'s Right to Rise\nsuper-PAC says it has already pulled in enough money to give his opponents\n"heart attacks.\'"\n\n\n\n*Inside the GOP\xe2\x80\x99s Effort to Close the Campaign-Science Gap With Democrats\n<http://www.bloomberg.com/politics/features/2015-07-08/inside-the-gop-s-effort-to-close-the-campaign-science-gap-with-democrats>\n// Bloomberg // Sasha Issenberg - July 8, 2015 *\n\n\n\nA Republican group aims to emulate President Obama\xe2\x80\x99s campaigns by bringing\nrigorous testing to campaign tactics. One problem: Not enough Republican\nscientists.\n\n\n\nThis spring, the Cato Institute identified 600 Americans who read more than\n20 books per year and made arrangements to send them each one more. The\nlibertarian think tank split these readers into three groups. One group\nreceived a free copy of Ayn Rand\xe2\x80\x99s Atlas Shrugged, one got longtime Cato\nexecutive David Boaz\xe2\x80\x99s The Libertarian Mind, and one a book that Cato\nscholars considered a useful placebo to free-market doctrine: the Bible.\nAfter three months, six months, and 12 months, members of all three groups\nwould be surveyed to see if the unsolicited books they had received could\nexplain differential response rates to one question: Do you consider\nyourself a libertarian?\n\n\n\nThe Cato researcher behind the project explained to other members of a\nbelow-the-radar Republican group known as the Center for Strategic\nInitiatives, or CSI, that the 600 books were just part of a pilot test. If\nthe design appeared to work properly, the experiment would be replicated on\na larger scale: 12,000 books this time. \xe2\x80\x9cPolitical books have never been\ntested,\xe2\x80\x9d says David Kirby, now a vice president and senior fellow at Cato.\n\xe2\x80\x9cThink tanks think that books persuade people. Do they?\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nVery few other members of the CSI circle had ever used books as tools for\nchanging minds. A range of political consultants and vendors, they tended\nto trade in more ephemeral modes of communication: television ads and\nrobocalls, direct mail, digital ads, and door knocks. But they were there\nfor the same reason that Kirby had been willing to entertain the perfidy of\nusing Cato resources to question whether reading Ayn Rand actually led\npeople to libertarianism\xe2\x80\x94a willingness to take everything they thought they\nknew about what works in politics and hold it up to empirical\ninvestigation.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe were disappointed in 2012 with how much money we spent and how little\nwe had to show for it.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nDavid Kirby, vice president and senior fellow, Cato Institute\n\nThe mere existence of the CSI field experiments seminar represents the\nright\xe2\x80\x99s most constructive engagement with the continued traumas of its loss\nin the 2012 Presidential race\xe2\x80\x94not just the fact that it had lost, but that\nit didn\xe2\x80\x99t know at the time it was losing, and even afterward was at a\nfurther loss to understand how or why it had done so. While many\nRepublicans responded by conceding catch-phrase-ready deficiencies\xe2\x80\x94a need\nto do more and better with Big Data or the Ground Game\xe2\x80\x94others were willing\nto acknowledge that the underlying problem was the lack of a culture within\nthe GOP to encourage innovation. For a small but significant share of the\nparty\xe2\x80\x99s electioneering class, however, any true reckoning with 2012 invites\na deeper epistemological crisis about how to run smarter campaigns in the\n21st century.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe should not assume anything. Absolutely every aspect of the campaign,\nfrom the best way to knock on doors to the best way to broadcast\ntelevision, should be tested,\xe2\x80\x9d says Blaise Hazelwood, a Republican\nvoter-contact specialist who founded CSI. \xe2\x80\x9cThis is the way I did it on this\ncampaign that won, so this is the way we should do it on all campaigns,\xe2\x80\x9d\nHazelwood says, mocking the prevailing sentiment of entrenched political\nconsultants. \xe2\x80\x9cThe test for them is whether they win or lose on election\nday. That cannot be a valid test.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nThe conservative establishment has a long tradition of organized\ngatherings. First there were Paul Weyrich\xe2\x80\x99s weekly \xe2\x80\x9ccoalitions\xe2\x80\x9d lunches,\nheld on Wednesdays when Congress was in session. Anti-tax activist Grover\nNorquist later claimed the breakfast slot that day, his sessions focused\nmore on economic policy than social issues. Donors and journalists in New\nYork started meeting one Monday per month for an hour and a half; after\nrelocating to South Carolina, Monday Meeting founder Mallory Factor took\nthe concept south with him, launching the Charleston Meeting. All these\nwere devoted to ideological cohesion and legislative strategy, the matching\nof like-minded donors and politicians. They tended to reaffirm certainties,\nrather than challenge them.\n\n\n\nThe CSI circle has yet to fall into a reliable schedule, and its\ngatherings\xe2\x80\x94which now take place roughly every six weeks or so at Cato\xe2\x80\x99s\nWashington headquarters\xe2\x80\x94already mark a very different mode of\ncollaboration. There is not a politician in sight, or many brand-name\noperatives; few attendees appear to be over the age of 40. This sphere of\npolitical operatives and party hacks angling to remake Republican campaigns\nincludes strategists and tacticians for many of the party\xe2\x80\x99s top\npresidential candidates, along with staffers from the Republican National\nCommittee and consultants attached to various elements of the Koch\npolitical network.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI sense it\xe2\x80\x99s one of the few places where the warring factions of the\nconservative side of the aisle play together in the same sandbox,\xe2\x80\x9d says\nColumbia University political scientist Don Green, who has advised the\ngroup since its launch. \xe2\x80\x9cYou have people who are close to the Tea Party and\npeople who are antagonistic towards the Tea Party, and they\xe2\x80\x99re all trying\nto learn from the same research method.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nAbout 50 people responded to Hazelwood\xe2\x80\x99s invitation to gather at Cato in\nearly June and, arrayed before her that Thursday afternoon, at long tables\nin lecture-hall formation, the schisms of the Republican Party in the early\ndays of the presidential campaign were unmistakable. One of the people she\nhad invited to present research that day came from Deep Root Analytics,\nwhich former Florida Governor Jeb Bush\'s presidential campaign has hired to\nhelp target its television ads. Another presenter represented FLC Connect,\na phone vendor that has worked for Wisconsin Governor Scott Walker and has\nclose links to his campaign-in-waiting. A pair of analysts from 0ptimus\nconsulting, now advising Florida Senator Marco Rubio, sat in the back of\nthe room, not far from where the founders of Targeted Victory, the firm\nformer Texas Governor Rick Perry has hired to handle digital advertising\nand media analytics, found seats after arriving a few minutes after  the\nscheduled 3:30 start time. Hazelwood herself is a longtime advisor to\nLouisiana Governor Bobby Jindal, through her firm Grassroots Consulting,\nand has since joined his allied super-PAC as a consultant. She began by\nreminding those in attendance of CSI\xe2\x80\x99s one rule: What they were about to\nhear was off the record. \xe2\x80\x9cAsk questions like you usually do,\xe2\x80\x9d she said.\n\xe2\x80\x9cAttack our speakers, like sometimes happens.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nHazelwood has been asking and answering some of the toughest questions in\nRepublican politics for years. Shortly after the 2012 elections, she faced\none from Sally Bradshaw: What did Republicans need to do to improve their\nelectoral mechanics? A longtime adviser to Bush, Bradshaw was one of five\nparty eminences who had been tapped by Republican National Committee\nChairman Reince Priebus to oversee the Growth and Opportunity Project, the\npostmortem report its authors were repeatedly instructed not to describe\npublicly as an \xe2\x80\x9cautopsy.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nTwelve years earlier, Hazelwood had been in a similar position when, as the\nRNC\xe2\x80\x99s political director, she had organized what was known as the 72-Hour\nTask Force to fine-tune field operations that Karl Rove and other top\nadvisers to President George W. Bush blamed for his unexpectedly narrow\nvictory. Starting in 2001, Hazelwood deployed dozens of controlled tests in\nlow-profile elections, usually with the goal of convincing party officials\nand activists that it was worth investing in the infrastructure to support\nvolunteer-based voter contact. (Many of those tests were modeled on the\ntypes of field experiments conducted by social scientists, although not\nconducted to academic standards.)\n\n\n\nMany Republicans credited the findings of the 72-Hour Task Force with\nhelping Bush in his re-election, but after his victory, the culture that\nhad incubated them withered away.
