The thinly veiled threat underneath all\nthis outrage is that the media will react to being treated badly by giving\nthe candidate bad press, but it\xe2\x80\x99s pretty clear that train left the station\na long time ago when it comes to Clinton, so the cost-benefit analysis\nprobably doesn\xe2\x80\x99t argue in favor of the campaign giving a damn either.\n\n\n\nAs it happens, another political reporter wrote a piece about the way the\npress covers Hillary Clinton yesterday and it was quite a blockbuster\nconfessional. Jonathan Allen of Vox laid it all out:\n\n\n\nThe Clinton rules are driven by reporters\xe2\x80\x99 and editors\xe2\x80\x99 desire to score the\nultimate prize in contemporary journalism: the scoop that brings down\nHillary Clinton and her family\xe2\x80\x99s political empire. At least in that way,\nRepublicans and the media have a common interest.\n\n\n\nI understand these dynamics well, having co-written a book that\ndemonstrated how Bill and Hillary Clinton used Hillary\xe2\x80\x99s time at State to\nbuild the family political operation and set up for their fourth\npresidential campaign. That is to say, I\xe2\x80\x99ve done a lot of research about\nthe Clintons\xe2\x80\x99 relationship with the media, and experienced it firsthand. As\nan author, I felt that I owed it to myself and the reader to report,\ninvestigate, and write with the same mix of curiosity, skepticism, rigor,\nand compassion that I would use with any other subject. I wanted to sell\nbooks, of course. But the easier way to do that \xe2\x80\x94 proven over time \xe2\x80\x94 is to\nwrite as though the Clintons are the purest form of evil. The same holds\nfor daily reporting. Want to drive traffic to a website? Write something\nnasty about a Clinton, particularly Hillary.\n\n\n\nAs a reporter, I get sucked into playing by the Clinton rules. This is what\nI\xe2\x80\x99ve seen in my colleagues, and in myself.\n\n\n\nThis does not come as a surprise to many observers. It\xe2\x80\x99s been obvious for\nmore than 20 years. But it\xe2\x80\x99s refreshing to see a journalist admit that the\ndynamic is driven by the media\xe2\x80\x99s Ahab-like obsession with bringing down\nHillary Clinton \xe2\x80\x94 and that this means they have a common interest with\nRepublicans. It\xe2\x80\x99s not ideological, it\xe2\x80\x99s professional.\n\n\n\nAllen goes on to list the unofficial rules for covering the Clintons and\nelaborates on each one. (There are, by his reckoning, five.) He notes that\nthe media must always assume that the Clintons are acting in bad faith\nuntil proven otherwise, that everything is newsworthy (even things that\nreally are nobody\xe2\x80\x99s business) because the Clintons are like America\xe2\x80\x99s royal\nfamily, and because everything Hillary Clinton does is, so the thinking\ngoes, \xe2\x80\x9cfake and calculated.\xe2\x80\x9d These assumptions distort political coverage\nin a dozen different ways. But it\xe2\x80\x99s two rules in particular which should be\nof very serious concern to the public.\n\n\n\nThe first is, \xe2\x80\x9ceverything, no matter how ludicrous-sounding, is worthy of a\nfull investigation by federal agencies, Congress, the \xe2\x80\x98vast right-wing\nconspiracy,\xe2\x80\x99 and mainstream media outlets.\xe2\x80\x9d Allen notes that the Clintons\nhave been investigated for 25 years and have probably revealed more about\ntheir lives, some of it intensely personal, than any other people in\nAmerican public life. This has made them protective of their privacy and,\nperhaps perversely, fatalistic about the media\xe2\x80\x99s hostility. But he also\nnotes something that we should acknowledge is a big problem for our\npolitics:\n\n\n\nThis is, for Republicans, a reasonable strategy. They know that if they\nkeep investigating her, it will do two things: keep the media writing about\nscandals that might knock her out, and turn off voters who don\xe2\x80\x99t want a\nreturn to the bloodsport politics of the 1990s. They leak partial stories\nto reporters hungry for that one great scoop that will give them the\nbiggest political scalp of them all.\n\n\n\nHe points out that the Republicans are never able to deliver, which often\nplays into Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s hands, but that\xe2\x80\x99s hardly a justification for the\nmedia\xe2\x80\x99s behavior. There is nothing new about this arrangement. This was\nexactly what happened back in the 1990s. It\xe2\x80\x99s embarrassing for the press\nthat so many of their ranks are either unaware of this history, don\xe2\x80\x99t care\nabout it, or are taking up the challenge to harpoon that big fish without\nhaving the slightest compunction about being used by political operatives\nfor partisan purposes. It\xe2\x80\x99s tragic for our country that after the\nridiculous spectacle of impeachment, a stolen election, the war in Iraq,\nand an epic economic meltdown that our political media is still this\nshallow. That they are willing to enable this three-ring circus that calls\nitself today\xe2\x80\x99s Republican Party in order to gain power is frightening.\n\n\n\nAllen\xe2\x80\x99s other point is: \xe2\x80\x9cEvery allegation, no matter how ludicrous, is\nbelievable until it can be proven completely and utterly false. And even\nthen, it keeps a life of its own in the conservative media world.\xe2\x80\x9d That\ncorrelates to another Clinton rule, which is the \xe2\x80\x9cWhere there\xe2\x80\x99s smoke\nthere\xe2\x80\x99s fire\xe2\x80\x9d tactic. The idea is for there to be so many accusations\nfloating around that a reasonable person must conclude that there\xe2\x80\x99s\nsomething to it, even if nothing has been proven. That, after all, is what\nBenghazi is all about.\n\n\n\nAllen writes:\n\n\n\nTerrorists killed four Americans. The conservative echo chamber seems\nconvinced Hillary Clinton is at fault. The reasonable argument to make is\nthat we shouldn\xe2\x80\x99t have been in Libya in the first place and the murders\nwere a down-the-chain result of bad policy. But the right wing wants to\nprove that they happened because of Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s actions \xe2\x80\x94 or inaction \xe2\x80\x94 on\nsecurity matters.\n\n\n\nThey\xe2\x80\x99ve talked about security requests denied for Libya (never mind that\nthe stronger contingent would have been in Tripoli, not Benghazi, and that\nthere\xe2\x80\x99s no evidence Clinton herself was aware of the requests), a\nstand-down order that prevented reinforcements from arriving in Benghazi\n(never mind that they wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t have gotten there until after the fighting\nwas done, and that even a House Republican committee found that there was\nno such order) and, most of absurd of all, that Clinton knew the attack was\ncoming. This is how Limbaugh put it in May.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe fact is they knew about the Benghazi attack 10 days before it was to\nhappen. They knew who did it.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nThe freedom of the conservative media to make wild allegations often acts\nas a bulldozer forcing reporters to check into the charges and, in doing\nso, repeat them. By the time they\xe2\x80\x99ve been debunked, they\xe2\x80\x99re part of the\nAmerican public\xe2\x80\x99s collective consciousness. Or, as it\xe2\x80\x99s been said, a lie\ngets around the world before the truth gets out of bed.\n\n\n\nThere\xe2\x80\x99s more to this, however, and it goes hand in hand with the previous\nrule. These investigations are little more than fishing expeditions in\nwhich Republicans demand more and more information and then selectively\nleak juicy bits to the press for partisan purposes. Trey Gowdy\xe2\x80\x99s Benghazi\nselect committee has descended into farce already, but that hasn\xe2\x80\x99t stopped\nthe New York Times from breathlessly reporting it like it\xe2\x80\x99s Watergate.\n\n\n\nBut it\xe2\x80\x99s not just The Times, although they\xe2\x80\x99ve been among the worst. Eric\nWemple of the Washington Post reported that Representative Elijah Cummings\ncame out swinging at Politico yesterday for running with leaked Clinton\nemails which they didn\xe2\x80\x99t actually see, based on intel from unidentified\n\xe2\x80\x9csources.\xe2\x80\x9d The selectively presented, and allegedly undisclosed, emails\ngave the appearance that Clinton was working hand-in-glove with adviser\nSidney Blumenthal to circulate Benghazi talking points from the Media\nMatters, where Blumenthal was then on payroll, inside the White House \xe2\x80\x94 an\ninsinuation used by Clinton detractors to suggest some sort of Benghazi\ncoverup.\n\n\n\nHowever, as the Washington Post explains:\n\n\n\nBut as Cummings notes in his letter, it didn\xe2\x80\x99t go down like that. The\n[Hillary Clinton email cited by Politico] actually attaches to a different\ne-mail correspondence between Clinton and Blumenthal, from a week before\nBlumenthal\xe2\x80\x99s boast about those Benghazi links. As documents released by the\nState Department last week show, Clinton was actually intent on sending to\nthe White House a Salon article claiming that the campaign of Republican\npresidential candidate Mitt Romney was planning a brand-new line of attack\nbased on Benghazi.\n\n\n\nCummings rips away, \xe2\x80\x9cIt appears that this source fed Politico an inaccurate\ncharacterization of these emails and that Politico accepted this\nmischaracterization without obtaining the emails themselves. The source\napparently took an email that was produced to the Select Committee in\nFebruary, isolated Secretary Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s statement about the White House,\nremoved it from the original email exchange about the presidential debates,\nand then added it to a different email exchange involving Media Matters.\xe2\x80\x9d\nAnother point: The Politico story cites a source as saying that the e-mail\nwasn\xe2\x80\x99t among those turned over by the State Department. Cummings writes\nthat State had passed it along in February.\n\n\n\nPolitico later issued a correction (which was clear as mud and clarified\nnothing).\n\n\n\nCummings is going to have his hands full trying to sort out these leaks.\nIt\xe2\x80\x99s a dirty job, but apparently he\xe2\x80\x99s decided that somebody has to do it,\nso that somebody will be him. It remains to be seen if his work to correct\nthe record of this Benghazi committee will have any effect. And who knows\nif Jonathan Allen\xe2\x80\x99s piece will be taken seriously by his fellow political\nreporters. It\xe2\x80\x99s clear they are using Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s lack of \xe2\x80\x9caccessibility\xe2\x80\x9d as a\nlame excuse for their sophomoric behavior, but it shouldn\xe2\x80\x99t take one of\ntheir own writing a Vox explainer on \xe2\x80\x9cthe Clinton rules\xe2\x80\x9d for them to\nunderstand that they are being willing dupes for Republican partisans who\nare laughing behind their backs at their credulousness.\n\n\n\nHillary Clinton doesn\xe2\x80\x99t need to be handled with kid gloves. The presidency\nis a tough job. But neither does she deserve to be held to a different\nstandard than anyone else or subject to a set of rules that are based upon\nlazy, false assumptions fed by partisans with an agenda they aren\xe2\x80\x99t even\ntrying to hide. The fact that the press is falling so comfortably into that\nold groove is a testament to the fact that nobody ever paid a price for\nwhat they did the first time.\n\n\n\n*Stop the bed-wetting: Hillary Clinton\'s doing fine\n<http://www.cnn.com/2015/07/07/opinions/pfeiffer-bedwetting-over-hillary-clinton/index.html>\n// CNN // Dan Pfeiffer \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nIt\'s officially bed-wetting season in the political world when it comes to\nHillary Clinton\'s campaign. With stories this week in Politico and The New\nYork Times about the newly competitive Democratic primary, the whispers\nhave begun about whether this is 2008 all over again. Back then, Clinton\nwas defeated by Obama, an insurgent, progressive outsider.\n\n\n\nBed-wetting is a term of art in Obamaland. In 2008, Obama\'s then campaign\nmanager David Plouffe made it famous in a New York Times article; it refers\nto the premature panic among pundits and party stalwarts alike during\ntrying political times. While bed-wetting is not an affliction exclusive to\na party, Democrats do seem to have a special affinity for it.\n\n\n\nWith Vermont Sen. (and presidential candidate) Bernie Sanders raising\nmillions, exciting progressives, drawing crowds and surging in the polls,\nit\'s suddenly the Summer of Sanders. Cue the second-guessing and the\nhandwringing over Clinton and her campaign strategy.\n\n\n\nBut while Clinton\'s campaign to date hasn\'t been perfect, she is doing\nexactly what she needs to do to ensure that she is the Democratic nominee\nand the 45th President of the United States.\n\n\n\nA little perspective:\n\n\n\nFirst, despite Sanders\' very impressive fundraising, Clinton outraised him\nby about $30 million. In the second quarter of 2007, Obama actually\noutraised Clinton. Sanders has surged in the polls, impressively\nconsolidating the anti-Clinton vote, but the latest polls have him down 40\npoints nationally and 19 points in Iowa.\n\n\n\nWhile Clinton had huge leads in national polls at this point in 2007, Obama\nwas always in striking distance in the early states. This cycle, the party\nis much more united around Clinton; in 2008, some of the best fundraisers\nand strategists were looking for an alternative and found one in Obama.\n\n\n\nSecond, Sanders is a wonderful senator and a very important voice in the\nDemocratic Party, but he is not Barack Obama.\n\n\n\nPresident Obama is a once-in-a-generation political talent -- a phenomenal\nspeechmaker and "retail politician" who is quick on his feet and possesses\nthe ability to see around corners.\n\n\n\nObama also had natural inroads into two critical constituencies within the\nparty: white college educated progressives and the African-American\ncommunity, giving him broader appeal than any previous insurgent candidate.\n\n\n\nFinally, Hillary Clinton circa 2015 is not Hillary Clinton circa 2008.\n\n\n\nHer first campaign was beset by timidity, dissension and constant changes\nin strategy in reaction to the D.C conventional wisdom du jour. In Obama\nheadquarters, we would shake our heads in bemusement at some of her\ncampaign\'s decisions as we realized it was either using an outdated\nplaybook or no playbook at all.\n\nHer campaign this time has been disciplined, cohesive and bold. Sure there\nare tactical things they could have done differently, but they have a smart\nstrategy and are executing it with a precision that reminds me of our\ncampaign in 2008.\n\n\n\nOne of her biggest mistakes her 2008 campaign made was treating field\norganization as an afterthought. Our field organizers and volunteers were\nthe heart of Obama\'s 2008 campaign; they were its most valued asset, were\ngiven speaking slots at campaign rallies and developed relationships with\nthe candidate.\n\n\n\nAt her recent campaign rally in New Hampshire, one of Clinton\'s field\norganizers addressed the crowd. Reporters took mild notice, but on the\nvarious text chains, email threads and social media feeds that constitute\nthe informal Obama alumni network, this was taken as a sign that this\nHillary Campaign gets it.\n\n\n\nThere is a long road to travel before the Iowa caucuses with many potential\npitfalls and a lot of work ahead for Clinton. Sanders is running a great\nrace and the Democratic Party (and Clinton) are better for it. Clinton is\nnot inevitable, and a Sanders win is far from impossible.\n\n\n\nHowever, it\'s worth remembering with that with all of the Clinton\ncampaign\'s mistakes and Obama\'s talents and advantages in 2008, we barely\nbeat her. This time around, the environment is better and she is a better\ncandidate, running a much better campaign against a less well-known\nopponent with fewer resources and a narrower coalition.\n\n\n\nFor all the contretemps about emails, speeches and roped-off reporters,\nelections are about fundamentals and the fundamentals point to a decisive\nif hard fought victory for Clinton.\n\n\n\nA lot can change in the coming months, but at this point in the race,\neveryone should stop all the bed-wetting.\n\n\n\n*Donald Trump\'s Latino comments are just GOP orthodoxy in a cruder shell\n<http://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2015/jul/07/donald-trump-mexico-immigration-republican-politics>\n// The Guardian // Jeb Lund \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nalling Donald Trump an idiot is not one of those things you will find on a\nlist of the world\xe2\x80\x99s most arduous tasks. As my colleague Simon Maloy points out, it\xe2\x80\x99s good\nlong-term strategy. Whenever Trump fizzles out or realizes that campaigning\nis work, his voters have to go somewhere, and Ted Cruz wants them to have a\nhome. And Trump is currently polling second in Iowa and New Hampshire. Ted\nCruz\xe2\x80\x99s interest in those voters is no different than any other candidate\xe2\x80\x99s.\nBut, like Homer Simpson, he keeps accidentally saying the innocuous things\nin his head and the Republican inner monologue out loud.\n\n\n\nLook back at that list. And Marco Rubio\xe2\x80\x99s immigration\npolicy probably differs from Trump\xe2\x80\x99s only by one gaudy border fence.\n\n\n\nThe party has run so long on nativist anxiety about foreigners plundering\nlady liberty, stealing jobs and slowly strangling the republic to death\nthat the next step is just calling immigrants rapists, thieves and\nmurderers. And thanks to years of purity testing in Republican primaries,\nafter trying to ignore the issue for weeks, the remaining candidates have\nonly two options left: try to join or outflank Trump to the right or try to\nnon-ignore ignore him by writing him off as \xe2\x80\x9cinappropriate.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nThe rest of the world can just call Trump an idiot, a man with few\nambitions outside of being Trumpy, whose remaining strands of what one\nmight call policy are wisps of spun sugar extruded by hot air, reminding\neveryone of the tacky coif that sits atop his blanched Smithfield Ham of a\nface. The Republican Party can\xe2\x80\x99t even luxuriate in ad hominem. Yeah, they\ncould call him an empty suit and a bozo, but that stops working the moment\nanyone notices that he sounds like a slightly loaded version of themselves.\n\n\n\n*Why Hillary Clinton Is Revising Expectations Downward\n<https://www.commentarymagazine.com/2015/07/07/hillary-clinton-inevitable-nominee-no-more/>\n// Commentary Magazine // Noah Rothman \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m baaaack!\xe2\x80\x9d former Secretary of State Hillary Clinton announced as she\ntook the stage in Iowa at former Senator Tom Harkin\xe2\x80\x99s annual steak fry\nevent in September of last year. Presidential campaigns are replete with\nbizarre moments, but perhaps none were as curious as Clinton implicitly\ncomparing herself to the poltergeist that torments little Carol Anne in the\nclassic flick of the same name. For a campaign that is itself haunted by\nthe ghosts of failure, it would have been in the best interests of the\ninevitable Democratic nominee to make the case for candidacy beyond her own\nprohibitive stature within her Party. If that pillar were to collapse,\nClinton\xe2\x80\x99s viability as Barack Obama\xe2\x80\x99s successor would soon follow. Today,\nas the specter of a modestly competitive Democratic primary looms,\nClinton\xe2\x80\x99s campaign is at work setting back expectations for how well she\nwill perform in the early primary states and, in doing so, is chipping away\nat the central pillar holding her candidacy aloft.\n\n\n\nIn an appearance on MSNBC on Monday, Clinton campaign communications\ndirector and former White House communications official Jennifer Palmieri\nconceded that the former secretary\xe2\x80\x99s campaign had become formally \xe2\x80\x9cworried\xe2\x80\x9d\nabout the insurgent challenge to her inevitability mounted by Vermont\nSenator Bernie Sanders. \xe2\x80\x9cHe will be a serious force for the campaign, and I\ndon\xe2\x80\x99t think that will diminish,\xe2\x80\x9d Palmieri confessed.\n\n\n\nWhen the New York Times investigated the thinking inside the Clinton\ncampaign, reporters discovered that there was emerging consensus that the\ncoronation had been abruptly called off. \xe2\x80\x9cI think we underestimated that\nSanders would quickly attract so many Democrats in Iowa who weren\xe2\x80\x99t likely\nto support Hillary,\xe2\x80\x9d an unnamed advisor told the Times. Apparently, that\nfear was confirmed by other similarly well-placed sources. Ultimately, the\nTimes report suggested what former Democratic advisor Joe Trippi contended\noutright: \xe2\x80\x9cShe could lose Iowa.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nClinton\xe2\x80\x99s support has ebbed in recent weeks, particularly in Iowa among\nlikely Democratic caucus-goers. The most recent Quinnipiac survey of\nDemocrats in the Hawkeye State showed Sanders support had more than doubled\nsince May to 33 percent while Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s had ebbed some from 60 to 53\npercent. In a caucus state, in which energy and enthusiasm are the central\nelements of victory, the candidate with the most animated supporters can\nengineer an upset \xe2\x80\x93 as Clinton, who came in third in Iowa in 2008 behind\nBarack Obama and John Edwards, would attest.\n\n\n\nAnd if Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s support is ebbing, she only has herself to blame.\nClinton\xe2\x80\x99s campaign has not substantially adapted to changing political\ncircumstances in almost a year. \xe2\x80\x9c[H]er remarks were neither exceptional in\nwhat she said nor particularly passionate in how she delivered them,\xe2\x80\x9d\nWashington Post columnist Dan Balz wrote after digesting Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s steak\nfry performance. \xe2\x80\x9cThey were safe and largely predictable, a kind of\nDemocratic Message 101 heading into the most important stretch of the fall\ncampaign.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nBut the midterm campaign came and went and Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s tactics failed to\nevolve. Her campaign remains safe and predictable; she projects the air of\na candidate who is allergic to unscripted events and substantial contact\nwith unscreened voters. Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s aversion to exposing herself to press\nscrutiny neared cartoonish levels when she was photographed perambulating\ndown a New Hampshire street amid a Fourth of July parade with the media\ngaggle almost literally in tow, straining at the ropes that held them at a\nsafe distance from the lofty figure in their midst.\n\n\n\nSo why would Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s campaign want to shed her formerly cultivated air of\ninevitability? Even Trippi concedes that Clinton would merely shrug off an\nunthinkable loss in Iowa and go on to win the nomination anyway. Why would\nthe campaign that has spent so much energy and capital to stave off a\nreprise of what she described in her memoirs as an \xe2\x80\x9cexcruciating\xe2\x80\x9d defeat in\nthe Hawkeye State embrace the prospect that history might repeat itself?\nPerhaps because Sanders is the best challenger that Clinton could have\nhoped for.\n\n\n\nA fringe politician with a small but fanatical following who once held\nradical and deeply impolitic social views poses about as much challenge to\nClinton as former Texas Rep. Ron Paul posed to Mitt Romney. Clinton is in\nno danger of losing her party\xe2\x80\x99s nomination to Sanders in the same way she\nwould, say, Massachusetts Sen. Elizabeth Warren. But if Clinton appears\nsoft in a primary and, ultimately, beatable in a general, those beads of\nsweat dotting the brows of Democratic Party elders will soon grow into a\ncascading torrent. Draft efforts that failed to draw Warren, or any other\ncredible Democrat, into the race will be resurrected. Democratic careerists\nwho dared not challenge their party\xe2\x80\x99s anointed heir will think twice about\nwhether they made the right move, and a late entry into the race might\nspark a stampede among skittish and unenthusiastic grassroots Clinton\nsupporters. It is in Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s interests to cast Sanders as the best that\nthe anti-Clinton elements in her party can do.\n\n\n\nIs Hillary Clinton truly vulnerable in Iowa? Perhaps. A narrow loss is easy\nto envision. Might Sanders rob her of her party\xe2\x80\x99s nomination? That\xe2\x80\x99s far\nharder to imagine; at least, harder than it would be to see another\ncredible Democrat with broader appeal and proper left-wing bona fides\npulling off a successful coup. That\xe2\x80\x99s probably the true nightmare scenario\nthat Clinton hopes to stave off by feigning injury.\n\n\n\n*TOP NEWS*\n\n\n\n\n*DOMESTIC*\n\n\n\n*\xe2\x80\x98Complicated\xe2\x80\x99 Support for Confederate Flag in White South\n<http://www.nytimes.com/2015/07/08/us/a-georgia-county-where-the-rebel-flag-is-still-revered.html?ref=us&_r=0>\n// NYT // Richard Fausset \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nBrandon Heath, Haralson County\xe2\x80\x99s chief magistrate judge, flies the\nConfederate battle flag on his property. A version of it adorns the front\nbumper of his cherry-red Chevrolet pickup. It is painted on the wall of the\ngymnasium of his alma mater, Haralson County High School, where the sports\nteams are called the Rebels and Rebelettes.\n\n\n\nLike a number of people in this rural, working-class county \xe2\x80\x94 which is 92\npercent white and just beyond the creep of Atlanta\xe2\x80\x99s western suburbs \xe2\x80\x94 Mr.\nHeath believes that efforts to remove the flag from public spaces across\nthe South are \xe2\x80\x9cplumb ridiculous.\xe2\x80\x9d And he insists that his reverence for the\nbanner has nothing to do with race.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s just about where we come from, and locally here, we\xe2\x80\x99re just real\nproud of that,\xe2\x80\x9d said Mr. Heath, 35, an auctioneer who, when not in court,\nfavors camouflage ball caps and speaks with an unhurried country twang.\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s all about your school, and your upraising, and who you are.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nSupport for the Confederate flag may be waning among Southern lawmakers in\nthe aftermath of the church shootings in Charleston, S.C. But here in this\ncounty of 29,000 people, as in many other stretches of the white,\nworking-class South, the flag remains a revered symbol, not only of the\nConfederate dead, but of a unique regional identity.\n\n\n\nAt the Georgia Peach Oyster Bar, President Obama\xe2\x80\x99s campaign poster, altered\nto say \xe2\x80\x9cNope,\xe2\x80\x9d combined with a Confederate flag. Credit Kevin Liles for The\nNew York Times\n\nIn Haralson County, a ragged patch of low hills and homesteads at the\nsouthern tip of Appalachia, it can seem like the battle flag is baked into\nthe culture. One finds it displayed on the welcome sign in Buchanan, the\ncounty seat, as part of the seal of the Sons of Confederate Veterans,\nalongside that of the Lions Club.\n\n\n\nAnd while support for the flag is widespread here, its supporters, and\ntheir justifications, vary drastically: There are overt racists and avowed\nantiracists; students of history and those who seem oblivious to it; ardent\ndefenders of the Lost Cause and others who do not understand why the\nblue-spangled X on a red field \xe2\x80\x94 as ubiquitous here as deer stands, church\nsteeples and biscuits with gravy \xe2\x80\x94 can be so controversial.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI just don\xe2\x80\x99t get why people are getting all mad about it,\xe2\x80\x9d said Corey\nDoyle, 19.\n\n\n\nMr. Doyle, who was recently hired as a car salesman, was standing the other\nday with five other white protesters on a grassy berm outside the local\nWalmart, whose corporate office decided to pull Confederate merchandise\nfrom its shelves after the Charleston massacre.\n\n\n\nThe protesters waved the battle flag and an old version of the Georgia\nstate flag. That state flag, which prominently incorporated the battle\nflag\xe2\x80\x99s design, was introduced in 1956 by an arch-segregationist state\nLegislature as courts were ordering the South to integrate. It was replaced\nin 2001 by lawmakers more sensitive to Georgia\xe2\x80\x99s image to outsiders.\n\n\n\nPassing cars and trucks honked in solidarity as they turned into the\nparking lot.\n\n\n\nEarnest Fryer, 28, an ice cream truck driver, was waving the old state\nflag. Asked about its segregationist origins, he drew a blank. To him, it\nwas the flag that his father had given him, and one that had long adorned\nthe wall of his room, he said. Like Mr. Heath and Mr. Doyle, Mr. Fryer\ninsisted that his stand on the flag had nothing to do with matters of race.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe don\xe2\x80\x99t want to offend nobody,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Fryer said, noting that he was part\nCherokee. Later, he said slavery was the \xe2\x80\x9cone thing that makes all the rest\nof my heritage look bad.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut there\xe2\x80\x99s a lot more about us than that one thing,\xe2\x80\x9d he added.\n\n\n\nAnd yet that one thing still looms disturbingly large.\n\n\n\nAt Kimball\xe2\x80\x99s General Store, a popular meeting place here, a man who\ndeclined to give his name blamed blacks for the new assault on the flag,\nand muttered a racial slur. Near Mr. Heath\xe2\x80\x99s office at the county\ncourthouse, a pickup parked beside a weatherworn house sported a pair of\nConfederate flags, and a window sticker that read \xe2\x80\x9cAmerican Nazi Party.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nJust across the county line, the Georgia Peach Oyster Bar has operated as a\nscandalous open secret. Its website features two Confederate battle flags,\nthe description, \xe2\x80\x9cThe Original Klan, Klam & Oyster Bar,\xe2\x80\x9d and a stunningly\nvirulent collection of racist signs. Patrons are confronted with a\nselection of crude cartoons and graffiti, and a menu that declares, on the\nappetizer page, \xe2\x80\x9cWe cater to hangins\xe2\x80\x99.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nMr. Heath acknowledged the existence of such sentiments here. But he also\nnoted that this overwhelmingly white place, so committed to the flag, also\nelected a black man, H. Allen Poole, as the chairman of its Board of\nCommissioners in 2004, and has re-elected him twice. Last year, voters\nelected the state\xe2\x80\x99s first Asian-American Superior Court judge, Meng Lim, a\nCambodian refugee who grew up in the Haralson County city of Bremen.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s complicated,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Heath said.\n\n\n\nAt Haralson County High School, where the sports teams are called the\nRebels and Rebelettes, students once voted by a wide margin to repaint the\nbattle flag at the gym when it was defaced. Credit Kevin Liles for The New\nYork Times\n\nFor Mr. Heath, the flag helped get him elected in 2008, when he bounced\naround the county\xe2\x80\x99s rural back roads in his pickup, hunting for votes. The\nbattle flag was affixed to the front bumper. A 12-gauge shotgun was in the\ngun rack, and an old bloodhound was in the back.\n\n\n\nIt was all part of a package that validated Mr. Heath\xe2\x80\x99s regular-guy\ncredentials and bolstered his argument that the magistrate court would be\nbetter run by a self-proclaimed good old boy with a high school diploma\nthan by the lawyer who was the incumbent at the time.\n\n\n\nMr. Heath saw it as an appeal to a common culture, not a racial gesture, a\nway to show voters that he was one of them: conservative, Republican (the\ncounty went 81 percent for Mitt Romney in the 2012 presidential election)\nand, as he said, \xe2\x80\x9csalt of the earth.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nOn a recent weekday morning, Mr. Heath gave a brief tour of Haralson\nCounty, starting with Hutcheson\xe2\x80\x99s Memorial Chapel and Crematory, where he\nintroduced the owner, Danny Hutcheson, the county coroner.\n\n\n\nMr. Hutcheson sat in a back room that was decorated with political and\nhistorical memorabilia, including a picture of an ancestor who, according\nto family legend, was robbed of his cattle by Yankee soldiers during the\nCivil War.\n\n\n\nHe says he does not display the flag for fear of upsetting his black\nfriends and clients. But he defends those who do.\n\n\n\nA reproduction of the old Georgia flag, which incorporates the Confederate\nbattle flag, on Mr. Heath\'s truck. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s just about where we come from, and\nlocally here, we\xe2\x80\x99re just real proud of that,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. Credit Kevin Liles\nfor The New York Times\n\n\n\nMr. Heath drove on to the high school where the trophy room of the gym\nfeatures the battle flag painted on the wall.\n\n\n\nSuch displays have caused trouble here in the past. In September 2000,\nsomeone painted over a flag at the gym, and students were allowed to vote\non whether to repaint it. Repainting won by a vote to 861 to 150, according\nto news reports at the time. A group of black football players threatened\nto boycott a game, but that never materialized. It all seemed perplexing to\nCain Jackson, a 22-year-old graduate, who is white.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t see how it\xe2\x80\x99s racist to anybody,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.\n\n\n\nLater, Mr. Heath paid a visit to Mr. Poole, the chairman of the county\ncommission.\n\n\n\nMr. Poole, a Republican, said Southern governors were wrong to take the\nbattle flag down. He noted that he, too, had graduated from Haralson County\nHigh School in 1974, and had played safety and outside linebacker on the\nfootball team.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI was a Rebel,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, \xe2\x80\x9cfor four years.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nBut not everyone is so comfortable. Angelica Griffin is also an\nAfrican-American, and also played sports at the high school. She said she\nwas \xe2\x80\x9cterrified\xe2\x80\x9d to criticize the flag while she was there.\n\n\n\nMs. Griffin, 28, recently completed law school at DePaul University in\nChicago and is studying for the bar exam. After the Charleston shootings,\nshe said, she posted her displeasure with the flag on social media,\nsparking debate and pushback from white friends back home.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cPeople were so apt to defend it, without even thinking about other people\nand how that flag makes them feel,\xe2\x80\x9d she said.\n\n\n\nBut Ms. Griffin also spoke about the time, in 2008, when her mother lost\nher job. White Haralson County neighbors showered her mother with money and\ngift cards so she could afford to drop her off at college.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou know what? It doesn\xe2\x80\x99t make sense,\xe2\x80\x9d Ms. Griffin said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s the great\nconundrum of the South.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n*Air Force jet collides with Cessna over South Carolina, killing two people\n<http://www.washingtonpost.com/news/post-nation/wp/2015/07/07/military-jet-collides-with-cessna-over-south-carolina/?hpid=z4>\n// WaPo // Mark Berman \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015*\n\n\n\nTwo people were killed Tuesday morning when an Air Force fighter jet and a\nsmall civilian plane collided in the air over South Carolina, according to\nfederal authorities.\n\n\n\nEmergency responders rushed to a region north of Charleston, S.C., shortly\nafter 11 a.m., as word emerged of the rare midair collision that sent\ndebris raining down on the area below.\n\n\n\nThere were two people killed aboard the small plane, a Cessna 150,\naccording to the National Transportation Safety Board.\n\n\n\nThe pilot of the F-16 Fighting Falcon ejected safely, according to a\nstatement from Shaw Air Force Base in Sumter, S.C., where the aircraft\noriginated.\n\n\n\nAir Force officials later identified the pilot as Maj. Aaron Johnson of the\n55th Fighter Squadron at Shaw. After the crash, Johnson was taken to a\nclinic at Joint Base Charleston to be examined.\n\n\n\nJohnson was conducting a routine instrument training mission when the crash\noccurred, Col. Stephen F. Jost, commander of the 20th Fighter Wing at Shaw,\nsaid at a news conference on Tuesday afternoon.\n\n\n\nIt did not appear that Johnson had any injuries, Jost said, and the pilot\nwas expected to return to Shaw on Tuesday evening.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI can tell you in my experience, I haven\xe2\x80\x99t had any close calls because the\nAir Force is very disciplined about how it operates its aircraft,\xe2\x80\x9d Jost\nsaid.\n\n\n\nWhile Jost said that he knows about military planes colliding, he has never\nseen a military plane crash into a civilian one.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s very rare, because of the procedures and the equipment we have in\nplace,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s unfortunate.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nA spokesman for Berkeley County said the two planes collided over\nLewisfield Plantation in Moncks Corner, a town about 45 minutes north of\nCharleston. The county government said it was setting up a command center\nin that town, which is near Lake Moultrie.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cFrom what I understand from a witness, the military plane struck the\nother, small aircraft broadside,\xe2\x80\x9d Bill Salisbury, the Berkeley County\ncoroner and chief of the county\xe2\x80\x99s rescue squad, said at an earlier news\nconference on Tuesday afternoon.\n\n\n\nDebris was seen on land as well as in the water, officials said Tuesday. In\nthe hours after the crash, authorities found the F-16\xe2\x80\x99s wreckage and some\nparts of the Cessna on the ground and the water, but they were still\nlooking for other parts of the Cessna.\n\n\n\nThe Cessna left the Berkeley County airport in Moncks Corner just before 11\na.m. and were likely heading for Myrtle Beach, Salisbury said. He said that\na wallet was found after the collision.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe have no reason to believe that anyone survived the crash,\xe2\x80\x9d Salisbury\nsaid.\n\n\n\nHe declined to identify the people who were on the Cessna, saying only that\nthey were believed to be from the area. Salisbury said that officials were\nstill working to find the two people.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cOur thoughts are with the friends and family of anyone aboard the civilian\naircraft,\xe2\x80\x9d Shaw Air Force Base officials said in the statement.\n\n\n\nThere were no reports of any injuries on the ground or any damage on the\nground, a spokesman for Berkeley County said on Tuesday afternoon, about\nsix hours after the crash.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cI turned around, and I saw the jet,\xe2\x80\x9d Wayne Ware, who lives in the area,\ntold the Post and Courier. \xe2\x80\x9cPieces started falling out of the sky. His\nengine is lying right there at the campground.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\n*INTERNATIONAL*\n\n\n\n*Afghans and Taliban end peace talks with plans to meet again\n<https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/asia_pacific/afghans-and-taliban-representatives-meet-in-pakistani-capital/2015/07/07/398462c8-24b1-11e5-b621-b55e495e9b78_story.html>\n// WaPo // Sudarsan Raghavan & Tim Craig \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015*\n\n\n\nPakistan\xe2\x80\x99s Foreign Ministry said Wednesday that peace talks between\nrepresentatives of the Taliban and an Afghan government delegation had\nconcluded but would restart after the Islamic holy month of Ramadan ends in\ntwo weeks.\n\n\n\nThe talks were held Tuesday night in Murree, a mountain resort 90 minutes\nnorth of Islamabad, Pakistan\xe2\x80\x99s capital.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe participants exchanged views and ways and means to bring peace and\nreconciliation in Afghanistan,\xe2\x80\x9d the Pakistani statement said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt was\nagreed that for lasting peace in the region, each side would approach the\nprocess in sincerity and with full commitment.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nThe two sides met Tuesday in what Afghan officials hoped would be a step\ntoward negotiating a peace deal with the insurgent group and ending the\ncountry\xe2\x80\x99s protracted war, Afghan and Pakistani officials said.\n\n\n\nThe gathering near Islamabad, under discussion for several weeks, was not\nthe first time the two sides have met to discuss a cease-fire. Meetings\nbetween Taliban representatives and Afghan officials have taken place in\nrecent months in Qatar, China and Norway.\n\n\n\nAt least one dead in Taliban attack on Afghan intelligence agency(0:48)\n\nThe Taliban on Twitter claimed responsibility Tuesday for two attacks that\nrocked the Afghan capital that same day. (Reuters)\n\nBut this meeting carried more significance because of Pakistan\xe2\x80\x99s\nlong-standing ties to the Taliban, as well as Afghan President Ashraf\nGhani\xe2\x80\x99s efforts to persuade Pakistan to play a significant role in bringing\nthe Taliban to the negotiating table. It was the first time such a\nsenior-level Afghan delegation has met face-to-face with Taliban\nrepresentatives.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe have always had a pretty clear view of what Pakistan can and cannot do\nin terms of delivering the Afghan Taliban to the negotiating table,\xe2\x80\x9d a U.S.\nofficial, who spoke on the condition of anonymity to freely discuss the\npeace efforts, said in a recent interview. \xe2\x80\x9cBut we see, at this point, a\nsustained effort by the Pakistanis to support President Ghani\xe2\x80\x99s effort.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nOn Tuesday, Ghani\xe2\x80\x99s office announced through its official Twitter account\nthat \xe2\x80\x9ca delegation from the High Peace Council of Afghanistan has traveled\nto Pakistan for negotiations with the Taliban.\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n\n\nThe council is a body that includes former Taliban members. It was created\nin 2010 by then-President Hamid Karzai to negotiate with elements of the\nTaliban. The delegation also includes Afghanistan\xe2\x80\x99s deputy foreign\nminister, Hekmat Karzai, a cousin of the former president.\n\n\n\nAccording to Pakistani officials, the Taliban sent four delegates\nrepresenting \xe2\x80\x9call top Taliban leaders.\xe2\x80\x9d A second U.S. official said the\nUnited States also sent representatives to the talks after being invited by\nthe Afghan and Pakistani governments.\n\n\n\nThe meeting between the two sides took place after the end of the daily\nRamadan fast, according to Pakistani officials. The talks continued past\nmidnight.\n\n\n\nIt remains to be seen whether the talks will have any impact on the\nconflict, now nearing the 14-year mark. Even as meetings have taken place\nin various countries, the Taliban has mounted fierce offensives across\nAfghanistan and dispatched suicide bombers to attack government officials\nand symbols of official power in Kabul and elsewhere.\n\n\n\nThe second U.S. official, who spoke on the condition of anonymity to\ndiscuss sensitive negotiations, said the fact that legitimate\nrepresentatives of the Taliban and the Afghan government were meeting was\nsignificant.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat means something. . . . But how you get to a process where you start\ntalking about substantive issues is a difficult question,\xe2\x80\x9d the official\nsaid.\n\n\n\nSome analysts have suggested that the Taliban\xe2\x80\x99s offensives are an attempt\nto strengthen its bargaining position ahead of potential peace\nnegotiations. There is also growing concern in the Taliban about the\nemergence of the Islamic State, which has been wooing Taliban factions to\ndefect and align with its cause. In Nangahar province, the Taliban is\nengaging in skirmishes with defectors operating under the Islamic State\nbrand who have managed to seize control of several areas of the province.\nThe specter of more fighters joining the Islamic State could prompt the\nTaliban\xe2\x80\x99s leadership to agree to a political settlement with the\ngovernment, some analysts say.\n\n\n\nBut there is also the question of which Taliban the Afghan government is\nnegotiating with. The insurgency is far less cohesive today than it was in\n1996, when it quickly seized power across Afghanistan. With its supreme\nleader, Mohammad Omar, not seen in years, many factions have become more\nindependent from the Taliban\xe2\x80\x99s core leadership. It remains unclear whether\nmany Taliban commanders would even accept a peace agreement \xe2\x80\x94 or would\ninstead continue fighting or would join the Islamic State.\n\n\n\nPakistan is viewed by some as a questionable intermediary. Many Afghans,\nincluding powerful political and military figures, remain suspicious of\nIslamabad and its motives. The Pakistani military and intelligence services\nhave long been viewed in both Afghanistan and Pakistan as the godfathers of\nthe Taliban, nurturing it as a proxy and providing haven to its leadership.\n\n\n\nPakistani officials on Tuesday said they are honest brokers.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cPakistan, as a friend of Afghanistan, is trying to facilitate\nresult-oriented talks between the Afghan government and the Taliban,\xe2\x80\x9d said\na Pakistani security official who spoke on the condition of anonymity under\ngovernment rules.\n\n\n\nIn a meeting Tuesday with local reporters and political analysts, Ghani\nsaid the meeting in Islamabad would focus on \xe2\x80\x9cconfidence-building and\npreparing key points in the peace talks agenda,\xe2\x80\x9d and would set the stage\nfor future discussions, according to a statement from his office.\n\n\n\nGhani said that peace talks would be led by the Afghans, suggesting that\nthe Pakistanis would play a less visible role, and that the government was\nspeaking with the insurgents from a position of strength, the statement\nsaid. He also said that women will continue to be part of the peace\ndelegations.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cOur goal is reducing the violence level in the initial phase and then end\nit finally,\xe2\x80\x9d Ghani said, according to the statement.\n\n\n\n*Eurozone Sets Sunday Deadline for Greece Financing Deal\n<http://www.wsj.com/articles/solution-to-greek-crisis-wont-come-overnight-juncker-warns-1436255691>\n// WSJ // Gabriele Steinhauser And Matthew Dalton \xe2\x80\x93 July 7, 2015 *\n\n\n\nEurozone leaders set Greece a Sunday deadline to come up with new and\neven-tougher economic measures if the country wants to avoid defaulting on\nthe European Central Bank and crashing out of the currency union.\n\n\n\nAs a sweetener for such a deal, leaders raised the possibility of some\nshort-term financing to help Athens make a July 20 payment and\xe2\x80\x94most\nimportant for Greek Prime Minister Alexis Tsipras\xe2\x80\x94action down the road to\nrelieve Greece\xe2\x80\x99s crushing debt burden.\n\n\n\nObstacles to an agreement that keeps Greece in the eurozone remain high,\nhowever. Most notably, the policy overhauls and budget cuts demanded go\nbeyond those that were resoundingly rejected by Greek voters in a\nreferendum last weekend.\n\n\n\nGerman Chancellor Angela Merkel said after Tuesday\xe2\x80\x99s emergency summit of\neurozone leaders that it is up to Greece to act. \xe2\x80\x9cOf course, at the very\nend, one will have to discuss how debt sustainability can be recreated but\nnot by saying first \xe2\x80\x98How do we close the gap?\xe2\x80\x99 but \xe2\x80\x9cWhat can Greece do?\xe2\x80\x99 \xe2\x80\x9d\nshe said.\n\n\n\nShe added that Mario Draghi, the ECB president, made clear to leaders at\nthe summit that Sunday would be \xe2\x80\x9cthe right moment to take decisions\xe2\x80\x9d for\nGreece to avoid a meltdown of its banking system.\n\n\n\nMr. Tsipras said that the negotiation process would be fast. \xe2\x80\x9cI believe\nthere will be a solution by the end of the week at the latest,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.\n\n\n\nLeaders said that the broad outlines of such an agreement needed to be\nnailed down at a new summit on Sunday of the leaders from the entire\nEuropean Union, including nine countries that aren\xe2\x80\x99t in the eurozone.\n\n\n\nWithout some new cash in the coming weeks, Greece won\xe2\x80\x99t be able to make the\n\xe2\x82\xac3.5 billion ($3.8 billion) bond payment to the ECB, leading to the\ncountry\xe2\x80\x99s second default in less than a month.\n\n\n\nSuch a nonpayment could push the ECB to cut emergency lending to Greek\nbanks\xe2\x80\x94a move that would send the country\xe2\x80\x99s financial system into meltdown\nand force the government to print its own money to recapitalize them.\n\n\n\nGreek banks have been shut for more than a week, after the ECB put a limit\non the emergency loans they had been drawing to buffer growing deposit\noutflows. Cash withdrawals from ATMs have been limited to \xe2\x82\xac60 a day and\ndepositors are unable to transfer money abroad.\n\n\n\nSome short-term funding and the prospect of a longer-term bailout deal from\nthe rest of the eurozone could allow Greece\xe2\x80\x94and the ECB\xe2\x80\x94to let banks reopen\nand normal economic activity in the country to resume.\n\n\n\nGetting there, however, would require a formidable turnaround by Mr.\nTsipras and his government.\n\n\n\nIn addition to the pension cuts and tax increases, rejected in the\nreferendum, a new rescue package to keep the government afloat for two to\nthree years would require overhaul measures that had dropped out of\nnegotiations in recent months.\n\n\n\nThese, Ms. Merkel said, include changes to labor laws to make it easier to\nfire workers, changes to product markets and the privatization of state\nassets.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThis isn\xe2\x80\x99t about a program from today, or from yesterday or from 10 days\nago, for a program until November\xe2\x80\xa6this program is, according to the\nnow-withdrawn Greek request, meant to be two years long, so it is a\nmultiyear program,\xe2\x80\x9d Ms. Merkel said.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat such a multiyear program has to entail more commitments is in itself\nclear,\xe2\x80\x9d she added.\n\n\n\nOnly once that is clear, leaders would look at ways to make Greece\xe2\x80\x99s debt\nsustainable again, Ms. Merkel said, adding that any debt relief wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t\ninclude cuts to the nominal value of rescue loans.\n\n\n\nBut talks on details of a final plan could drag on for weeks.\n\n\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe short-term deal is only possible in a longer-term deal,\xe2\x80\x9d French\nPresident Fran\xc3\xa7ois Hollande said at his postsummit news
